1 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fishbein v. Kozlowski


(SC 15996)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


252 Conn. 38; 743 A.2d 1110; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 440


September 21, 1999, Argued  
December 22, 1999, Officially Released *


* December 22, 1999, the date that this opinion was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the defendant's suspension of the plaintiff's license to operate a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont and Daly, Js., with Lavery, J., dissenting, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court. * .



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed judgment of Appellate Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain affirming the trial court's judgment that dismissed plaintiff's appeal of suspension of operator's license by the Commission of Motor Vehicles, based on trial court's holding that police had legally stopped plaintiff's vehicle.


OVERVIEW: While police were conducting surveillance of suspected drug house, plaintiff drove up and stopped in front of house. Car's passenger went to door of house and returned to car. Before car was in motion, police pulled cruiser next to car and turned on cruiser's overhead lights. Plaintiff failed field sobriety tests and was arrested for driving while intoxicated. At police station, plaintiff took two breath tests, which indicated that plaintiff's blood alcohol exceeded limit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a. Connecticut Commissioner of Motor Vehicles (Commissioner) issued notice of suspension of plaintiff's driver's license and informed him of right to hearing. At requested hearing, Commissioner determined four elements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(f) were met. On appeal, plaintiff argued that probable cause to arrest element implicitly incorporated requirement of lawful stop. The court disagreed and concluded that license suspension hearing was properly limited to four enumerated issues contained in statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment, concluding that the lack of reasonable and articulable suspicion to justify an initial investigatory stop was not a basis to overturn Commissioner of Motor Vehicles' decision, if Commissioner found that, subsequent to the stop, police had probable cause to arrest plaintiff for driving while intoxicated.

 

2 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Griffin


(SC 15495)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 671; 741 A.2d 913; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 422


February 18, 1999, Argued  
December 21, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Griffin v. Warden, York Corr. Inst., 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 492 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and with the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion in limine to restrict the scope of voir dire questioning regarding the death penalty; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found the existence of both aggravating and mitigating factors, and the court rendered judgment of conviction in accordance with the verdict and imposed a term of life imprisonment without the possibility of release on the capital felony count only, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction of two counts of murder and one count of a capital felony from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of murder and one count of a capital felony. Claiming that a death qualified jury denied her an impartial jury for the trial's guilt phase, defendant filed a motion in limine to restrict death penalty issues from the voir dire's scope. After the denial of the motion, defendant was convicted on all counts. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and held that the federal constitution not only permitted questioning of venirepersons regarding attitudes on the death penalty prior to the guilt phase of the trial, it also provided defendant a constitutional right to ask such questions. Further, it rejected the proposition that use of the jury death qualification process at a trial's guilt phase deprived defendant of an impartial jury. The court determined that the results were the same under Connecticut's constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed because defendant's claim that she was denied an impartial jury due to the trial court's requiring death-qualified jurors for the trial's guilt phase failed. A death qualified jury must be empanelled for both stages of a capital case.

 

3 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ross


(SC 16124), (SC 16135)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 579; 742 A.2d 312; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 409


October 14, 1999, Argued  
December 14, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 28, 1999.
Appeal after remand at, Judgment entered by State v. Ross, 269 Conn. 213, 849 A.2d 648, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 214 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations, in three cases, charging the defendant with eight counts of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the cases were consolidated and where the court, Hendel, J., granted, in part, the defendant's motion to dismiss and dismissed two of the four counts of capital felony in the second case; thereafter, the cases were transferred to the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of capital felony in each case; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and the court, Ford, J., rendered judgment of guilty in each case in accordance with the verdicts and imposed the death penalty on each of the six counts, from which the defendant filed three separate appeals to this court, which affirmed the judgments of the trial court with respect to the finding of guilt but reversed the judgments with respect to the imposition of the death penalty and remanded the cases to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing; on remand to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, the court,  [***2] Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion to bar further prosecution and his motion for a new trial, and granted the defendant's motion in limine to require the state to abide by the rules of evidence generally applicable to criminal trials when rebutting mitigating factors in the defendant's sentencing hearing, and the defendant appealed and the state, on the granting of certification pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a, filed an expedited appeal to this court, which, sua sponte, consolidated the appeals.
State v. Ross, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1999 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 26, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from Superior Court, New London (Connecticut), defendant appealed denial of his motion for a new trial, and plaintiff State appealed the grant of defendant's motion in limine requiring the plaintiff to abide by the rules of evidence when rebutting mitigating factors in the defendant's sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of a capital felony, was granted a new penalty phase hearing. At that hearing, defendant's motion in limine to restrict the plaintiff State to the normal rules of evidence with respect to evidence used to rebut mitigation was granted, and his renewed motion to compel the State to disclose exculpatory information in its possession was denied. Both defendant and the plaintiff appealed. The court held that the plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a did not require the plaintiff to shoulder a higher evidentiary standard to rebut the existence of a mitigating factor than the defendant had to in order to carry his burden of proof. Additionally, the trial court's finding that the exculpatory information, notes made by the defendant's psychiatric expert regarding admissions by the plaintiff's psychiatric expert, had already been disclosed to the defendant was not clearly erroneous, and, further, that the information itself was not material in the Brady context. Even if the information had not been disclosed to the defendant, it was not material within the meaning of Brady because it was available to the defendant through independent sources.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part and case remanded with direction to deny defendant's motion in limine. Rules of evidence were not applicable in plaintiff State's efforts to rebut mitigation; withheld exculpatory evidence was not material.

 

4 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Atc P'Ship v. Town of Windham


(SC 16173)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 597; 741 A.2d 305; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 410


November 2, 1999, Argued  
December 14, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 28, 1999. Certiorari Denied June 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3821.
Writ of certiorari denied ATC Pshp. v. Town of Windham, 530 U.S. 1214, 147 L. Ed. 2d 249, 120 S. Ct. 2217, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3821 (2000)
Related proceeding at Atc Pshp. v. Town of Windham, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2618 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 29, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Action pursuant to, inter alia, 42 U.S.C. § 1983, to recover damages for the alleged violation of the plaintiff's right to substantive due process under the fourteenth amendment to the federal constitution as a result of the condemnation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, where the court, Beach, J., granted the defendants' motions to strike the third amended revised complaint; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Town of Windham v. ATC Pshp., 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1423 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 7, 1997)
ATC Pshp. v. Town of Windham, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 7 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 4, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven at Meriden (Connecticut) striking its third amended complaint and granting judgment in favor of defendants in an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state constitutional principles involving condemnation of plaintiff's real property under eminent domain.


OVERVIEW: Defendant municipality condemned plaintiff's property for the purpose of ongoing economic redevelopment. Prior to the condemnation, plaintiff and defendant negotiated unsuccessfully for the sale of the property, resulting in defendant issuing an ultimatum to either take its price or proceed to condemnation. Defendant also allegedly levied an improper alias tax warrant on the property and ordered the local police department to prevent plaintiff from gaining access to its property. Plaintiff sued under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging defendant violated its rights under substantive due process. The court affirmed the lower court's striking of plaintiff's complaint because defendant's actions did not rise to the level of egregiousness warranting substantive due process analysis. There were also specific constitutional provisions to protect plaintiff's property rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV, V. The state constitutional claims failed largely because the rights allegedly interfered with were economic in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment because defendant municipality's attempts to coerce property sale at low price by threatening condemnation proceeding and using police to prevent plaintiff's access to property did not rise to level of egregiousness sufficient for substantive due process analysis of civil rights action.

6 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cobb


(SC 14384)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 285; 743 A.2d 1; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 407


February 19, 1999, Argued  
December 7, 1999, Officially Released


NOTICE:

[EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 2 OF 5. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Cobb v. Connecticut, 531 U.S. 841, 121 S. Ct. 106, 148 L. Ed. 2d 64, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5401 (2000)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Claims of Racial Disparity v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, two counts of the crime of capital felony, and one count each of the crimes of robbery in the third degree, sexual assault in the first degree and murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to a three judge court, Kulawiz, Barnett and Langenbach, Js.; judgment of guilty; thereafter, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the court found the existence of aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and imposed the death penalty on the capital felony counts and a term of imprisonment on the robbery count, and the defendant appealed.
State v. Cobb, 234 Conn. 735, 663 A.2d 948, 1995 Conn. LEXIS 308 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which, following trial to a three judge panel, convicted him of capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(5), (7), and imposed two sentences of death under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a (Rev. to 1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for capital felony in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(5), (7), and the imposition of two sentences of death following trial to a three judge panel. Defendant's convictions arose from an incident in which he deflated a woman's tires, offered assistance ,and forced her to drive to a secluded area. He then sexually assaulted her, threw her off a dam onto concrete, and forced her into water until she died of asphyxiation. The court held that evidence found in the course of searches of defendant's car and house were properly admitted. Defendant voluntarily waived his right to a jury trial. It was not error to find aggravating factors and no mitigating factors, and the death sentences were supported by evidence. The death penalty statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a (Rev. to 1989), complied with due process requirements. The penalty was not excessive under proportionality review.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed on the grounds that evidence gathered during searches of defendant's car and house were properly admitted, defendant's waiver of a jury trial was voluntary, aggravating factors supported the imposition of the death penalty, the death penalty statute complied with federal constitutional requirements, and the sentence was not disproportionate.

10 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coleman


(SC 15947)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 249; 741 A.2d 1; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 403


March 23, 1999, Argued  
November 30, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 3, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2495.
Writ of certiorari denied Coleman v. Connecticut, 529 U.S. 1061, 146 L. Ed. 2d 473, 120 S. Ct. 1570, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2495 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Coleman v. Comm'r of Corr., 2005 Conn. LEXIS 259 (Conn., July 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, sexual assault in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree and robbery in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Spear and Freedman, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which reversed the Appellate Court's judgment and remanded the case to that court for consideration of the defendant's remaining claims raised on appeal; on remand, the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Spear and Freedman, Js., reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction of burglary in the second degree only and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment of not guilty on that count only, and the [***2] defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Coleman, 48 Conn. App. 260, 709 A.2d 590, 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 132 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction of burglary in the second degree only and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment of not guilty on that count only.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, sexual assault in the first degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment only as to the conviction of burglary in the second degree, and affirmed the judgment in all other respects. On appeal, the issues where whether the defendant's challenge to the trial court's instructions that "the law is made to protect society and innocent persons, and not to protect guilty ones" was worthy of review and whether the instructions violated the defendant's federal or state constitutional rights to have the jury adequately instructed regarding the presumption of innocence and the concept of reasonable doubt. The court determined that it had previously considered and rejected claims essentially identical to defendant's claims and affirmed the judgment without discussion.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the court had previously considered and rejected claims essentially identical to defendant's claims.

 

11 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watson


(SC 15924)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 220; 740 A.2d 832; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 405


March 23, 1999, Argued  
November 30, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J., on the robbery charges; verdict of guilty; thereafter, in a trial to the court, the defendant was found to be a persistent dangerous felony offender and the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdicts, from which the defendant appealed; the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Spear and Daly, Js., affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, on two certified issues, from Connecticut Appellate Court decision affirming defendant's first-degree robbery convictions and an enhanced sentence imposed after trial court determined that defendant was a persistent dangerous felony offender.


OVERVIEW: In two certified issues, defendant convicted of first-degree robbery and given enhanced sentence as persistent dangerous felony offender challenged jury instruction and state's cross-examination of defendant's alibi witness. Trial court did not err in instructing jury that principles of reasonable doubt and presumption of innocence were designed to protect the innocent and not the guilty. When viewed in their entirety, instructions adequately apprised jury that defendant was entitled to presumption of innocence unless and until state proved defendant guilty beyond reasonable doubt; there was no reasonable possibility of juror confusion. Trial court did not err in permitting state to cross-examine defendant's alibi witness regarding witness's failure to tell authorities about alibi where defendant failed to properly alert court that witness had previously spoken to defense counsel about alibi. Under circumstances, witness's testimony did not so taint trial as to cast doubt upon its fundamental fairness. Appellate court judgment affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellate court judgment affirmed. Jury instructions adequately apprised jury that defendant was entitled to presumption of innocence, and alibi witness's cross-examination testimony regarding witness's failure to tell authorities about alibi did not so taint trial as to cast doubt upon its fundamental fairness.

 

12 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Anson


(SC 16047)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 202; 740 A.2d 804; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 390; 163 L.R.R.M. 2020


April 28, 1999, Argued  
November 16, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from, inter alia, awarding any contracts in connection with a certain construction project at one of the state universities, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Langenbach, J., granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by Fusco Corporation; thereafter, the court granted the motions to dismiss filed by the defendant and the intervening defendant and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed; subsequently, the appeal was transferred to this court, which granted the plaintiffs' motion for an expedited appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), granting defendants' motions to dismiss plaintiffs' action to enjoin defendant commissioner of public works from awarding any contracts in connection with a construction project at a state university.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, subcontractors and a trade association of builders, sued the defendant commissioner of public works and the intervening defendant contractor to enjoin the awarding of contracts in connection with a construction project at a state university. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the plaintiffs lacked standing to raise their challenges to the validity of the project labor agreement. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' claims for lack of standing. The court found plaintiff subcontractors had no standing to pursue the challenge to general bid specifications because, in their own capacity, they could not bid directly for government projects. Plaintiff trade association failed to establish that the use of a project labor agreement constituted an infringement of the constitutional rights of its members. Thus, it did not have standing to challenge the terms of the contract between the state and the successful bidder.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because plaintiffs failed to make an evidentiary showing sufficient to establish their claimed right to standing to challenge the validity of defendant commissioner's use of a project labor agreement for the project.

Santini v. Connecticut Hazardous Waste Mgmt. Serv.


(SC 16023)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


251 Conn. 121; 739 A.2d 680; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 377


May 25, 1999, Argued  
November 9, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 5, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover damages for the alleged inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiffs' real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Norris L. O'Neill, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment in favor of defendant from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) finding that no unconstitutional taking occurred in an action to recover damages for inverse condemnation of plaintiffs' real property.


OVERVIEW: The defendant, Connecticut Hazardous Waste Management Service, a political subdivision of the state, publicly announced that it was selecting a site for the disposal of radioactive waste, and that land overlapping plaintiffs' development was one of three finalist locations. Plaintiffs sued defendant claiming that designating plaintiffs' property as a potential site constituted a temporary taking by inverse condemnation without just compensation and resulted in the destruction of the fair market value of their properties. The trial court granted judgment for defendant. Plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed concluding that defendant's conduct which consisted of nothing more, in a constitutional sense, than mere planning and temporary steps in anticipation of condemnation of property, not necessarily that of the plaintiffs, did not constitute a taking under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. Defendant's intention was not sufficiently definitive, fixed and irreversible to meet requirement of substantial invasion of a specific property interest.


OUTCOME: Judgment for defendant affirmed because defendant's mere planning and temporary steps in anticipation of condemnation of property, not necessarily that of plaintiffs, did not constitute a constitutional taking.

State v. Woods


(SC 15688)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 807; 740 A.2d 371; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 356


January 12, 1999, Argued  
October 12, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted Woods v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1036 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 3, 2003)
Judgment entered by, On rehearing at State v. Woods, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1875 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Murray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), alleging improper comments made by the prosecutor in his closing arguments, and inadequate self-defense instructions given to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder, arguing comments made by the prosecutor in closing arguments regarding defendant's failure to call his prior attorney to testify were unconstitutional, and self-defense instructions inadequately advised the jury that defendant's subjective belief of imminent danger, even if mistaken, could justify his conduct. The court declined to review defendant's first claim because it was not preserved at trial. Moreover, defendant could not prevail on his claim under plain error because the prosecutor's comments were proper argument, which went to weight of the evidence and weakness of defendant's case. Defendant's argument the comments violated his right to an attorney or attorney-client privilege were invalid because merely calling a non-constitutional claim constitutional did not justify review. The court found that mistake instruction was properly not given because defendant offered no evidence to prove mistake and the trial court's self-defense charge adequately instructed the jury.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; the court found defendant failed to preserve the right to challenge the prosecutor's comments on appeal and the comments were neither plain error nor did they implicate the missing witness argument rule; defendant's requested jury instruction was not proper because defendant offered no evidence supporting mistake of fact.

State v. Malave


(SC 15898)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 722; 737 A.2d 442; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 319


January 12, 1999, Argued  
September 21, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1258. As Amended December 21, 1999.
Writ of certiorari denied Malave v. Connecticut, 528 U.S. 1170, 145 L. Ed. 2d 1099, 120 S. Ct. 1195, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1258 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Malave v. Gomez, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15899 (D. Conn., July 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Spear and Cretella, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Malave, 47 Conn. App. 597, 707 A.2d 307, 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 42 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed his battery convictions, while refusing to consider the merits of his claim that the Secondino rule should be abandoned.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of assault in the first degree, for stabbing two men in a bar fight. The state requested and received a missing witness jury instruction, because of the defendant's failure to call a witness that could have supported his alibi. The Connecticut Supreme Court granted defendant's petition for certification limited to the issue of whether the missing witness rule of Secondino v. New Haven Gas Co., 147 Conn. 672, 165 A.2d 598 (1960), should be abandoned. The court held that the Secondino rule should be abandoned, because modern discovery procedures, and the elimination of the voucher rule had eliminated the need for it. However, the court held that the missing witness instruction in this case was harmless. The defendant had not demonstrated that the jury's evaluation of that evidence would have been different had the court not given the Secondino instruction.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction affirmed; although, for reasons of policy, the Secondino rule should be abandoned, the missing witness instruction given by the trial court was harmless.

State v. Misiorski


(SC 15983)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 280; 738 A.2d 595; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 294


February 16, 1999, Argued  
August 17, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Request for clarification to determine whether the statutory notification provisions concerning persons convicted of certain sexual offenses and who are on parole or probation were applicable to the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Scheinblum, J., issued an order authorizing the department of adult probation to implement the notification provisions, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) authorizing the office of adult probation to notify defendant's neighbors and bowling league participants of defendant's conviction for fourth-degree sexual assault and public indecency.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to fourth-degree sexual assault and public indecency in a case involving a mentally impaired victim. The office of adult probation informed the trial court that it intended to notify defendant's neighbors of the conviction. Stat. § 54-102s (c) vested the office of adult probation with discretion to make community notification regarding probationers convicted of any sexual offense, not only those offenses enumerated under the statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The trial court's designation of defendant as a "sexual offender" placed defendant among those offenders subject to careful supervision by the office of adult probation. Further, Connecticut law allowed a probation officer to notify the public about sexual offenders if the officer determined that public safety would be advanced.

Peabody N.E. Inc. v. DOT


(SC 16072)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 105; 735 A.2d 782; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 276


April 22, 1999, Argued  
August 10, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover moneys the plaintiffs had paid in the settlement of a claim by a subcontractor arising out of the defendant's alleged breach of a certain highway construction contract the defendant had executed with the named plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, Stengel, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporations appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, (Connecticut), which granted defendant state department of transportation's motion to dismiss the plaintiffs' action. Plaintiffs had filed the suit to recover moneys plaintiffs had paid in the settlement of a claim by a subcontractor arising out of defendant's alleged breach of a highway construction contract.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporations brought two separate actions within the applicable statute of limitations period and the court on appeal examined whether plaintiff could bring a third action, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-592. The third action was brought after the applicable statute of limitations period had expired; within one year of the determination of the last action filed within the applicable limitations period; and was not brought within one year of the determination of the first action filed within the applicable limitations period. The court on appeal concluded that such an action was, as a matter of law, time barred. The court determined that plaintiffs' federal action, which was the first to be brought, was for purposes of § 52-592 (a), the "original action." Because that action was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction more than five years prior to the filing of the complaint in the present action, plaintiffs could not rely upon § 52-592 (a). The case was filed less than one year after the dismissal of the first state court action, which was brought within the statute of limitations period, but the court found that the federal action, filed earlier, was the "original action."


OUTCOME: Dismissal of plaintiffs' action was affirmed because the suit was time barred. Plaintiffs' federal action, which was the first action filed by the plaintiff within the period of the applicable statute of limitations, was the original action for purposes of that statute. The action under consideration was filed more than five years after the dismissal of the original action, and failed to satisfy the requirements of the statute of limitations.

 

18 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Salmon


(SC 15930)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 147; 735 A.2d 333; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 278


April 27, 1999, Argued  
August 10, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by B & B Bail Bonds Agency, Inc., for release from a bond it had executed as surety on the defendant's behalf that was forfeited as a result of the defendant's failure to appear, and motion for a rebate from the bond forfeiture after payment of a compromise settlement executed with the state, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, White, J., denied the motions and B & B Bail Bonds Agency, Inc., appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Lavery, Schaller, Spear and Sullivan, Js., which, sua sponte, rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, and B & B Bail Bonds Agency, Inc., on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bondsman sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Court, (Connecticut), which dismissed its appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-263 of a trial court's order to forfeit its bond.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed an appellate judgment dismissing appellant bail bondsman's appeal of a trial court's order to forfeit its bond. The principal issue in the certified appeal was whether a bail bondsman, who was a nonparty to the underlying criminal action, could appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-263 from a trial court's order to forfeit its bond. The court concluded that although a writ of error could be brought, a bail bondsman, as a nonparty, did not have a right of appeal under § 52-263. Applying principles of statutory construction, the court held that the proper interpretation of the term "party" for purposes of § 52-263 included only actual parties to the underlying action. Further, the court expressly adopted a bright-line test requiring appellant, in order to establish a right of appellate review pursuant to § 52-263, to establish in the following sequence that (1) it was a party to the underlying action; (2) it was aggrieved by the trial court decision; and (3) the appeal was from a final judgment. The court rejected arguments that the bright-line test should be prospective only in its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an appellate judgment dismissing appellant bail bondsman's appeal of a trial court's order to forfeit its bond because as a nonparty, a bail bondsman did not have a right of appeal under the applicable Connecticut statute.

State v. Kruelski


(SC 16029)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


250 Conn. 1; 737 A.2d 377; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 272


June 3, 1999, Argued  
August 3, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1226.


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crime of offering to make home improvements without being registered, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, where the court, Moraghan, J., granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Hull, J., with Heiman, J., dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings; on remand, the court, Carroll, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Schaller and Healey, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the appellate court (Connecticut), concluding that further criminal proceedings were not barred by the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. amend. V, and affirming the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss, in an action charging defendant with offering to perform home improvements without being registered as a contractor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(5). Defendant claimed that because the trial court rendered a judgment of acquittal in his trial, further prosecution was barred by his constitutional right not to be placed twice in jeopardy for the same offense. The state maintained that the trial court's judgment did not constitute an acquittal for purposes of double jeopardy because it was based solely on defendant's statute of limitations defense, and not on a determination that the state's evidence regarding any element of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(5) was insufficient to support a guilty verdict. The court agreed with the state. Defendant's statute of limitations defense was not a defense that, when proved, negated any element of the offense or established a legal justification for an otherwise criminal act. The trial court's judgment was based solely on defendant's statute of limitations defense and not on any resolution in favor of defendant of any element of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(5). Thus, the judgment rendered by the trial court did not constitute an acquittal for purposes of double jeopardy, and defendant could be retried.


OUTCOME: The judgment affirming denial of defendant's motion to dismiss was affirmed because the court found that defendant's midtrial acquittal based on his statute of limitations defense did not constitute an acquittal for purposes of double jeopardy, and consequently, the legal restraints of the law pertaining to defendant's double jeopardy rights did not bar a retrial.

State v. Eady


(SC 15858)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


249 Conn. 431; 733 A.2d 112; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 229


March 26, 1998, Argued  
July 6, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7945.


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of less than four ounces of marijuana and possession of marijuana with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number thirteen, where the court, Graham, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court, Mullarkey, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed; this court affirmed the judgment of dismissal; thereafter, this court granted the state's motion for reconsideration en banc.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State moved for reconsideration en banc after a Connecticut five-judge court affirmed the lower court's grant of criminal defendant's motion to dismiss drug charges against him for lack of sufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with various drug offenses after police seized illegal drugs from his home. A firefighter who had entered the home in response to a fire saw the drugs in plain view and showed them to police officers. Defendant filed motion to suppress on grounds that the warrantless search and seizure violated his rights under U. S. Const. amend. IV. The lower court granted defendant's motion to suppress and subsequent motion to dismiss. State appealed by permission and a five-judge court affirmed. The state moved for reconsideration en banc and the court reversed. It held that U.S. Const. amend. IV did not require suppression of the illicit drugs seized by an agent of the state, lawfully present in the defendant's bedroom, who observed a substance that a reasonably prudent firefighter would have believed to be drugs. The court found that the officer's entry was merely an extension of the firefighter's lawful presence and that the officer was not constitutionally required to obtain a warrant.


OUTCOME: Upon reconsideration en banc, the lower court's judgment that affirmed defendant's motion to dismiss was reversed and the case was remanded with direction that the motion to suppress be denied and for further proceedings according to law. The court found the seizure of the drugs lawful under the plain view exception.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developers appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted defendant city, planning and zoning commission, and commissioners' motion to dismiss plaintiffs' action alleging federal equal protection violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.

Clarke v. Commissioner of Correction


(SC 15575)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


249 Conn. 350; 732 A.2d 754; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 210


January 19, 1999, Argued  
June 22, 1999, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petitions for writs of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the petitions were consolidated and tried to the court, Martin, J.; judgments denying the petitions, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Lavery and Heiman, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgments, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court. Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Although the habeas court rejected petitioner's claim of actual innocence on the merits, the appellate court (Connecticut) affirmed because petitioner's claim did not present any "newly discovered" evidence of actual innocence of drug offenses for which he was convicted. The state supreme court certified petitioner's appeal to determine whether petitioner was required to establish that claim of innocence was sustained by new evidence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an amended habeas corpus petition claiming actual innocence of the drug-dealing offenses of which he stood convicted. In rejecting petitioner's claim of actual innocence on the merits, the habeas court did not employ the "newly discovered evidence" requirement. Contrariwise, the appellate court affirmed because the evidence on which petitioner relied for the actual innocence claim was not "newly discovered" within the meaning of that phrase in habeas corpus parlance. The state supreme court granted certification to appeal the important question of whether a habeas corpus petitioner who claimed actual innocence of the crime of which he stood convicted must establish that the claim of innocence was sustained by newly discovered evidence. Finding that the case did not present facts that squarely and necessarily required such question to be addressed, the court dismissed petitioner's appeal on the ground that certification was improvidently granted. Because the state supreme court did not decide whether petitioner's claim of actual innocence must be based on new evidence, the issue should be regarded as an open question in the court's habeas jurisprudence.


OUTCOME: Holding that certification to appeal was improvidently granted because there had been no adjudication to suggest a substantial basis for habeas corpus petitioner's claim of actual innocence with respect to drug-dealing convictions, the court dismissed petitioner's appeal from lower courts' alternative denials of petitioner's writ. Thus, it remained an open question whether petitioner's claim of actual innocence must be based on new evidence.

Chase Manhattan Bank v. Gavin


(SC 15875)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


249 Conn. 172; 733 A.2d 782; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 155


October 27, 1998, Argued  
June 1, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7105.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision by the defendant denying the plaintiffs' request for refunds of income taxes paid on five certain trusts, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, tax session at Hartford, where the court, McWeeny, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a grant of summary judgment and judgment thereon from the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) in favor of defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services, after defendant denied plaintiffs' request for refunds of income taxes paid on certain trusts.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services, thus denying plaintiff trustee's request for refunds of 1993 income taxes paid on four testamentary and one inter vivos trust. Plaintiffs appealed, contending that the taxation scheme, as applied, violated the due process clause and commerce clause of the constitution. All of the trusts were resident trusts as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-701(a)(4). The court held that the taxability of the income of the resident testamentary trusts was based on the fact that the testators were Connecticut domiciliaries at death. The income of the inter vivos trust was taxable because both the settlor of the trust when the trust was established and the beneficiary were Connecticut domiciliaries. The contacts between the trusts and the state were sufficient constitutionally to treat the trusts as if they were domiciliaries of the state and, therefore, to tax their undistributed income. The court also concluded that any incentives and risks had not been sufficiently established so as to result in a dormant commerce clause violation. The court found the denial of refunds was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement below denying refunds for the tax paid on the trusts, on the grounds that the contacts with Connecticut were sufficient to satisfy the due process clause, and gave the trusts fair warning that they were subject to its tax jurisdiction. The state was entitled to tax all of their income, wherever generated, like that of other domiciliaries. No dormant commerce clause violation was established.

City of Danbury v. Dana Inv. Corporation/Lot No. GO8065


(SC 15878)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


249 Conn. 1; 730 A.2d 1128; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 147


April 21, 1998, Argued  
May 25, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in 111 cases, to foreclose a municipal tax lien on certain real property owned by the named defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and referred to Hon. Walter M. Pickett, Jr., judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment in each case of strict foreclosure, from which the defendant Philbury, Inc., filed a joint appeal; thereafter, the court taxed certain additional costs and fees to the defendant Philbury, Inc., and the defendant Philbury, Inc., filed an amended joint appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation jointly appealed from judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which rendered 111 separate judgments of strict foreclosure of municipal real estate tax liens in favor of plaintiff city and taxed certain additional costs and fees to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant corporation owned 111 individual lots of an undeveloped, or paper, subdivision. Plaintiff city brought 111 separate actions to foreclose on 111 separate tax liens for unpaid real estate taxes. The cases were tried together as contested foreclosure cases. The trial court rendered a judgment of strict foreclosure and awarded the city separate fees and costs in each case. Defendant appealed. The appellate court affirmed the trial court judgment in all respects except for the award of sheriff's fees, which was reversed and remanded, as an abuse of discretion. On appeal, defendant contended it should have been permitted to contest the assessments underlying the liens being foreclosed, and it was improper for the trial court to award multiple entry fees, attorney's fees, appraisal fees, and sheriff's fees and costs in each of the 111 cases. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's untimely challenge to the assessments or awarding fees and costs. The court properly reasoned that the 111 cases were not for the recovery of the same demand because each lot was a separate tax entity.


OUTCOME: Judgments of strict foreclosure of municipal real estate tax liens in favor of plaintiff city affirmed in all respects, because the trial court did not abuse its discretion, except for the award of sheriff's fees, which was reversed to be reduced drastically and recalculated.

 

26 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Barton v. Ducci Elec. Contrs., Inc.


(SC 15953)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


248 Conn. 793; 730 A.2d 1149; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 146


November 3, 1998, Argued  
May 25, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the eighth district denying the plaintiff's application for permanent partial disability benefits, brought to the compensation review board, which reserved certain questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Workers' Compensation Review Board (Connecticut) reserved questions of law pending in plaintiff employee's appeal of a decision from the Workers' Compensation Commissioner for the Eighth District, which had denied plaintiff's application pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308(b) for permanent partial disability benefits for damage to his skin in a propane fire that occurred while he had been employed by defendant corporation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that, by the plain language of the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308(b), the workers' compensation commissioner was only authorized to grant compensation for the loss or permanent partial disability of a scheduled body party or organ, noting that there was no provision that provided the commissioner with discretion to award compensation regarding an unscheduled body part or organ, such as skin. The court then noted that, as neither a fundamental right nor a suspect class was at issue, the rational basis test was the appropriate standard for determining the constitutionality of the classification under the statute. The court held that the statute did not violate the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions where the legislature's legitimate interest in reducing the costs of the workers' compensation system was a rational justification for constructing Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308(b). The court remanded with direction to affirm the decision of the commissioner, declining to discuss the due process challenge because plaintiff had not provided sufficient argument in support of such claims.


OUTCOME: The court remanded with instructions to affirm the denial of plaintiff employee's application for permanent partial disability benefits for damage to his skin, finding that the statute which authorized the workers' compensation commissioner to award compensation regarding scheduled body parts and organs, which did not include skin, did not violate constitutional equal protection provisions where there was a rational basis for the statute.

State v. Jason B.


(SC 15841)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


248 Conn. 543; 729 A.2d 760; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 127


November 6, 1998, Argued  
May 4, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7134.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with being a youthful offender for having committed the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the court, Barry, J.; judgment of guilty of being a youthful offender for committing the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Landau, Dupont and Shea, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant teenager appealed a decision from the Appellate Court of Connecticut, which affirmed the judgment of guilty against defendant of being a youthful offender, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-76b, for having committed the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court rejected the contention that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71 was unconstitutionally vague and had violated defendant teenager's equal protection rights, finding that a person of ordinary intelligence would have understood that a person born in May, 1978, was more than two years older than a person born in August, 1980. The court noted that the lack of knowledge by defendant or a person in his particular age category did not enhance his vagueness challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71. The court then upheld the validity of defendant's conviction where the challenged information, which charged a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, was not so obviously defective that by no reasonable construction could it have been said not to have charged the offense for which conviction was had. The court affirmed the adjudication of guilt, finding that the legislature's articulated reasons for enacting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71, namely, the prevention of teenage pregnancy and the limitation of the opportunity of more sexually experienced adolescents to take advantage of those much younger, provided a rational basis the statute's enactment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to adjudicate defendant teenager a youthful offender, finding that defendant had been properly found to have been "more than two years older" than the victim within the meaning of the statute where difference in time between his birth date and the victim's was two years, three months, and seven days; assault statute was valid where it had passed rational basis review.

 

30 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ham v. Greene


(SC 15806)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


248 Conn. 508; 729 A.2d 740; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 126


January 21, 1999, Argued  
May 4, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, false arrest, malicious prosecution and violations of the plaintiff's civil rights under the state and federal constitutions as a result of alleged misconduct by the defendants, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Corradino, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court denied the defendants' motion to arrest judgment, to set aside the verdict, to grant a directed verdict or for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or, in the alternative, for a new trial, or in the further alternative, for a remittitur, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, and the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) denying their motion to arrest judgment, to set aside the verdict, to grant a directed verdict or for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or for a new trial, or for a remittitur, in an action to recover damages for, inter alia, false arrest, malicious prosecution and violations of plaintiff's civil rights.


OVERVIEW: A jury delivered a verdict holding defendant police department detectives liable for common-law malicious prosecution and false arrest claims and federal civil rights claims. Defendants' motion to arrest judgment, to set aside the verdict, to direct a verdict in their favor or for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or, in the alternative, for a new trial or a remittitur was denied by the trial court which rendered judgment in accordance with the jury verdicts. Defendants appealed. Plaintiff had been arrested and held on the basis of an affidavit prepared by defendants supporting a request for an arrest warrant. The affidavit was based on statements from informants who that conflicted with the testimony of neutral witnesses in descriptions of the shooter. One informant had failed to identify plaintiff in two previous statements. The court found that these omissions materially contributed to the objective basis for finding probable cause. The court could not conclude as a matter of law that the probable cause calculus would not have been different or that the omitted information could not possibly have affected the magistrate's decision to issue the warrant. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict below in favor of plaintiff. The jury's verdict reflected its answer that more probably than not, no warrant would have issued based upon the corrected affidavit. The court could not conclude that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to set aside the verdict and direct judgment in defendants' favor.

Angelsea Prods. v. Commission on Human Rights & Opportunities


(SC 16008)

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a declaratory ruling by the named defendant determining that the failure of a commission hearing officer to complete within the statutory time period an investigation of the defendant Susan E. Hyde's complaint alleging discriminatory employment practices by the plaintiff did not deprive the named defendant of jurisdiction to proceed on that complaint, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Maloney, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court, which resolved the reserved questions in favor of the plaintiff; subsequently, the court, DiPentima, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for entry of a final judgment in it's favor consistent with this court's resolution of the reserved questions and granted the motion to dismiss filed by the named defendant and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon transfer from the Connecticut Appellate Court and under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-83(b) and 46a-84(b), plaintiff employer appealed defendant commission on human rights and opportunities' declaration that that it had jurisdiction under 1996 Conn. Acts 96-241 over defendant employee's complaint, and that employee's public hearing should continue.


OVERVIEW: Defendant employee filed a complaint with defendant commission on human rights and opportunities against plaintiff employer for discrimination. Plaintiff moved to dismiss. The commission declared that it had jurisdiction over defendant employee's complaint and that her public hearing should continue. Plaintiff appealed, and the case was transferred to the court. The court affirmed because 1996 Conn. Acts 96-241 gave the commission jurisdiction in all cases in which it failed to meet time deadlines, application of 1996 Conn. Acts 96-241 did not violate plaintiff's due process rights to an adequate and meaningful opportunity to adjudication, and 1996 Conn. Acts 96-241 did not violate the principle of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: Defendant commission on human rights and opportunities' declaration that that it had jurisdiction over defendant employee's complaint and that employee's public hearing should continue was affirmed because the statute granting jurisdiction to the commission violated neither plaintiff employer's due process rights, nor separation of powers.

State v. Hodge


(SC 15266)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


248 Conn. 207; 726 A.2d 531; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 76


March 18, 1998, Argued  
April 6, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7157.
Writ of certiorari denied Hodge v. Connecticut, 528 U.S. 969, 145 L. Ed. 2d 319, 120 S. Ct. 409, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7157 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hodge v. Strange, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7566 (D. Conn., Apr. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony and carrying a pistol without a permit and with two counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict of guilty of one count each of murder, the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the capital felony count and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Hodge, 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2789 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 23, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut) that entered convictions against him for murder, manslaughter, and carrying a pistol without a permit.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's mother's kitchen was damaged in a fire, defendant began to negotiate an insurance settlement with the victims, who were the owner and an associate of the insurance company. When defendant became dissatisfied with the settlement, he arranged a meeting with the victims at their office. The victims refused to authorize a higher settlement amount. When defendant got up to leave the office, he shot both victims with a handgun and killed them. On appeal, defendant's initial argument was a Batson claim, which asserted that the prosecution exercised its peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory manner. The court reviewed the trial court's rejection of defendant's Batson claim under the clearly erroneous standard of review and upheld the trial court's decision that each peremptory challenge was supported by valid, race neutral reasons. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the trial court's jury instruction on the affirmative defense of emotional disturbance included a definition of "extreme" that imposed an unreasonably high threshold on him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for murder, manslaughter, and carrying a pistol without a permit were affirmed. The court held that the prosecution did not exercise its peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory manner. The court also upheld the trial court's jury instruction on defendant's affirmative defense of extreme emotional disturbance.

State v. Schiappa


(SC 15696)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


248 Conn. 132; 728 A.2d 466; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 68


March 24, 1998, Argued  
March 23, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5671.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree, conspiracy to commit murder and hindering prosecution in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree and hindering prosecution in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Landau and Hennessy, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings on the charge of manslaughter in the first degree, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the prosecution's petition for certification to appeal the appellate court's reversal of defendant's convictions of manslaughter pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3) and hindering prosecution pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-166.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend beat and stabbed defendant's husband in a cemetery one evening. At defendant's trial, her friend testified that he did not remember much of the encounter. The trial judge thus admitted the friend's roommate's testimony regarding a statement the friend made implicating defendant in her husband's death. Likewise, the judge permitted testimony by the roommate regarding statements made by the roommate, instructing the jury that it should make a preliminary determination regarding whether defendant's friend made a statement in defendant's presence that could be construed as one resulting in an adoptive admission. The appeals court reversed. The court here affirmed defendant's convictions of manslaughter pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3) and hindering prosecution pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-166. The court held that the hearsay statement of the roommate regarding statements made by defendant's friend were properly admitted under the against penal interest exception due to the friend's partial memory loss regarding the circumstances of the death. The court also upheld the trial court's handling of the adoptive admission under plain error review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court, and affirmed defendant's convictions of manslaughter and hindering prosecution, affirming the trial court's admission under the statement against penal interest exception to the hearsay rule of one witness' testimony due to his partial memory loss, as well as the statement of another witness made in defendant's presence which was admitted as an adoptive admission by defendant.

Statewide Griev. Comm. v. Spirer


(SC 15853)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 762; 725 A.2d 948; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 29


December 10, 1998, Argued  
March 2, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, D'Andrea, J.; judgment suspending the defendant from the practice of law for six months, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Schaller, J., with Spear, J., concurring and dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney in a certified appeal challenged a decision from the appellate court (Connecticut), suspending him from the practice of law for five years, following his felony convictions in federal court.


OVERVIEW: After a plea of guilty in the federal court, defendant attorney was convicted under 18 U.S.C.S. § 1344(a)(1), (2) and 18 U.S.C.S. § 2. In an action by plaintiff statewide grievance committee, the trial court suspended defendant from the practice of law for six months. Plaintiff claimed on appeal that the trial court abused its discretion when it (1) suspended defendant from the practice of law for only six months and (2) did not discipline defendant further because of his admission at the presentence hearing that he had made certain misrepresentations in federal court. The appellate court found that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-91a, the trial court was bound to impose suspension from the practice of law for at least five years; thus, it reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case. On defendant's petition for certification, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-91a applied only to felony convictions in a Connecticut state court. Thus, the lower court improperly applied § 51-91a. Under the circumstances, the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The court reversed the judgment below and remanded the case with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's imposition of suspension for five years of defendant attorney, who was convicted in federal court, and remanded the case with directions to affirm the trial court's imposition of a six-month suspension. The trial court did not abuse its broad discretion. The appellate court improperly concluded that the statute in question applied to attorneys convicted of felonies in federal court or courts of other states.

City Recycling, Inc. v. State


(SC 15940)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 751; 725 A.2d 937; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 26


December 2, 1998, Argued  
February 23, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a statute prohibiting the commissioner of environmental protection from authorizing the construction of a new volume reduction plant within one-quarter mile of a child day care center in a municipality with a population of greater than 100,000 persons, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Hickey, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved two questions of law for the advice of this court. Further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recycling company sought declaratory judgment that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-208a(a) was unconstitutional because it prohibited defendant commissioner of environmental protection from processing its application to expand its existing recycling facility. Plaintiff claimed the law violated his right to substantive due process and equal protection of the law, and these questions were reserved for the appeals court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff recycling company submitted an application to expand its recycling facility. Defendant state of Connecticut and defendant commissioner of the department of environmental protection refused to process the application because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-208a(a) prohibited defendant commissioner from approving establishment of a new volume reduction plant within one-quarter mile of a child day care center. Plaintiff sought declaratory judgment that § 22a-208a(a) violated its right to substantive due process and equal protection. The parties agreed upon a stipulation of facts and reserved two questions of law for the appeals court. The appeals court refused to answer the reserved questions because they should have been construed as facial challenges to the law, and plaintiff did not provide a sufficient basis for the appeals court to determine that it suffered any constitutional deprivation. The stipulated facts were insufficient because they did not state that plaintiff's proposed facility posed no reasonable possibility of environmental hazards, and, if there was a reasonable possibility of such hazards, § 22a-208a(a) would pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The appeals court refused to answer the questions the parties reserved for the court because it held that plaintiff's challenges to the statute should have been construed as facial challenges to the law's constitutionality, and the facts to which the parties stipulated failed to indicate that the proposed expansion to plaintiff's facility posed no reasonable possibility of environmental hazards.

State v. Delgado


(SC 15632)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 616; 725 A.2d 306; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 15


November 4, 1998, Argued  
February 5, 1999, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by State v. Delgado, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3668 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 23, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Delgado v. Comm'r of Corr., 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2218 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), entering defendant's conviction as an accessory to murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8, 53a-54 and possession of a firearm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k. Defendant claimed reversal was necessary where, inter alia, the evidence was insufficient to convict and he was deprived of his right to counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions as an accessory to murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8, 53a-54 and possession of a firearm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k were upheld where sufficient evidence existed to show he aided in killing a person and where defendant enjoyed his right to counsel. Defendant was a gang member who argued with a rival gang member. Defendant and another member of his gang shot and killed the member. Defendant confessed he thought he had shot the victim. Defendant was convicted and appealed, claiming there was insufficient evidence to convict, he was denied the right to counsel when substitute counsel was used, and an accessory liability jury instruction was improper. The reviewing court affirmed, holding where there was sufficient evidence that defendant aided in the victim's death, that he shot the victim at close range and acknowledged his involvement, the conviction was proper. Where substitute counsel was used during jury deliberations, defendant's right to counsel was not implicated because no adversarial matters were undertaken. Where the trial court clearly delineated the dual intent requirement of accessorial liability, no error occurred.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's entry of defendant's accessory to murder and firearm possession convictions, holding where there was sufficient evidence to show defendant's shooting of victim aided in causing his death, conviction was proper. Where substitute counsel was used during jury deliberations and no adversarial matters were handled, defendant was not denied his right to counsel.
