In re Adoption of Baby Z.


(SC 15868), (SC 15869)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 474; 724 A.2d 1035; 1999 Conn. LEXIS 4


May 26, 1998, Argued  
January 26, 1999, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in the first case, by the petitioners from a decision by the Probate Court in the district of Ledyard on an appeal from a decision by the respondent adoption review board, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich, where the court, Handy, J., granted the respondent adoption review board's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioners appealed. Appeal, in the second case, by the petitioners from a decision by the respondent adoption review board denying the application by the Probate Court in the district of Ledyard for a waiver of the adoption placement requirement pursuant to General Statutes § 45a-764, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich and tried to the court, Handy, J.; judgment for the petitioners granting the appeal and remanding the case to the respondent adoption review board for further proceedings, from which the respondent adoption review board appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from an adoption-related probate decision. Respondent sought review of that same judgment insofar as it sustained petitioners' administrative appeal involving the function of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-724(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners' probate petition to adopt a child whom they, as same-sex partners, had raised was denied. Reviewing that denial, the lower court determined that respondent review board could waive the requirement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-724(a)(1) that only a statutory parent may give a child in such an adoption. Respondent review board denied petitioners' resulting application for such a waiver. Petitioners appealed the lower court's dismissal of their probate court appeal. Respondent review board appealed the lower court's decision to pursue a waiver application through remand. The court considered petitioners' and respondent's appeals pursuant to Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 4023 (now § 65-1), and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c). Basing its decision on a literal reading of § 45a-724(a)(1) that did not provide for waiver, the court held that respondent review board's decision to deny petitioners' adoption petition was not reviewable. Finding respondent review board to be an agency within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-166(1), the court thus affirmed the dismissal of petitioners' probate appeal. On similar grounds, the court reversed the lower court's decision to remand.


OUTCOME: The court determined that respondent review board's decision to deny petitioners' adoption petition was not a reviewable order and that respondent review board did not have the authority to waive the statutory adoption requirements. Accordingly, the court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of petitioners' probate appeal and reversed the lower court's decision to sustain petitioners' administrative appeal.

 

40 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cumberland Farms v. Town of Groton


(SC 15797)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 196; 719 A.2d 465; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 394


April 24, 1998, Argued  
November 3, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, and referred to Hon. D. Michael Hurley, judge trial referee, who granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Schaller and Spear, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The zoning board of appeals of defendant town denied plaintiff landowner's application for a zoning variance. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the trial court's decision, concluding that the landowner's inverse condemnation action was premature because its administrative appeal from the denial of its application for a variance was not yet final and, therefore, the action was not justiciable. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the town's zoning board of appeals (board) denied the landowner's application for a variance to the zoning regulations, the landowner appealed the board's decision regarding its variance application to the trial court. The landowner filed a separate complaint claiming inverse condemnation of the property. The trial court granted the town's motion to dismiss the inverse condemnation action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction due to the pending appeal of the board's decision. The court found that the board's denial of the variance application constituted a final decision that rendered ripe for adjudication the inverse condemnation claim. The regulatory action upon which the taking claim was based was complete when the board, as the initial decision-maker, denied the application for a variance, and the inverse condemnation action then became justiciable. The exemption from the exhaustion doctrine was applicable to pure taking claims. The necessity of submitting multiple plans was not a per se rule but was based on the circumstances of each case. Submission of additional plans would have been unavailing and, thus, was not a requisite to establishing finality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. The case was remanded to the appellate court with directions to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings according to law.

In re Darlene C.


(SC 15886)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


247 Conn. 1; 717 A.2d 1242; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 342


May 28, 1998, Argued  
September 15, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and families for the termination of the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, Juvenile Matters, Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the court, Foley, J., dismissed the petition and, sua sponte, enjoined the petitioner from filing petitions for termination of parental rights drafted, signed and filed by persons not admitted to the practice of law and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the commissioner of the state department of children and families, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, Juvenile Matters, Child Protection Session at Middletown (Connecticut), which enjoined the commissioner from filing petitions for termination of parental rights drafted, signed, and filed by persons not admitted to the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that a social worker had prepared and filed a defective petition in a termination of parental rights case. Without first affording the commissioner an opportunity to be heard, the trial court, sua sponte, ordered the commissioner to cease and desist from the further unauthorized practice of law. On review, the court held that the drafting, signing, and filing of termination and neglect petitions by nonlawyer representatives of the commissioner were acts expressly permitted under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17a-112 and 46b-129. Moreover, Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 26-1(l) permitted any person authorized by statute to execute termination and neglect petitions. Thus, such activities did not constitute the unauthorized practice of law.The court reversed the judgment to the extent that it enjoined the commissioner from filing petitions for the termination of parental rights that were prepared, signed, and filed by persons not admitted to the practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order in part, concluding that the commissioner of the department of children and families and her designees were statutorily authorized to prepare, sign, and file petitions for the termination of parental rights.

State v. Cardwell

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from, inter alia, selling admission tickets to sporting and entertainment events in violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, L. Sullivan, J.; judgment for the state enjoining the defendant from, inter alia, selling tickets to entertainment events for a price greater than $ 3 more than the price printed on the ticket, and granting certain other relief, and the defendant appealed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court at Hartford (Connecticut) determined that defendant sole proprietor engaged in conduct that violated Conn. Gen. The court issued a permanent injunction against the sole proprietor and assessed penalties and fines. The sole proprietor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state filed a complaint charging the sole proprietor with engaging in ticket scalping, in violation of § 53-289 and CUTPA, engaging in various other practices in violation of CUTPA, and violating § 35-1 by operating an office in Connecticut without having filed a trade name certificate with the town clerk in violation of CUTPA. State v. Blackman


(SC 15401)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


246 Conn. 547; 716 A.2d 101; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 328


June 3, 1998, Argued  
August 25, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) judgment, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, and felony murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c. Defendant appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: The police had set up a sobriety checkpoint, stopped defendant, and took defendant into custody when he could not produce a license. Defendant was read Miranda rights and signed a rights waiver. Defendant was transferred to a different police unit, since there was a warrant for his arrest, signed a rights waiver, and first gave those police an alibi and then voluntarily admitted being at the scene of the shooting. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress his statements since, without deciding whether the sobriety checkpoint was reasonable, defendant's statements were not the product of the initial stop. The court compared the Colvin and Daugaard cases where the statements were the product of the execution of a valid arrest warrant and subsequent lawful interrogation. That defendant was already in custody merely facilitated the execution of the valid arrest warrant. Defendant was not questioned about the killing by the checkpoint officers. The evidence was sufficient to convict. In context, the reasonable doubt instruction was proper, not a constitutional magnitude violation, and so not entitled to Golding plain unpreserved error review.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Francis


(SC 15633)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


246 Conn. 339; 717 A.2d 696; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 317


May 27, 1998, Argued  
August 18, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, carrying a pistol without a permit and altering or removing an identification mark on a pistol, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) for murder, carrying a pistol without a permit, and altering or removing an identification mark on a pistol. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in improperly limiting defendant's right to cross-examine, and in instructing the jury on the presumption set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-36 and on the intent element of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54(a), carrying a pistol without a permit, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35, and altering or removing an identification mark on a pistol, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-36. Defendant appealed from the judgment of the trial court, claiming that the trial court erred in refusing to allow him to introduce evidence that two key state's witnesses were gang members, and in instructing the jury on the presumption set forth in § 29-36 and on the intent element of murder. The court found that defendant's claims that the trial court improperly limited his cross-examination were not appealable because the trial court did not make a ruling on the matter. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, finding that the trial judge had properly instructed the jury on the intent element of murder. The court, however, reversed defendant's conviction for altering or removing identification mark on a pistol because the trial court's instructions, viewed in their entirety, presented the statutory inference as mandatory, thereby misleading the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of murder and carrying a pistol without a permit because the trial court had not made an appealable ruling on the admissibility of witnesses' gang membership and did not err in instructing on the intent element of murder. The court, however, reversed, defendant's conviction for altering or removing identification mark on a pistol because the instructions presented the statutory inference as mandatory.

In re Dean

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Judicial Review Council entered a decision to publicly censure respondent superior court judge for certain conduct resulting in the violation of the canons of the Code of Judicial Conduct, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-51n(a)(1). The judge sought judicial review of the decision.


OVERVIEW: The judge, who had been ordered to pay a certain sum of weekly installment, refused to make further payment when he filed for bankruptcy. The court determined that whether the judge's conduct compromised the integrity of the court did not depend upon his being liable for contempt. It held that the public censure sanction was appropriate to preserve the integrity and independence of the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The decision to censure the judge was affirmed.

Packer v. Board of Educ.


(SC 15862)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


246 Conn. 89; 717 A.2d 117; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 297


March 26, 1998, Argued  
August 4, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, an injunction prohibiting the defendant from enforcing the expulsion of the named plaintiff from a public school, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where Hon. Walter M. Pickett, judge trial referee, granted the plaintiffs' application for a temporary restraining order; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' application for a temporary injunction and entered an order directing that the previous temporary restraining order be continued until further order of the court; subsequently, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for clarification of the judgment and rendered a supplemental judgment, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) that granted plaintiff student's application for an injunction prohibiting enforcement of plaintiff's expulsion from school on the grounds, inter alia, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d(a)(1) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to plaintiff and on its face.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff student was arrested for possession of marijuana and drug paraphernalia that were found in plaintiff's car off the school campus. After a hearing before defendant school board, plaintiff was expelled from school for violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d(a)(1), which allowed expulsion for off campus activity that seriously disrupted the educational process. The court affirmed the lower court's grant of the injunction but found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233d(a)(1) was not unconstitutional on its face. The court held that § 10-233d(a)(1) was unconstitutional as it was applied to plaintiff because it did not give a reasonable person notice that possession of marijuana was the type of activity that would be considered seriously disruptive of the educational process. Plaintiff was not provided with constitutionally adequate notice that his behavior would result in expulsion. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague on its face because it did give notice that other conduct, such as phoning in a bomb threat, was clearly disruptive of the educational process.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court granting the plaintiff student's application for an injunction was affirmed because the statute under which plaintiff was expelled did not give plaintiff constitutionally adequate notice that his conduct could lead to expulsion. The order was reversed insofar as it concluded that the statute at issue was facially unconstitutional.

State v. Wright


(SC 15816)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


246 Conn. 132; 716 A.2d 870; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 299


June 2, 1998, Argued  
August 4, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Landau and Schaller, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of a Connecticut court of appeals, which affirmed his conviction for the crime of larceny from the person, a class C felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the legislative classification of larceny from the person as a class C felony, and simple robbery as a class D felony, violated his rights to equal protection of the laws under the federal or state constitution. He contended that his rights were violated because larceny was a crime of a less serious nature than robbery and the statutory penalties were more severe for the less serious crime. On appeal the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the legislature rationally could have concluded as a categorical matter, larceny from the person was a more serious offense than simple robbery, and therefore warranted a more severe penalty. Trespass to the person of the victim that inheres in larceny from the person potentially was a source of greater harm than the force or threat of force that characterizes a simple robbery. Alternatively, the legislature might have considered the ease with which the crime potentially could be committed. Either way, for purposes of rational-basis review, articulation of the legislative rational was unnecessary, so long as the court conceivably or reasonably be related to a legislative purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's larceny conviction.

Vitti v. Allstate Ins. Co.


(SC 15734)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


245 Conn. 169; 713 A.2d 1269; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 231


February 17, 1998, Argued  
June 30, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Action to recover proceeds allegedly due pursuant to the underinsured motorist provision of an automobile liability policy issued by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and submitted to the court, Moraghan, J., on a stipulation of facts; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer challenged an order from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) that did not reduce the amount payable to plaintiff insured under an underinsured motorist policy by amounts plaintiff would receive as social security disability benefits, and the appeal was transferred directly from the Appellate Court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insured was injured in an automobile collision, and he received the entire amount of the negligent driver's liability coverage. Plaintiff filed an action to recover under the underinsured motorist provision of a policy issued to him by defendant insurer, and the trial court refused to offset defendant's liability by amounts plaintiff would receive as social security disability benefits after determining that this reduction would be contrary to public policy. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that both Conn. Agencies Regs. § 38a-334-6 (d) and the language of the policy unambiguously allowed defendant to offset the available underinsured coverage by the social security benefits paid or payable to plaintiff. The court found that the regulation was within the scope of the authorizing statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-336, and it was not contrary to the legislature's intent. Allowing an offset for social security benefits did not conflict with the statutory intention to guaranty a minimum level of compensation to all motorists equal to the coverage of their own policy without allowing multiple compensation for the same harm. Thus, the regulation was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's order and remanded with direction to reduce the judgment by the amount of social security payments that plaintiff insured would have received because the policy issued by defendant insurer and a Connecticut insurance regulation permitting the offset were unambiguous and not contrary to the statutory intention of guaranteeing a minimum level of compensation to insured motorists.

James L. v. Commissioner of Correction


(SC 15847)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


245 Conn. 132; 712 A.2d 947; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 218


April 23, 1998, Argued  
June 23, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Bishop, J., denied the respondent's motions to dismiss and for summary judgment; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), and respondent State's motions to dismiss and for summary judgment were denied. After a hearing, the petition was granted and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of sexual offenses, and his conviction was upheld on appeal. In his first habeas petition he claimed ineffective assistance of trial counsel, and his petition was denied. He filed a second habeas petition, alleging ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The principal issue on appeal was whether, after a finding of ineffective assistance of counsel, a habeas court had the authority to restore petitioner's right to sentence review under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195, after the statute's 30 day time limit has passed. The court found that petitioner had not abused the writ by filing a new claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel after rejection of a similar claim against his trial attorney, and concluded that the two petitions do not raise the "same ground" within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 23-29 (3). The 30 day time limit did not act as a jurisdictional bar to consideration of an application for sentence review that was delayed by reason of ineffective assistance of counsel. The habeas court, therefore, had the authority to consider what remedy was appropriate in light of its finding of a constitutional deprivation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting petitioner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and reinstating his right to seek a review of his sentence.

State v. Angel C.


(SC 15702), (SC 15703), (SC 15704), (SC 15795)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


245 Conn. 93; 715 A.2d 652; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 220


March 19, 1998, Argued  
June 23, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations, in the first three cases, charging the defendants with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters, where the cases were transferred to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court; thereafter, the court, Devlin, J., denied the defendants' motions to dismiss, and the defendants were presented to the court on conditional pleas of nolo contendere to the charge of being a youthful offender on the charge of conspiracy to commit robbery in the second degree; judgment, in each case, of guilty in accordance with the plea, and the defendants filed separate appeals; subsequently, the appeals were consolidated and transferred to this court. Information, in the fourth case, charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, conspiracy to commit kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree, attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior [***2] Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford, where the case was transferred to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court; thereafter, the court, Spada, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss, and the state filed a substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court, Espinosa, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charges of unlawful restraint in the first degree, burglary in the third degree and sexual assault in the fourth degree; the court, Espinosa, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea, and the defendant appealed; the appeal was thereafter consolidated with the appeals in the first three cases and transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An appeal arose out of four consolidated cases, each challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127(a), after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) denied the four defendants' motions to dismiss charges against them on a variety of crimes. The defendants were juveniles who were charged as adults.


OVERVIEW: Three assailants accosted and attempted to rob a pedestrian and defendants were arrested and charged with the crime. Another defendant was charged with sexual assault. Pursuant to the provisions of the newly enacted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127 (a), the defendants were automatically transferred to the criminal docket. They filed motions to dismiss the transfers, alleging § 46b-127 (a) was unconstitutional. When those motions were denied, an appeal was filed. The court found the statute did not deny the defendants procedural or substantive due process because the defendants had no liberty or property interest in their juvenile status. Moreover, prosecutorial discretion in whether to prosecute the defendants as adults or as juveniles was not a denial of due process, nor was it a denial of equal protection. The statute did not facially treat similarly situated individuals differently and the defendants presented no evidence, nor even an allegation, of unequal treatment in practice. Finally, the passage of the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because control of the criminal docket was not an exclusive judicial function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denials of the motions to dismiss.

Doe v. Doe


(SC 15436), (SC 15437)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 403; 710 A.2d 1297; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 98


March 20, 1997, Argued  
April 7, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the court, Stanley, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the plaintiff and a minor child in the parties' custody filed a joint appeal, and the defendant filed a separate appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which ruled that it did not have jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56 to adjudicate a child custody issue. Defendant husband and the wife had raised the minor child since birth, but only the husband was a natural parent; a surrogate mother had given birth to the child, and the wife had never formally adopted the child.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife had raised a child since birth. The husband was the child's natural father, but the natural mother had been a surrogate. The parental rights of the surrogate and her spouse had previously been terminated, but the wife had never formally adopted the child. Incident to a dissolution proceeding in a divorce between the husband and wife, the issue of the child's custody was raised. The trial court ruled that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction under § 46b-56 to adjudicate the custody issue because the child was not a "child of the marriage." On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a prompt trial with respect to custody. Specifically, the court held that while the child was not "a child of the marriage," the trial court, nevertheless, had jurisdiction under § 46b-56 to adjudicate the custody issue as between the husband, as the child's father, and the wife, as a third person asserting a claim to custody of the child. The court also held that given the undisputed facts of the case, the statutory presumption in favor of a parent over a nonparent, as afforded by § 46b-56b, had been rebutted as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling and held that it had jurisdiction to adjudicate the custody issue between the husband, as the child's natural father, and the wife, as a third person asserting a claim to custody. Furthermore, the court remanded for a trial on the custody issue and concluded that due to the undisputed facts of the case, the statutory presumption in favor of the husband had been rebutted as a matter of law.

 

55 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. City of Hartford


(SC 15754)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 206; 710 A.2d 746; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 66


October 29, 1997, Argued  
March 31, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from enforcing a traffic regulation that prohibits vehicular access to a particular street during certain time periods, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Wagner, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners alleged that the temporary closing of a road by defendant city violated the provisions of the deed conveying the road to the city, impaired the property owners' private easement of access, and constituted a taking without just compensation. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) rejected the property owners' claims and they appealed from the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted a regulation pursuant to which a street abutting the property owners' businesses was closed to vehicular traffic for three hours on weekdays. The property owners alleged that several of their tenants had lost clients and that they lost tenants and rent due to the closing. The trial court rendered judgment for the city because the property owners did not prove that they suffered damages due to the closing or that the loss of tenants and rent was due to the closing rather than the prevailing economic conditions. On appeal, the court held that (1) the language in the deed did not contemplate unrestricted vehicular access to the street so the regulation did not violate the terms of the deed, (2) the enforcement of the regulation represented a legitimate use of the city's police power to advance economic, aesthetic and safety-related goals, (3) the street closings did not interfere with the use of the property to such a degree so as to constitute a taking of the property, and (4) the property owners did not prove that they were singled out to bear an economic burden and the street closings merely posed a minor inconvenience to persons seeking access to the properties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's rejection of the property owners' claims and the entry of judgment for the city.

 

56 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Pamela B. v. Ment


(SC 15719)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 296; 709 A.2d 1089; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 79


September 30, 1997, Argued  
March 31, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of certain procedures used by the defendant commissioner of children and families regarding orders of temporary custody concerning minor children who are the subjects of neglect petitions and for an injunction requiring the named defendant to establish certain procedures for all cases in which orders of temporary custody have been issued ex parte, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the action was withdrawn as against the defendant John Rowland and where Hon. Jerry Wagner, judge trial referee, granted the motion by the named defendant et al. to strike those portions of the plaintiff's revised complaint seeking injunctive relief; thereafter, the court, L. Sullivan, J., denied the motion by the named defendant et al. to dismiss or strike the remainder of the revised complaint, and, on the granting of certification pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a, the named defendant et al. filed an expedited appeal and the plaintiff filed an expedited cross appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state government officials (officials), appealed the denial of their motion to dismiss and or strike by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut). The officials asserted that the claim of plaintiff parents was not justiciable. The parents cross-appealed the decision to strike their claim for injunctive relief, but argued that their claim for declaratory relief was properly allowed.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed suit against the officials when their child was taken into temporary custody after an allegation of neglect. The parents claimed that their rights were violated when the trial court granted this order on the officials' ex parte application without first holding a hearing. The officials filed a motion to strike the parents' complaint for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief. The trial court granted the motion to strike the claim for injunctive relief but denied the motion to strike the claim for declaratory relief. Both parties appealed. The court held that the parents' claim was justiciable. The officials were bound to act within constitutional principles, and the court, through an evidentiary proceeding could disclose whether the alleged violations could be remedied. The parents' claims were appropriate for redress through declaratory judgment because they could not effectively challenge the denial of a meaningful and timely hearing in any other way, and because there were no other viable avenues available to them. Sovereign immunity did not bar the parents' claims for injunctive relief against the officials, so the motion to strike this claim was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the officials' motion to dismiss the parents' claim for declaratory relief. The parents' claim was justiciable and they were allowed to seek declaratory relief against the officials. The court reversed the trial court's grant of the officials' motion to strike the parents' claim for injunctive relief because this claim was not barred by sovereign immunity.

 

57 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Austin


(SC 15369)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 226; 710 A.2d 732; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 91


December 5, 1997, Argued  
March 31, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the New Haven Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a) and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a) and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35, and the court affirmed the convictions. The court found that the trial court repeatedly gave a proper statement of the elements of each offense. The court held that the jury could not have been misled, in view of the entire charge and the instructional sheets that were distributed to the jury that properly listed the elements of each offense. The court held that any possible risk of jury confusion over the element of intent was eliminated by the trial court's numerous proper instructions on the elements of murder. The court found that the trial court properly informed the jury that it had to decide whether defendant was intoxicated at the time of the offense and, if so, whether that intoxication rendered him incapable of forming the intent required for the charged offenses. The court held that while the trial court used the phrase "reckless indifference manslaughter," there was no reasonable possibility that the jury could have been misled regarding the requirement of extreme indifference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and carrying a pistol without a permit. The court held that the one-to-one confrontation identification, although suggestive, was not unnecessarily so and was reliable under the circumstances. The court held that the photographic identification was also not unnecessarily suggestive because defendant's photo was not so distinctive in skin tone from the other photos.

Southeastern Conn. Reg'l Resources Recovery Auth. v. Department of Pub. Util. Control


(SC 15666)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 280; 709 A.2d 549; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 94


January 21, 1998, Argued  
March 31, 1998, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant determining that the defendant Connecticut Light and Power Company was not obligated to purchase, at a certain contracted rate, the entire surplus electricity output of a solid waste disposal plant owned and operated by the plaintiffs in excess of the plant's projected net electrical capacity, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Munro, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiffs' appeal, from which the defendant Connecticut Light and Power Company appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant power company sought review of a judgment of the trial court that sustained an appeal of plaintiff authority and companies from a ruling by defendant department that was issued in response to a request for a resolution of a payment dispute between defendant power company and plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant power company, who was required to purchase electricity from plaintiff authority and companies, challenged the trial court's judgment that sustained an appeal by plaintiffs from a ruling by defendant department that was issued in response to defendant's request for a resolution of a payment dispute. The court affirmed and found that the controlling statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-243e, required that defendant, which entered into an agreement to purchase electricity from plaintiffs, pay the same rate plaintiffs charged a municipality or municipalities for electricity. The court rejected defendant's assertion that the agreement was ambiguous because there was definitive language that established the parties' intent. The court noted that any ambiguity that defendant found was not the result of the contract, but was the result of defendant's interpretation of the agreement's language. The court found that the agreement was clear that the quantity to have been purchased by defendant was not limited to a set amount. The held that the agreement with plaintiffs required defendant to purchase the entire output of electricity provided by plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: A judgment that upheld an appeal to a decision related to a purchase agreement of electricity was affirmed because the agreement was not ambiguous, because there was no limitation on the amount purchased, because the agreement's price structure conformed to statutory requirements, and because the agreement clearly required the purchase of the total output of electricity.

Binette v. Sabo


(SC 15547)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


244 Conn. 23; 710 A.2d 688; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 57


June 4, 1997, Argued  
March 10, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, violations of the plaintiffs' civil rights under the state and federal constitutions as a result of alleged misconduct by the defendant municipal police officers, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the case was removed to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut and referred to Chief United States District Judge Peter C. Dorsey, who denied without prejudice the defendants' motion to dismiss four counts of the plaintiffs' complaint for failure to state a cause of action and certified to this court the question of law whether the plaintiffs have a cause of action for damages under the state constitution for the injuries alleged in those four counts of their complaint.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Connecticut certified an appeal on an action by plaintiff victims to recover damages for violations of their civil rights under the state and federal constitutions as a result of alleged misconduct by defendant municipal police officers.


OVERVIEW: In their claim of action, plaintiffs alleged that defendants entered their home without permission or a warrant, threatening arrest to one of the plaintiffs and striking the other on his head, causing an epileptic seizure. Plaintiffs contended that the courts should have recognized a damages remedy directly under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9. The action was removed to the lower court, which certified the question for review. The court found for plaintiffs and concluded that they had stated a damages claim directly under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9. The court did not rely on existing state law but created a new tort action not previously recognized. The court held that, in the absence of any persuasive argument or authority to the contrary, it possessed the inherent authority to create a cause of action directly under the Connecticut Constitution and held that the legislature neither prohibited an award of damages for violations of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9, nor otherwise expressed its preference for an alternative statutory or administrative remedy.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative in favor of plaintiffs, holding that, in the circumstances presented, the Connecticut Constitution gave rise to a private cause of action for money damages for violations of the state constitution.

State v. Kinchen


(SC 15791)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


243 Conn. 690; 707 A.2d 1255; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 52


December 4, 1997, Argued  
March 3, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Misdemeanor summons and complaint charging the defendant with criminal trespass in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the court, Dean, J., sua sponte, dismissed the complaint and rendered judgment thereon, and the state appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty (Connecticut), dismissing a charge against defendant for criminal trespass in the first degree, a misdemeanor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-107. The state argued the trial court lacked the authority to dismiss the charge based on its belief that a jury trial was not warranted. The court transferred the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for criminal trespass based on a police report made by his employer that defendant was seen on the employer's property after being fired because he was suspected of stealing and being told to leave the premises. Defendant pled not guilty and requested a jury trial. The trial court told the state that it was concerned about the trial court's backlog, and did not see any basis for the criminal trespass. It further stated that it would be embarrassed to put the case before a jury and unless the state reduced the charge, it would decide the matter. The state refused, and the trial court dismissed the case. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had no authority to dismiss the charge absent a constitutional infirmity or other fundamental defect in the state's exercise of its prosecutorial authority. The court ruled that the record clearly showed that the judge did not dismiss the case on the ground of evidentiary insufficiency, nor did it weigh all relevant factors under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56 to justify dismissal of the case for insufficient cause. Thus, the court held, the trial court improperly usurped the state's prosecutorial function.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the charge against defendant and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings in accordance with law.

Board of Educ. v. State Bd. of Educ.


(SC 15656)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


243 Conn. 772; 709 A.2d 510; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 48


October 31, 1997, Argued  
March 3, 1998, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant determining that the plaintiff was required to provide transportation for students attending a certain private school in the town of Stafford to that school including times when the public schools of the town were not in session, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, and tried to the court, McWeeny, J.; judgment for the defendants dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Board of Education of the Town of Stafford (Town Board) appealed the judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant State Board of Education's (State Board) decision that the Town Board was required to provide transportation, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-281, for students attending private school even when the public schools were not in session. The appeal was transferred to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The State Board held that the private school was improperly denied transportation when the public schools were closed. The court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of the State Board and found, inter alia, that (1) the underlying transportation request by defendant parents was not moot because the case involved an active controversy where the Town Board indicated a disposition to continue denying transportation; (2) the State Board could address not only the mootness decision but also the case merits because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-186 empowered the State Board to hear appeals de novo; (3) the State Board's decision resolved a contested case because legal rights were determined; (4) the plain language of § 10-281, the "same kind of transportation services," meant that the students would ride to and from school under the same safe and reliable conditions, rather than meaning that transportation should only occur when the public schools were in session; and (5) § 10-281 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I or Conn. Const. art. VII because its secular purpose was to provide safe and dependable transportation to all school children without advancing or inhibiting religion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Hines


(SC 15309)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


243 Conn. 796; 709 A.2d 522; 1998 Conn. LEXIS 55


December 10, 1997, Argued  
March 3, 1998, officially released

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder and criminal possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court improperly admitted a portion of a statement from one of the witnesses made to the police, which was consistent with a later trial testimony, regarding a telephone threat made to the victim on the morning of the murder. Defendant argued that because he neither offered a theory of recent fabrication with respect to the threat nor attempted to impeach the witness' credibility regarding the telephone call, the court improperly admitted the prior consistent statement concerning the threat. The court disagreed with defendant's argument and affirmed his convictions. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting the testimony. The court concluded that the trial court reasonably could have concluded that the prior consistent statement regarding the telephone threat was admissible for rehabilitative purposes in light of the possibility that the jury might otherwise have drawn an inference of recent fabrication of his trial testimony on that subject. Moreover, the court also found no merit in defendant's remaining assertions of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of murder and criminal possession of a firearm.

64 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Joyce


(SC 15394)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


243 Conn. 282; 705 A.2d 181; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 461


September 23, 1997, Argued  
November 25, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2597.
Writ of certiorari denied Joyce v. Connecticut, 523 U.S. 1077, 140 L. Ed. 2d 674, 118 S. Ct. 1523, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2597 (1998)
Subsequent appeal at Joyce v. State's Atty., 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 328 (Conn. App. Ct., July 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Freedman, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Joyce, 229 Conn. 10, 639 A.2d 1007, 1994 Conn. LEXIS 85 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) that convicted him of arson in the first degree. On appeal, he contended that the trial court improperly failed to suppress the results of a chemical analysis conducted pursuant to a search warrant in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV, and Conn. Const. art. I, § 7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of arson, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111(a)(4). On a prior appeal, the court concluded the state's chemical testing of defendant's burned clothing without a warrant constituted an unreasonable search in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 7, and reversed the conviction. State then applied for and obtained a search warrant to test defendant's clothing. Defendant moved to suppress the results of the test at his subsequent trial for arson, but that motion was denied. He was thereafter convicted, and sought review. On appeal, he challenged the legality of the second search. The court held that: (1) the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress, as police had an independent basis for the possession and testing of the clothing, and the underlying search warrant was supported by probable cause; (2) the trial court was not collaterally estopped from admitting evidence of insurance proceeds as a motive for defendant to commit arson; and (3) state's failure to preserve certain evidence did not deprive defendant of a fair trial in violation of his due process rights. The trial court's judgment of conviction was thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of arson was affirmed. Chemical testing of defendant's clothing for flammable chemicals did not constituted an unconstitutional search of defendant's person, as police obtained information in support of the underlying warrant from an independent source. Additionally, sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction for arson.

Iovieno v. Commissioner of Correction


(SC 15411)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 689; 699 A.2d 1003; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 298


February 21, 1997, Argued  
August 26, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Sferrazza, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, Landau and Spear, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an action in habeas corpus alleging ineffective assistance of counsel in that his attorney failed to timely file an appeal of the inmate's first habeas petition, which was dismissed as untimely pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-470(b). The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the inmate's second petition as untimely without reaching the merits. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-470(b), which set a 10-day limitation period in which a petition for certification to appeal from a judgment of a habeas court must have been filed, did not limit the subject matter jurisdiction of the habeas court, but merely defined the scope of review. The court overturned the appellate court's ruling and held that the inmate's habeas petition was not time-barred by § 52-470(b). In so holding, the court found that 1) the legislature intended the language of § 52-470(b) to define the scope of review and not to limit the jurisdiction of the appellate court; 2) a habeas writ was a proper remedy for an ineffective assistance of habeas counsel claim; and the remedy extended to claims alleging ineffective assistance of appellate habeas counsel; 3) the inmate properly established that his counsel's failure to timely file his first habeas petition fell below the objective standard of reasonableness; and 4) the inmate was not required to establish actual prejudice or the likely success of his petition for certification on appeal, as he was deprived of the opportunity to seek review of a habeas judgment solely due to ineffective counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to that court with the direction to reverse the judgment of the second habeas court and to remand the case to the first habeas court for consideration of the merits of the inmate's petition for certification to appeal from the judgment on his first habeas petition.

Miller v. Commissioner of Correction


(15421)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 745; 700 A.2d 1108; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 322


March 25, 1997, Argued  
August 26, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, and tried to the court, Bishop, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent commissioner of corrections sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which granted petitioner inmate's writ of habeas corpus and granted his request for a new trial. Petitioner was charged and convicted with two counts of assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate was convicted of two counts of assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1). Petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus and contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions. Petitioner further contended that he was innocent. The trial court granted petitioner's writ and his request for a new trial. Respondent commissioner of corrections sought review. The court held that the proper standard for evaluating petitioner's claim of actual innocence was twofold: petitioner must first have established by clear and convincing evidence that, taking into account all of the evidence, he was actually innocent of the crime, and second, petitioner must have established that, after considering all of the evidence, no reasonable fact finder would have found him guilty. The court held that the clear and convincing standard required an exceedingly persuasive case that petitioner was actually innocent. The court held that substantial evidence supported the finding by the habeas corpus that petitioner established his innocence by clear and convincing evidence. The court affirmed a judgment of the habeas corpus court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the habeas corpus court, which granted petitioner inmate's writ of habeas corpus against respondent commissioner of corrections and granted petitioner's request for a new trial. The court held that petitioner established by clear and convincing evidence that he was innocent and that no reasonable fact finder would have found him guilty.

State v. Coleman


(15468)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 523; 700 A.2d 14; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 274


March 26, 1997, Argued  
August 19, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, two counts of the crime of burglary in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of unlawful restraint in the first degree and robbery in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Fracasse, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Fracasse, J.; judgment of guilty of four counts of sexual assault in the first degree and of one count each of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree as a lesser included offense, unlawful restraint in the first degree and robbery in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Spear and Hennessy, Js., which remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings on the defendant's motion to dismiss; on remand, the court Fracasse, J., again denied the defendant's motion to dismiss, and the defendant filed an amended appeal to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Spear and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting [***2] of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of four counts of sexual assault in the first degree, one count each of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, and robbery in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of sexual assault in the first degree, one count each of burglary in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, and robbery in the third degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(2), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-102, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a095(a), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136(a), and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-133. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, and defendant sought review. Defendant had previously successfully attacked his plea agreement and a new trial was ordered. The court held that the trial court improperly determined that second degree burglary was a lesser included offense of first degree burglary and vacated that conviction. The court held that neither the equal protection clause nor the double jeopardy provision imposed an absolute bar to a harsher sentence upon reconviction. The court held that the trial court had not acted with vindictiveness in imposing a harsher sentence upon reconviction for the purpose of punishing defendant for exercising his rights. The court affirmed as modified judgments of the lower courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified judgments of the trial courts, which convicted defendant of sexual assault, burglary in the first and second degree, unlawful restraint, and robbery. The court held that burglary in the second degree was not a lesser included offense of first degree burglary. The court held that neither the equal protection clause nor the double jeopardy clause imposed an absolute bar to a harsher sentence upon reconviction.

Worsham v. Greifenberger


(SC 15491)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 432; 698 A.2d 867; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 271


March 27, 1997, Argued  
August 12, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident allegedly caused by the negligence of the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Karazin, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to defendants, a driver and his employer, in the employee's negligence action to recover for personal injuries he sustained on the grounds that the employee's action had abated.


OVERVIEW: The employee received workers' compensation benefits after he was involved in an automobile accident while driving the employer's vehicle. The employer sued defendants in order to recover the workers' compensation benefits that it paid to the employee. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-293 (1997), the employer notified the employee of the initiation of the lawsuit, however, the employee was not informed that his action against defendants would abate if he failed to intervene within 30 days. The employee then filed his negligence action against defendants more than 30 days after receiving the notice. Defendants' motion for summary judgment on grounds that the employee's action had abated was granted. In reversing the judgment, the court held that the notice was constitutionally inadequate under the federal Due Process Clause to support a complete abatement of his cause of action because it failed to notify the employee of the consequences of his failure to intervene in the action within 30 days of the notice. Therefore, the abatement of his claim based upon his failure to intervene in a timely fashion, unconstitutionally deprived him of his property interest in his legal claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which had granted summary judgment for defendant, and it remanded the case for further proceedings. The court specifically delineated a new procedure to bring the notice provisions of the abatement statute in compliance with the federal due process clause.

 

69 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Solek


(SC 15595)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 409; 699 A.2d 931; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 270


May 27, 1997, Argued  
August 12, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, sexual assault in the first degree and sexual assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hartmere, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the capital felony count, and the state, on the granting of certification pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a, filed an expedited appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with capital murder in connection with a sexual assault that resulted in the death of the victim. The Superior Court (Connecticut) granted defendant's motion to dismiss a capital felony count. The state, on the granting of certification pursuant to Con. Gent. Stat. § 52-265a, filed an expedited appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man were charged with killing a woman in the course of a sexual assault. Defendant objected to a capital felony count on the ground it would have caused confusion for a jury because the murder count alleged that defendant had aided the other perpetrator to commit the murder. The trial court dismissed that count. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the dismissed count provided defendant with constitutionally adequate notice of the charge sufficient to enable the him to prepare a defense, (2) the legislature intended the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(7) to encompass the situation where a defendant aided another in killing a victim during a sexual assault, (3) defendant could be convicted of a substantive offense, through the use of accessory principles even though he had not committed the substantive offense because the accessory statute merely provided an alternate means for the substantive crime to be committed, (4) an early probable cause determination was not determinative of the offenses defendant could have been convicted of, (5) defendant could be convicted as an accessory even though he was charged only as a principal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of a capital murder count against defendant because the dismissed count adequately apprised defendant of the charge against him and there was no substantive reason for confusion concerning his role as either an accessory or a principle. Furthermore, preliminary determinations were not binding on the final outcome of the case.

State v. McIntyre


(SC 15352)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 318; 699 A.2d 911; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 328


June 4, 1997, Argued  
August 5, 1997, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied McEntyre v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 554 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, conspiracy to commit murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and carrying a pistol without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and carrying a pistol without a permit. On appeal, defendant alleged that (1) he was deprived of due process because the state failed to disclose certain exculpatory evidence; (2) the trial court improperly admitted certain statements into evidence; (3) the trial court abused its discretion when it precluded the testimony of certain alibi witnesses; and (4) the evidence was not sufficient to sustain his conviction for carrying a pistol without a permit. Upon review, the court reversed defendant's conviction for carrying a pistol without a permit because the state conceded that the evidence against defendant was insufficient. The court affirmed defendant's remaining convictions. The court recognized that the State might not have disclosed certain exculpatory evidence. However, the court found that defendant failed to show the materiality of the State's nondisclosure. The court further held that the trial court's admission of two improper statements was harmless. The court also held that the trial court had the authority to preclude the testimony of alibi witnesses because defendant failed to comply with discovery rules.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for carrying a pistol without a permit and directed the trial court to enter a judgment of acquittal on that count. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and conspiracy to commit murder.

State v. Wilchinski


(SC 15598)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 211; 700 A.2d 1; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 242


May 30, 1997, Argued  
July 29, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Information charging the defendant with the crime of negligent storage of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, where the court, Dunnell, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court In the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), Geographical Area Number 12, for negligent storage of a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217a, alleging that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded nolo contendre to an information charging him with one count of criminally negligent storage of a fire arm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217a, with reservation of right to appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the statute had a core meaning that was sufficiently clear to satisfy the due process requirements of the state and federal constitutions. The terms "container" and "secure" were given meaningful substance by their context within the framework of the statute as a whole. The inclusion of a reasonable person standard in the statute was not impermissibly vague. The statute was not vague as applied to defendant's conduct as a fact finder could reasonable find that he did not use an appropriate physical impediment to restrict his children's access to the gun. Because defendant did not demonstrate that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217a was vague as applied to his conduct, he could not mount a facial challenge to the statute. The acts of defendant's son did not constitute an efficient intervening cause for the purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. 53a-217a.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for negligent storage of a firearm was affirmed on the grounds that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and that defendant's actions came well within the statute's core meaning.

Connecticut Nat'l Bank v. Giacomi


(SC 15539)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


242 Conn. 17; 699 A.2d 101; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 235


January 14, 1997, Argued  
July 22, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Action to recover the balances due on promissory notes executed by the defendants, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where all of the defendants except Valerie S. DePastino filed counterclaims, and where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, Blue, J.; judgments for the defendants on the complaints and for the plaintiff on the counterclaims, from which the plaintiff appealed; this court reversed the trial court's judgments and remanded the cases to that court for further proceedings; on remand, the court, Blue, J., rendered judgments for the defendants on the complaints, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied its prayer for relief against defendant makers of a promissory note.


OVERVIEW: The bank brought separate actions, as payee, against the makers of promissory notes that were payable on demand. The bank sought to recover the balances due on promissory notes executed by the makers. The makers were among a group of investors in a now defunct partnership. The makers did not deny that they had executed the notes or that demand had properly been made; they alleged that the special defense under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36-498(g) that the promissory notes were unenforceable as contracts in violation of Connecticut Uniform Securities Act (CUSA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36-470 et. seq. (1993). The trial court found that the bank was barred from pursuing these actions because it violated the provisions of CUSA in that the bank acted as an agent of the seller who perpetrated the fraud. On appeal, the court rejected the trial court's theory that the bank, as a corporate entity, was an agent and held that only a natural person could be an agent under CUSA for a violation under § 36-498(c).


OUTCOME: The judgment relieving certain makers of liability to the bank on the note was affirmed because the bank's conduct constituted a violation under CUSA. The court reversed the judgment against the bank with respect to the makers who did not establish that the bank's conduct violated CUSA and remanded with respect to those makers to determine damages.
