State v. Colvin


(SC 15525)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


241 Conn. 650; 697 A.2d 1122; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 199


April 24, 1997, Argued  
July 15, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a housing project, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Spada, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court, Miano, J., rendered judgment dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Spear and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut challenged a decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed the superior court's suppression of drugs seized from defendant's vehicle. The seizure occurred after police officers had ordered defendant to accompany them to his vehicle. One of the officers then looked through the window and observed the bag in plain view. Defendant argued that his arrest was illegal and that the evidence was inadmissible.


OVERVIEW: The police had observed defendant for 25 minutes sitting 200 feet from his car, but had not witnessed any sale of narcotics or act giving the appearance of a sale when they approached him and ordered him to accompany them to his vehicle. The parties assumed on appeal that the police detained defendant illegally. The court noted that not all evidence that would not have been discovered but for the illegal action of law enforcement officials was fruit of the poisonous tree. The court stated that the first issue was whether the allegedly tainted evidence was in some sense the product of illegal government activity. The court determined that the trial court had heard no evidence supporting the conclusion that the discovery of the narcotics was the product of the unlawful arrest. The court concluded that the police had a perfect right to be where they were and to observe the cocaine notwithstanding the wrongful detention. Because there was no evidence indicating a causal connection between the arrest and the discovery of the drugs, the court ruled the evidence should not have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to that court with direction to remand the case to the trial court with direction to deny the motion to suppress and to reinstate the information and proceed according to law.

Great Country Bank v. Pastore

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

Donald W. Celotto, judge trial referee, who granted the motion filed by Centerbank to be substituted as plaintiff; thereafter, the court granted the substitute plaintiff's motion to strike certain special defenses filed by the named defendant et al., and its motion for summary judgment; subsequently, the court granted the substitute plaintiff's motion for strict foreclosure and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon, and the named defendant et al. appealed; this court thereafter granted the motion filed by Wilshire Funding Corporation to be substituted as plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank brought an action to foreclose mortgages on certain real property. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted the bank's motions to strike certain special defenses, for summary judgment, and for strict foreclosure. OVERVIEW: The mortgagors defaulted on their obligation to pay taxes. The court held that: (1) the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction because the clerk's failure to note the referral in the court file did not deprive the referee of authority to hear the case, and the blanket referral order issued before the expiration of the referee's term provided authority to preside because there was no gap in time between the expiration of the referee's term and his reappointment; (2) the mortgagors waived the right to appeal the granting of the motion to strike because three of the six new special defenses were substantively the same as the original three special defenses but had been rewritten to correct deficiencies; (3) the affidavit alleging that certain sums paid into a lockbox had not been accounted for by the bank in determining whether the mortgagors were in default was insufficient to defeat the motion for summary judgment because it was inadmissible hearsay as the affiant's knowledge was based upon communications with the tenants; and (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the mortgagors a continuance under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 382.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of strict foreclosure in favor of the bank.

Hall v. Gilbert & Bennett Mfg. Co.


(SC 15608)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


241 Conn. 282; 695 A.2d 1051; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 171


March 27, 1997, Argued  
June 3, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district determining that the commissioner had no jurisdiction to determine whether the plaintiff suffered from a previous disability, brought to the compensation review board, which reversed the commissioner's decision and remanded the matter for a hearing on the issue of transfer, and the defendant second injury fund appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant second injury fund sought review of a decision of the Connecticut Workers' Compensation Review Board (board), which reversed the trial commissioner's decision that he had no jurisdiction to entertain an insurer's request that a claim be transferred to appellant pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349c. The board remanded the matter for a hearing on the issue of transfer.


OVERVIEW: Appellee workers' compensation insurer sought to transfer to appellant second injury fund the claim of an employee who suffered permanent total disability due to the combination of a new injury with preexisting permanent conditions. The trial commissioner denied the request on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349c required a panel of three physicians to decide the matter. The workers' compensation review board (board) held that § 31-349c applied prospectively only and reversed. Appellant sought review and contended that the legislature intended § 31-349c to apply retroactively to cases in which the claimant's second injury predated the effective date of the statute. The court agreed and held that the evidence that the legislature intended the statute to apply retroactively was sufficient to rebut the presumption of prospective application. Appellee asserted constitutional challenges to § 31-349c, but the court concluded that the arguments were not ripe for review. The court reversed the decision of the board and remanded the case to the board with direction to remand it to the commissioner for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the workers' compensation review board and remanded the case to the board for remand to the trial commissioner for further proceedings. The court held that a statute requiring the issue to be decided by a panel of three physicians applied retroactively to the claimant's case.

Northeast Sav., F.A. v. Hintlian


(SC 15536)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


241 Conn. 269; 696 A.2d 315; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 159


January 16, 1997, Argued  
June 3, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property owned by the named defendant et al., and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the named defendant et al. filed a counterclaim; thereafter, the defendants were defaulted and the matter was referred to Hon. Robert Satter, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment of foreclosure by sale; subsequently, the court denied the motion to open the judgment filed by the named defendant et al., and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individual sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which rendered judgment of foreclosure by sale and denied a motion to open the judgment in an action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property owned by the individual, and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue raised by this appeal was whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-25, which established procedures relative to the appraisal of property for which a judgment of foreclosure by sale had been rendered, violated the due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The court held that because the filing procedure mandated by § 49-25 afforded the individual adequate notice of the relevant appraisal, the procedure did not run afoul of constitutional requirements. The court also held that because fundamental fairness required that an evidentiary hearing be allowed upon a proper request, a foreclosure court necessarily had the inherent equitable power under § 49-25 to grant such a request. The court therefore concluded that because the individual would be afforded an evidentiary hearing at which he could challenge the court-ordered appraisal prior to any action by the trial court on plaintiff bank's motion to approve the sale of the property, the individual's due process claim had to fail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

State v. Porter


(SC 15363)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


241 Conn. 57; 698 A.2d 739; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 155


September 24, 1996, Argued  
May 20, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Certiorari Denied April 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2310.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Parker, J., denied the defendant's motion to admit into evidence the results of his polygraph examination; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Parker, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of arson in the first degree; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a new trial, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Landau and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Connecticut), which denied his motion to admit into evidence the results of his polygraph examination.


OVERVIEW: The defendant sought to have evidence of the results of his polygraph test admitted during his trial for arson. The trial court ruled that polygraph evidence was inadmissible and denied the defendant's motion. The intermediate appellate court affirmed that ruling. The court reviewed the Daubert test for admissibility of scientific evidence and stated that scientific tests should conform to some measure of general acceptance in the scientific world. The court concluded that Connecticut's judges served a gatekeeping function with regard to scientific evidence and that there had to be some scientific validity involved in the test before it might be admitted. With polygraph examinations, the court stated there is little probative value to the test and the accuracy of the test could readily be questioned. The defendant's right to compulsory process was not impinged by the court's refusal to admit the polygraph evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the intermediate appellate court's ruling which affirmed the denial of the defendant's motion to admit the results of his polygraph test.

State v. Matos


(15433)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 743; 694 A.2d 775; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 128


February 19, 1997, Argued  
May 6, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, assault in the first degree and criminal use of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Miano, J., denied with prejudice the defendant's application for youthful offender status; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Barall, J.; verdict of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, assault in the first degree and criminal use of a firearm; subsequently, the court, Barall, J., dismissed the criminal use of a firearm count and rendered judgment in accordance with the remainder of the verdict, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder, assault in the first degree, and criminal use of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, assault in the first degree, and criminal use of a firearm. He appealed from his conviction, arguing that his rights to due process and equal protection were violated. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's substantive due process rights were not violated. The legislature's decision to grant preverdict benefits and, therefore, to determine youthful offender status before trial, was rational. The court noted that a defendant who was convicted of a lesser included crime, but was acquitted of the class A felony that statutorily deprived him of youthful offender status, was unable to apply for postverdict benefits. The court held that such a result did not violate defendant's substantive due process rights. Also, it was rational for the legislature to exclude from youthful offender eligibility those defendants charged with murder. The youthful offender statutes did not violate defendant's right to equal protection because a rational basis existed for the classification. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding evidence proffered by defendant on the basis of its irrelevance to defendant's self-defense claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, assault in the first degree, and criminal use of a firearm. The court held that defendant's substantive due process and equal protection rights were not violated by youthful offender statutes. The court noted that it was rational for the legislature to exclude from youthful offender eligibility those defendants charged with murder.

State v. Payne


(15395)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 766; 695 A.2d 525; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 127


December 6, 1996, Argued  
May 6, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of risk of injury to a child and with two counts of the crime of coercion, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of risk of injury to a child and coercion, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, Landau and Schaller, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirming the conviction for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 (1993), and misdemeanor coercion in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-192.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of misdemeanor coercion, violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-192, and risk of injury to a child, violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 (1993), after threatening children in order to extract urine samples from them. In the appeal of defendant's conviction for risk of injury to a child, the court concluded, based on principles of statutory interpretation and definitions of the term "health," that the first part of § 53-21 encompassed injury to the child's mental health. The plain language of the first part of the section indicated the legislature's understanding that the broad class of intentional conduct that could harm a child included mental, as well as physical health. No physical contact by the defendant was required for conviction. The court further held that § 53-21, as interpreted to include injury to a child's mental health, was not unconstitutionally vague. A person of ordinary intelligence would know that health in the first part of the section would include mental health, and that the person would have fair warning that using threats to force a child to publicly urinate in a cup would constitute a violation of the section.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the conviction of defendant for risk of injury to a child and misdemeanor coercion.

Cislo v. City of Shelton


(15451)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 590; 692 A.2d 1255; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 130


January 21, 1997, Argued  
April 29, 1997, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for indemnification for, inter alia, attorney's fees incurred by the plaintiff in defense of a criminal action filed against him while he was a police officer for the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the court, Rush, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the court, Rush, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to open the judgment and the plaintiff filed an amended appeal to the Appellate Court, Heiman and Schaller, Js., with Lavery, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant officer sought review of the order of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) that affirmed the summary judgment of the trial court in favor of appellee City of Shelton. The officer sought indemnification for attorney's fees incurred in defense of a criminal action against him under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-39a. The appellate court concluded that the provisions of § 54-142a (c) did not effectuate a dismissal for purposes of § 53-39a.


OVERVIEW: The officer was arrested and charged with the sexual assault of a police informant. The assistant state's attorney entered a nolle prosequi (nolle) in the criminal action against the officer because the informant had disappeared. The officer's counsel objected to the entry of the nolle and moved to dismiss the case. The trial court declined to dismiss the case and accepted the entry of the nolle pursuant to § 54-56b. The officer brought the action against the city under § 53-39a, seeking indemnification for economic losses he incurred while defending the criminal charges against him. The trial court determined that the officer was not entitled to relief because § 53-39a provides for indemnification only if the criminal charges were dismissed or the officer was found not guilty. Here, the criminal action against the officer was terminated by the entry of a nolle. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court concluded that the entry of a nolle followed by the elapse of the statutory period of 13 months, which resulted in the mandatory erasure of the pertinent records pursuant to § 54-142a(c), constituted a dismissal for purposes of § 53-39a.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to that court with the direction to reverse the summary judgment in favor of the officer, and to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings according to law.

82 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Waz


(15471)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 365; 692 A.2d 1217; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 80


November 5, 1996, Argued  
April 15, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of four ounces or more of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, where the court, Cofield, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of possession of four ounces or more of marijuana; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence, and subsequently, entered a judgment of guilty after a conditional plea of nolo contendere was presented to the trial court on possession of narcotics charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a conditional plea of nolo contendere to possession of more than four ounces of marijuana, and the trial court entered a judgment thereon. The sole issue on appeal was whether Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7 prohibited the police from subjecting a mail parcel in the possession of the United States Postal Service to a canine sniff examination by a trained narcotics detection dog based upon a reasonable and articulable suspicion that the mail contained illegal drugs. The trial court had denied defendant's motion to suppress on this issue. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion. The state constitution required no more than a showing that the investigating officers had a reasonable and articulable suspicion that the parcel contained contraband, and the trial court found that the investigating officers had so shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. The court found that the investigating officer had shown reasonable and articulable suspicion that a parcel belonging to defendant contained contraband.

 

83 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Chotkowski v. State


(15399)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 246; 690 A.2d 368; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 56


November 1, 1996, Argued  
March 18, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Action to recover damages for breach of an employment contract, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, Fineberg, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.  [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor worked for appellee state. When his employment ended, the doctor filed an action under 1991 Conn. Acts 91-8 (Spec. Sess.) for breach of express and implied contract. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) issued judgment for the state. The doctor appealed. The appeal was transferred under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 4023 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: A doctor filed a claim for lost wages with the commissioner under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-142, 4-148 after his employment with the state ended and was granted permission to sue. The doctor filed an action against the state under 1991 Conn. Acts 91-8 (Spec. Sess.) based on breach of contract and promissory estoppel theories. The trial court issued judgment for the state. The doctor appealed and asserted that the trial court improperly decided that he failed to show that he was entitled to relief. The state asserted that the trial court lacked jurisdiction, 91-8 violated Conn. Const. art. first, § 1, and the commissioner lacked authority over the request to sue. The court held that the trial court properly rejected the state's challenge to 1991 Conn. Acts 91-8 (Spec. Sess.) because 91-8 served a legitimate public purpose, doctor's request to sue was not barred because his claims were not excepted from the commissioner's jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. 4-142, consideration of the claims by the commissioner was not barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. 4-148(c), and trial court's judgment was proper because the doctor was entitled to statutory and not contractual employment rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the state was affirmed.

In re Flanagan


(15419)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


240 Conn. 157; 690 A.2d 865; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 59


December 11, 1996, Argued  
March 18, 1997, officially released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5397.


PRIOR HISTORY: (PROCEDURAL HISTORY) Appeal to this court from a decision of the judicial review council to censure publicly the respondent for certain conduct resulting in violations of two of the canons of the Code of Judicial Conduct.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of a decision of appellee judicial review council, which publicly censured him for violations of canons 1 and 2A of the Connecticut Code of Judicial Conduct on the basis that he had sex with a married court reporter who was assigned to his court.


OVERVIEW: The judge contended that the review council improperly charged him with consensual sexual misconduct on the basis of evidence adduced at his probable cause hearing even though the court reporter's written complaint had been limited to forced or coerced sexual misconduct. The court found that the findings of the review council were proper. The court held that the review council had authority to make a finding of probable cause based upon improper consensual sex between the judge and the court reporter even though improper consensual sex was not specifically alleged in the complaint that initiated the investigation. The court found that such authority existed because the judge explicitly waived any claim that the review council lacked probable cause and because the judge was not required to be given notice, during the investigatory stage of the proceedings against him, of each of the precise charges upon which he may have been sanctioned. The court further held that the review council properly found that the judge had violated the canons of the state judicial conduct code even though no expert testimony was shown to support that conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the judicial review council because the court reporter's allegations were sufficient to support the ultimate finding of probable cause.

Blakeslee Arpaia Chapman, Inc. v. EI Constructors


(15381)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 708; 687 A.2d 506; 1997 Conn. LEXIS 11


June 4, 1996, Argued  
January 21, 1997, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of a construction subcontract, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the named defendant was defaulted for failure to appear; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, R. Walsh, J., as against the remaining defendants; judgment in part for the plaintiff against the named defendant et al., from which the defendant Aetna Insurance Company appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) rendered judgment in favor of plaintiff subcontractor in its action for breach of a subcontract against defendants contractor, municipality, and surety. The subcontractor and surety appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contractor defaulted on a contract for the construction of a water treatment plant. The trial court awarded damages to the subcontractor. On appeal, the court declined to determine the enforceability of a "pay-when-paid" clause because the municipality paid the contractor all sums that were due it. The court held that the subcontractor was entitled to recover lost profits only for work actually performed. The court further held that the subcontractor was entitled to damages for labor and material items, for the cost of standby labor, and for the liquidation value of the steel. The court determined that the subcontractor was not entitled to recovery for the extra costs of subsurface conditions because the subcontractor should have anticipated and made allowance for the conditions. The court held that the subcontractor's unified offer of judgment was properly made under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a. Therefore, the court concluded that the trial court properly awarded offer of judgment interest. Lastly, the court held that statutes challenged by the surety did not violate the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment in favor of the subcontractor in its action against the contractor, the municipality, and the surety, was affirmed.

Slimp v. Department of Liquor Control


(15454)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 599; 687 A.2d 123; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 488


November 6, 1996, Argued  
December 31, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the named defendant's suspension of the plaintiffs' out-of-state shipper's permit for beer as a result of the plaintiffs' payment to certain of their Connecticut distributors of promotional allowances based on retail sales, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Hodgson, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an out-of-state shipper and a liquor permittee, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant Connecticut Department of Liquor Control's decision that suspended plaintiffs' beer shipment permit for violations of the Liquor Control Act.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, plaintiffs contended that the trial court improperly concluded that: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-6-A29(f) was a valid exercise of the department's regulatory authority because its terms could be interpreted so as to be consistent with the provisions of the Liquor Control Act; (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-63(c) did not violate the Sherman Antitrust Act and thus, did not implicate the Supremacy Clause; and (3) the imposition of a 400-day suspension of the out-of-state shipper's permit was not an abuse of the department's administrative discretion. The court agreed with the trial court on all issues except the finding that plaintiffs had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 30-63(c). Thus, the matter regarding the constitutionality of § 30-63(c) was not reviewed. The court found that § 30-6-A29(f) was a valid exercise of the department's regulatory authority because federal law did not permit plaintiffs' promotional scheme which was the basis for the suspension of their license. Furthermore, the 400-day suspension was not reversible by the court because the suspension of beer permits was primarily an administrative function in the exercise of an executive power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court regarding all issues, except that the court determined that plaintiffs lacked standing on the challenge the constitutionality of the department regulation that was at issue.

State v. Synakorn


(15265)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 427; 685 A.2d 1123; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 459


November 7, 1996, Argued  
December 10, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, possession of marijuana with intent to sell, and possession of cocaine with intent to sell within 1000 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), that convicted him of possession with intent to sell at least one-half gram of cocaine in free-base form. The crime was a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a). Defendant was also convicted of possession of marijuana. On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that § 21a-278(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 21a-278(a) provided for a minimum prison term of not less than five years and not more than 20 years and a maximum term of life imprisonment for sale of an aggregate weight of one ounce or more of cocaine or an aggregate weight of one-half gram or more of cocaine in a free-base form. Defendant contended that this violated the equal protection for the law as there was no rational basis for providing the same penalty for possession of a half a gram of free-based cocaine as the penalty for possession of one ounce of cocaine in powder form. The court ruled that defendant had waived his equal-protection claim because the claim was not raised before trial by way of a motion to dismiss the information; Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Sup. Ct. §§ 810, 815 required that a claim that the law defining the offense charged was unconstitutional be raised by a motion to dismiss the information. The exception was that where there was a demonstration of good cause for such a failure a court could grant relief from the waiver. This exception did not apply to the case sub judice.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Castagno v. Wholean


(15409)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 336; 684 A.2d 1181; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 438



November 26, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Action by the plaintiff maternal grandparents seeking visitation rights with the defendants' minor children, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Higgins, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents brought suit against defendant parents, seeking visitation rights with their minor grandchildren. Parents brought a motion to dismiss, which the trial court granted. Grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that unless the family unit had been disrupted by death or de facto separation, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. Grandparents argued that the trial court misconstrued § 46b-59 to contain threshold requirements not expressed in the plain language of the statute. The court began its analysis by concluding that grandparents' reading of the statute would have allowed any person to petition a trial court for visitation rights, no matter how remote his or her connection was to the child. The court also noted that at common law, grandparents had no right to visitation. After studying the rules of statutory construction and examining the legislative record, the court concluded that the legislature intended § 46b-59 to afford the trial court jurisdiction to entertain a petition for visitation only when the minor child's family life had been disrupted. Grandparents failed to allege such in their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of grandparents' petition for visitation.

 

91 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Natural Gas Corp. v. Miller


(15474)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 313; 684 A.2d 1173; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 440



November 26, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Petition for the appointment of a receiver of rents, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, O'Neill, J.; judgment for the plaintiff granting the petition, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which appointed a receiver of rents and entered a lien against the owners' property in favor of appellee gas company. On appeal, the action was transferred to the Supreme Court of Connecticut pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 4023 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: The company supplied gas and gas heating system services to the property owners' multi unit apartment building. The owners had fallen into arrears on their account and as a result the company filed a petition for the appointment of a receiver of rents pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-262f. The trial court granted the petition and appointed a receiver and a lien was entered against the owner's property in the amount of the unpaid utility charges. On appeal, the court concluded that the determination of the amount that the owners owed at the § 16-262f proceeding did not preclude the owners from fully litigating whatever counterclaims they may have had against the company at a later time and in a separate forum. Accordingly, the court held that a § 16-262f hearing did not impinge on the owners' procedural due process rights. The owners were not permitted to litigate their counterclaims during the receivership hearing because it would violate the statute, which limited the hearings to a finding of the amount of arrearage. Thus, the doctrine of res judicata could not be invoked to preclude the owners from litigating their counterclaims against the company in a later proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the lower court, which appointed a receiver of rents and a lien on the owners' property on behalf of the gas company.

State v. Rodriguez


(15339)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


239 Conn. 235; 684 A.2d 1165; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 434


September 26, 1996, Argued  
November 12, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of robbery in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, and with one count each of the crimes of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree and larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Stanley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Heiman and Hennessy, Js., with Schaller, J., dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which reversed defendant's convictions for two counts each of kidnapping and robbery in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, and one count each of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts each of kidnapping and robbery in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, and one count each of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree. Upon review the appellate court reversed the convictions, and upon further review, the court reversed the appellate court. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress because a police officer who stopped defendant had probable cause to believe that defendant had committed a robbery. The court held that the probable cause arose from grounds entirely independent of a search of defendant's pockets because the police officer initially stopped defendant for reckless use of a highway by a pedestrian, and then realized that he fit the description of a robbery suspect. The court held that there were two independent and simultaneous investigations occurring pertaining to the activities of defendant on the night of the robbery, and that the robbery investigation proceeded from beginning to end without being influenced by search of his pockets.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment which had reversed defendant's convictions for two counts each of kidnapping and robbery in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, and one count each of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree.

State v. Harrell


(15238)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


238 Conn. 828; 681 A.2d 944; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 310


April 25, 1996, Argued  
August 13, 1996, Officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony and arson in the first degree, and with two counts of the crime of arson murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Corrigan, J., following a hearing, determined that there was no probable cause for the charge of capital felony, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed; thereafter, the court, Miano, J., dismissed the charge of capital felony, and the state, on the granting of permission, filed an amended appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with a capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b (8), arson in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111, and with arson murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54d. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) found that there was no probable cause for the charge of capital felony and dismissed the capital felony charge. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant stemmed from his role in the arson of an apartment that resulted in the death of two people. After a probable cause hearing, the trial court found that probable cause existed to support the arson murder charge, but that as a matter of law, only an intentional murder could be a predicate murder to a capital felony murder charge under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b. The state argued that the term "murder" in the capital felony statute was a generic term that broadly and unambiguously referred to alternate methods for committing the crime of murder, and thus, encompassed unintentional as well as intentional murder. Defendant argued that the term "murder" unambiguously was limited to homicide in its most aggravated form, namely, intentional murder, and alternatively, that the term "murder" was ambiguous. Upon review, the supreme court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because it was not apparent that the legislature unambiguously intended both intentional and unintentional murder to fall within the meaning of the term "murder" in the capital felony statute. The ambiguity of the term was construed in favor of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that dismissed the capital felony charge against defendant.

State v. Dyson


(15185)

238 Conn. 784; 680 A.2d 1306; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 316

96 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Washington v. Meachum


(15281)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


238 Conn. 692; 680 A.2d 262; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 311


March 26, 1996, Argued  
August 6, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action for declaratory and injunctive relief prohibiting the defendant from, inter alia, implementing and enforcing certain state agency regulations regarding the monitoring and recording of prison inmates' telephone conversations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the court, Blue, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiffs and in part for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendant cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates challenged the judgement of the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which upheld state agency regulations on the monitoring and recording of inmates' collect telephone conversations and the monitoring of their outgoing mail. Appellee corrections commissioner filed a cross-appeal from the judgement that inmates be given extended telephone privileges to confer with their attorneys.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Agencies Regs. §§ 18-81-28 through 18-81-51 permitted the monitoring and recording of inmates' personal collect telephone calls and outgoing mail. A class of inmates sought a declaratory judgement against the corrections commissioner to stop the implementation and enforcement of the regulations. They claimed the regulations violated the eavesdropping statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-187 through 53a-189, the wiretapping statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 54-41a through 54-41t, and their constitutional rights. The trial court held there were no statutory or Constitutional violations but ordered extended telephone access between inmates and their attorneys and that such conversations were not to be listened to by prison officials. Both sides filed appeals. The court held that the regulations did not violate the statutes because the inmates gave permission for the collect calls to be monitored. The extended telephone access was not required in order for inmates to have reasonable access to the courts or assistance of counsel. The inmates did have an expectation of privacy in their telephone conversations with their attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with regard to the plaintiffs' personal collect calls and with regard to the review of the plaintiffs' outgoing mail. The court reversed the judgement expanding attorney-client telephone access, but affirmed the judgement that inmates were entitled to privacy in those telephone calls.

 

97 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Webb


(14409)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


238 Conn. 389; 680 A.2d 147; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 301


December 1, 1995, Argued  
July 30, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information, in six counts, charging the defendant with the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, kidnapping in the first degree, criminal attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found the existence of aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and imposed the death penalty on the first three counts and terms of imprisonment on the remaining counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital felony, murder, kidnapping in the first degree, and related offenses after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut). A death sentence was imposed based upon a special verdict of the same jury pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a. Defendant appealed the conviction and death sentence on grounds of alleged errors in the guilt and sentencing phases of trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appeal included challenges to the constitutionality of the capital sentencing statute under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-46a, 53a-46b(b)(3), providing for proportionality review. On appeal, the court held (1) the death penalty statute did not facially violate the Due Process Clauses of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 9. (2) The trial court did not deny defendant the right to counsel, the conduct of jury voir dire was proper, and the trial court did not err in failing to recuse itself. (3) The bifurcated conviction and sentencing procedures for capital felonies did not violate defendant's right to an impartial jury as guaranteed by the state constitution. (4) Although the trial court improperly instructed the jury concerning the statutory aggravating factor for especially heinous, cruel, or depraved behavior, the error was harmless. (5) Defendant was permitted on remand to challenge the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-100 requiring execution by lethal injection because defendant's sentence was for death by electrocution. And (6) the death sentence imposed on defendant was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the death sentence imposed on defendant, except that the case was remanded for the trial court to consider defendant's claim that death by lethal injection constituted cruel and unusual punishment under the state constitution.

 

98 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


First Fed. Bank v. Whitney Dev. Corp.


(15377)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


237 Conn. 679; 677 A.2d 1363; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 235


May 1, 1996, Argued  
July 9, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where Hon. Donald W. Celotto, state trial referee, granted the motion filed by Berkeley Federal Bank and Trust, FSB, to be substituted as party plaintiff; thereafter, the matter was referred to Hon. Anthony V. DeMayo, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment of strict foreclosure in favor of the substitute plaintiff; subsequently, Hon. Donald W. Celotto, state trial referee, granted in part the motion to open the judgment filed by the defendant Carmel Sullivan to allow her to put forward a defense of protection from dispossession under General Statutes § 47a-23c and reentered the judgment of strict foreclosure nunc pro tunc; following a hearing on the defense of protection under General Statutes § 47a-23c, Hon. Donald W. Celotto, state trial referee, granted the motion by the substitute plaintiff for an order of possession in its favor and for an order of ejectment of the defendant Carmel Sullivan, from which the defendant Carmel Sullivan appealed. Reversed; further proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.  [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank commenced suit to foreclose against defendants, a mortgage note executor, condominium association, and tenant in possession. Upon grant of a judgment of foreclosure, plaintiff attempted to execute a judgment against the tenant. The tenant claimed that she was protected under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-23c. The Superior Court in the District of New Haven (Connecticut) ordered ejectment, and the tenant in possession sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff bank commenced suit against defendants, a mortgage note executor, condominium association, and tenant in possession, to foreclose upon property. The trial court granted plaintiff's motion to foreclose and plaintiff sought to eject the tenant from the premises. The tenant claimed that she was protected from dispossession under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-23c. The trial court granted plaintiff's ejectment motion and the tenant sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-23c protected the tenant from ejectment because the tenant was a tenant in sufferance, continued in possession after her rightful possession had ceased, and was thus a protected tenant under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-23c; (2) the operative previsions of Conn. Gen. Stat. §47a-23c did not permit plaintiff from ejecting the tenant because plaintiff failed to show probable cause for the ejectment. Therefore, the court concluded that plaintiff could not eject the tenant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that ordered ejectment of defendant tenant in possession and held that the tenant was statutorily protected from ejectment in the absence of probable cause, which plaintiff bank failed to show.

 

99 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Szymkiewicz


(15253)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


237 Conn. 613; 678 A.2d 473; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 238


March 21, 1996, Argued  
July 9, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the sixth degree and breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number ten, and tried to the jury before Leuba, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Lavery and Schaller, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of breach of the peace, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversing defendant's conviction of breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(1). The lower court had held that there was insufficient evidence to sustain defendant's conviction because the conduct for which defendant was prosecuted consisted only of speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial of breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(1). She successfully appealed her conviction. The appellate court construed the statute under which defendant was convicted to proscribe only physical conduct, and concluded that there was insufficient evidence to establish a violation. On appeal, the court held that the appellate court improperly concluded that § 53a-181(a)(1) did not include speech that constituted "fighting words" and held that the evidence was sufficient for conviction without evidence of physical conduct. The court found that the jury could reasonably have concluded that defendant engaged in conduct that was tumultuous, threatening or violent and that defendant's language, which could have led to imminent retaliation or violence, contained a sufficient aspect of physicality to be punishable pursuant to § 53a-181(a)(1). The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to that court with direction to affirm the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court held that "fighting words" without physical conduct were sufficient to sustain a conviction for breach of the peace. The court therefore reversed the judgment of the appellate and court remanded the case to that court, so that the trial court's judgment could be affirmed.

 

100 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sheff v. O'Neill


(15255)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


238 Conn. 1; 678 A.2d 1267; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 239


September 28, 1995, Argued  
July 9, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine whether the defendants have failed to provide the plaintiffs with a substantially equal educational opportunity as a result of the alleged segregation by race and ethnicity of students in public schools in the greater Hartford metropolitan area, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the court, Hammer, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the appeal was transferred to this court, which ordered the parties to stipulate to all undisputed facts and to prepare and submit to the trial court proposed findings of facts that are disputed, and further ordered the trial court to issue findings on each of the disputed facts.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minority schoolchildren appealed a decision of the Hartford-New Britain Superior Court (Connecticut), which found in favor of defendant public officials on the schoolchildren's claims under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 20, and art. VIII, § 1, that their de facto segregated public schools denied them an equal, free, and public education.


OVERVIEW: Minority schoolchildren asserted that 14 of Hartford's 25 public schools were almost entirely minority and that this de facto racial segregation deprived them of an education equal to those of schoolchildren living in other school districts. The court found the question justiciable and held that state action, in terms of failing to remedy the inequalities, brought the public officials within the purview of the court. The court next found that Conn. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and art. I, §§ 1 and 20, imposed on the legislature an affirmative constitutional obligation to provide the minority schoolchildren with an educational opportunity substantially equal to that enjoyed by other schoolchildren and that this obligation exceeded any based on the federal constitution. The court found that the initiatives undertaken by the public officials had not eradicated the significant disparities between school districts. The court granted the minority schoolchildren declaratory judgment on their claims but directed the trial court to retain jurisdiction to grant consequential relief, if needed, thus giving the public officials time to fashion their own remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the public officials, and the case was remanded with direction to render a declaratory judgment for the minority schoolchildren; the superior court was directed to retain jurisdiction.

 

101 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gerardi


(15173)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


237 Conn. 348; 677 A.2d 937; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 203


October 31, 1995, Argued  
June 18, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a machine gun, having a weapon in a motor vehicle, altering an identification mark on a pistol or revolver, and reckless endangerment in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Karazin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of a machine gun, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of possession of a machine gun for an aggressive and offensive purpose. Defendant was found not guilty of knowingly having a weapon in a vehicle, altering or removing a weapon's identification mark, and reckless endangerment. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant sought appellate review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a vehicle stopped by police in the course of their investigation of gunshots being fired from an automobile. After a vehicle search, the police found two shell casings; further investigation led to the discovery of a machine gun on the side of the road. On appeal, defendant alleged that the trial court's jury instructions on the mandatory rebuttable presumptions of possession and purpose set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-202(d), (e), (g) violated the Due Process Clause of the federal constitution. The court held that the instructions violated defendant's constitutional rights to have the State prove each element of the crime charged. The court held that it was inconceivable that the legislature intended for a jury to be required to infer that defendant had possessed a machine gun for an offensive or aggressive purpose from the mere fact that the gun was unregistered or that live ammunition or shell casings were located in the immediate vicinity of the gun. The court held that the erroneous jury instructions might have contributed to defendant's conviction. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that defendant was guilty of possession of a machine gun for an aggressive and offensive purpose. The court held that jury instructions based upon statutory rebuttable presumptions violated defendant's due process rights and constituted prejudicial error. The court remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Troupe


(14882)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


237 Conn. 284; 677 A.2d 917; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 201


January 17, 1996, Argued  
June 11, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions for sexual assault, sexual assault in the third degree, and kidnapping in the first degree which were ordered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault, sexual assault in the third degree, and kidnapping in the first degree. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that admission of evidence of constancy of accusation testimony did not violate his rights under the confrontation clause of U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court held that U.S. Const. amend. VI was not violated because the victim and the witnesses testified in court and were subject to cross-examination. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to strike the state's expert's testimony for violation of a sequestration order. The court held that defendant failed to prove that the sequestration order was violated. The court held that defendant was not denied a fair trial when the state amended a charging information shortly before trial to assert kidnapping charges. The court held that defendant brought this claim to light for the first time on appeal, and expressly disavowed this claim in his argument to the trial court in support of a motion to strike. Thus, the record below contained nothing to substantiate the defendant's contention on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for sexual assault, sexual assault in the third degree, and kidnapping in the first degree. Admission of evidence of constancy of accusation testimony did not violate his rights under the confrontation clause of the Sixth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution. The Sixth Amendment was not violated because the victim and the witnesses testified in court and were subject to cross-examination.

State v. Hill


(15011)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


237 Conn. 81; 675 A.2d 866; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 153


December 6, 1995, Argued  
May 21, 1996, officially released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of heroin with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Fasano, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Fasano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted and sentenced defendant for possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and for possession of heroin with intent to sell. Defendant claimed error in the admission of improperly seized evidence, exposure to double jeopardy, and insufficiency of evidence.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant in the street holding a plastic bag and talking to a man. Both men left in different directions when they saw the officer, who followed defendant into an open apartment belonging to defendant's friend and retrieved the bag, which contained crack cocaine and heroin. Defendant was convicted of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277. Defendant appealed, claiming that: (1) the narcotics were seized without a warrant or probable cause; (2) conviction on the two narcotics offenses constituted double jeopardy; and (3) the evidence was insufficient to establish an intent to sell the narcotics. The court affirmed the trial court, finding that: (1) defendant was not seized when he was approached by the officer on the street, and defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the apartment and hence no standing to contest the seizure; (2) the Legislature did not intend to bar multiple punishments for the simultaneous possession of both crack cocaine and heroin; and (3) uncontroverted expert testimony indicated that only a drug dealer would have possessed the quantity, type, and combination of narcotics seized.


OUTCOME: The court found for the State and affirmed the decision of the trial court.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain, (Connecticut), which dismissed the taxpayer's challenge of a tax assessment by defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services for the taxpayer's in-state use of an airplane purchased out of state.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer bought an airplane out of state and was assessed a tax for his in-state use. The taxpayer filed a letter of protest and requested an agency hearing. After the hearing, the assessment was upheld and the taxpayer sought review. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

State v. Bruno


(14851)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


236 Conn. 514; 673 A.2d 1117; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 83


September 19, 1995, Argued  
March 26, 1996, decision released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Bruno v. Tarascio, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 721 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 1, 2002)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Bruno, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1625 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, and three counts of tampering with physical evidence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to a three judge court, Pickett, Susco and Fineberg, Js.; judgment of guilty of one count of murder and three counts of tampering with physical evidence, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Bruno, 1993 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1752 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 14, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) for one count of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a and 53a-8, and for three counts of tampering with physical evidence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-155 (a) (1) and 53a-8. Defendant received a total effective sentence of sixty years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and of tampering with physical evidence. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion for disclosure and an in camera examination of any psychiatric or school records of two state's witnesses for the purpose of discovering material relevant to their abilities to accurately perceive, recall and relate events. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that defendant failed to establish a sufficient foundation from which the trial court could have concluded that there was a reasonable ground to believe that the records would yield evidence useful to the witnesses' impeachment concerning lack of capacity to remember and relate events. The court also held that the trial court's failure to retain the records as a sealed exhibit was improper but concluded that its action was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted defendant of murder and evidence tampering. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's request for an in camera inspection of confidential records of state witnesses and that the trial court's failure to seal and secure the confidential records for the record was improper but constituted harmless error.

Lash v. Aetna Cas. & Sur. Co.


(15223)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


236 Conn. 318; 673 A.2d 84; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 55


November 2, 1995, Argued  
March 19, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to vacate an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the named defendant et al. filed motions to confirm the award, and tried to the court, DeMayo, J.; judgment denying the application to vacate and granting the motions to confirm, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, Heiman and Spear, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed a judgment denying a motion by plaintiff, insured's administrator, to vacate an arbitration award and granting defendant insurers' motions to confirm the award. The administrator appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The insured was killed when he was a passenger in a vehicle that was struck head-on by another vehicle. The administrator recovered from a policy issued to the driver of the other vehicle. The insured was also insured under underinsured motorist policies issued by the insurers, and the administrator argued that he was entitled to recovery under each of those policies. Holding that the administrator was not entitled to recover underinsured motorist benefits, the court affirmed the confirmation of the arbitration award in favor of the insurers. In a prior case, the court concluded that underinsured motorist coverage under separate policies covering a claimant could not be aggregated or "stacked" for purposes of determining whether a vehicle was underinsured within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. The court could not overrule its earlier decisions unless the most cogent reasons and inescapable logic required it, especially when the precedent concerned the interpretation or construction of a statute. There was nothing ambiguous in the language of § 38a-336(e) and the intent of the legislature was clearly expressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the administrator's motion to vacate the arbitration award and confirming the insurers' motions to confirm the award.

 

108 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trine


(15277)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


236 Conn. 216; 673 A.2d 1098; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 51


December 5, 1995, Argued  
March 12, 1996, Decision Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Parker, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Purtill, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, Lavery and Heiman, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state government sought reversal of the decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) overturning defendant convicted offender's drug conviction, with the appeal centering on whether the "plain feel" doctrine applied under Conn. Const. art. I § 7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant accused offender was present inside a residence for which a search warrant had been issued. When the police entered, they ordered defendant and the others present to lie on the floor, and then frisked each person for weapons. Although defendant had no weapon, the frisk indicated to the officer conducting it that defendant was in possession of crack cocaine. Defendant was arrested for that crime. He sought suppression, but that motion was denied. He then pled no contest while reserving the right to argue the suppression claim on appeal. He was successful before an intermediate appellate panel, and the prosecution then appealed that ruling. On further review, the court reversed. It held that Conn. Const. art. I § 7 did not prohibit the seizure of contraband discovered during a protective weapons frisk, provided that as here the illegal nature of the item felt was immediately apparent. Given that in defendant's case the officer who conducted the weapons frisk could determine from his sense of touch that what he felt in defendant's clothing was crack cocaine, the seizure of that substance was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment below was reversed, and defendant's conviction reinstated. There was no violation of Conn. Const. art. I § 7 when crack cocaine felt inside defendant's clothing during a protective frisk was seized.
