State v. Cassidy


(15101)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


236 Conn. 112; 672 A.2d 899; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 45


September 22, 1995, Argued  
February 27, 1996, decision released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, robbery in the first degree and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Bridgeport, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before McGrath, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court convicted defendant of kidnapping in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and failure to appear in the first degree. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that certain comments made by the prosecutor during his closing argument to the jury violated his rights under U. S. Const. amend. VI and XIV and under Conn. Const. Art. 1, § 8. Specifically, defendant argued that the prosecutor improperly argued to the jury that the defendant, because he was present in court throughout the trial, was able to tailor his testimony to that of the state's witnesses who in contrast to the defendant, were subject to the trial court's sequestration order. The court determined that the prosecutor's argument invited the jury to draw an inference adverse to defendant solely because he asserted his constitutional right to be present at trial and, consequently, that those comments unreasonably interfered with defendant's free exercise of that right. Furthermore, the court determined that the argument was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt and, therefore that defendant was entitled to a new trial on the kidnapping, robbery, and the restraint charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for failure to appear, but reversed his convictions for kidnapping, robbery, and unlawful restraint and remanded for a new trial.

 

112 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chance


(14871)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


236 Conn. 31; 671 A.2d 323; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 31


September 22, 1995, Argued  
February 13, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of arson in the first degree and information charging the defendant with the crime of assault of a department of correction employee, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Stanley, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a correctional center inmate, was charged with arson in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111, and assault of a department of correction employee, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c. The cases were consolidated in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) and defendant was convicted of both charges by a jury. Defendant appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(b).


OVERVIEW: Not served dinner when he demanded it, defendant set his mattress afire. A few days later, a correctional officer, checking for defendant's presence through the screened window of his cell door, was struck in the face with urine. On appeal, the court held that severance for trial of the two charges was not required where the charges were clearly distinguishable and arose from two discrete incidents, the assault evidence was presented last so as not to inflame the jury on the arson charge, the issues were simple and straightforward, and the trial court instructed the jury not to consider the assault evidence in its deliberations on the arson charge. Defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the uncharged offense of criminal mischief, which was not a lesser included offense of arson. The state could impeach a defense witness about his bias toward corrections officials, and the state's cross-examination of defendant about his prior acts of misconduct did not unduly press the issue once defendant denied the misconduct. Psychiatric evaluation as a condition of probation was not inconsistent with the denial of defendant's motion for a psychiatric evaluation prior to sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both judgments of conviction.

 

113 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Reid v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


(15152)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 850; 670 A.2d 1271; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 12


October 26, 1995, Argued  
January 30, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant upholding an order by the Lebanon zoning enforcement officer that the plaintiff cease year-round occupancy of certain of his premises, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich and tried to the court, Hendel, J.; judgment for the defendant dismissing the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich (Connecticut), which dismissed the landowner's appeal and entered judgment in favor of appellee zoning board of appeals, upholding the board's decision that the landowner was required to cease the year-round occupancy of his premises.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's predecessor-in-interest had acquired from the board a variance, based on a finding of personal hardship, which gave her the right to use her property on a year-round basis for her lifetime. Several years after the landowner acquired title, a zoning enforcement officer ordered him to cease occupying the premises year-round. Pending the owner's appeal of the officer's action, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(b) was enacted. On appeal, the landowner argued, among other things, that § 8-6(b) was to be applied retroactively and that it required a finding that he was entitled to the benefit of the variance. The court agreed and reversed the trial court's judgment. The court agreed with the trial court that the variance was granted for the life of the predecessor and was, therefore, invalid under the rule that zoning power regulated the use, not the user, of land. Nevertheless, the court determined that the purpose of § 8-6(b) was to validate any variance that ran with the land, despite an invalid and integral condition. Therefore, the court concluded that the illegal condition of the life use was severed from the variance and the variance survived to the benefit of the landowner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment sustaining the landowner's appeal in accordance with the court's opinion.

State v. Esposito


(14870)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 802; 670 A.2d 301; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 15


September 27, 1995, Argued  
January 30, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, robbery in the first degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial; on remand, the case was tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of felony murder and burglary in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for felony murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, and of burglary in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101 (a) (1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony murder based on evidence that his accomplice killed a man during the course of a burglary while several people were in the home. He was granted a new trial and was again convicted. On appeal, the court held that there was no Brady violation in the first trial as a result of the prosecution's failure to provide the defense with a previously recorded statement of a State witness because the recording was little more than cumulative material. The court rejected defendant's contention that his testimony in the first trial should have been held inadmissible in the second trial because he had been unconstitutionally compelled to testify in the first trial due to the nondisclosure of the tape recording. The court held that although the trial court erred in excluding certain evidence that a co-defendant had threatened defendant and his family, the error was harmless. The court found that the excluded evidence was only indirectly probative of defendant's defense. The trial court did not err in excluding certain polygraph evidence as unreliable. It was within the trial court's discretion to admit expert testimony by a dog handler as to tracking evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

D.A. Pincus & Co. v. Meehan


(15175)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 865; 670 A.2d 1278; 1996 Conn. LEXIS 14


December 7, 1995, Argued  
January 30, 1996, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from decisions by the defendant denying the plaintiff's claims for deduction from corporation business taxes interest it had paid on moneys borrowed to carry certain municipal obligations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Tax Session at Hartford, where the appeals were consolidated and tried to the court, Blue, J.; judgments sustaining the plaintiff's appeals, from which the defendant filed a joint appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Connecticut Commissioner of Revenue Services, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff taxpayer's appeal from a decision by the commissioner that denied the taxpayer's deduction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-217(a)(A) from its corporate business taxes for tax interest paid on money borrowed to carry municipal obligations.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer engaged in the business of buying and selling municipal obligations. The taxpayer included the interest that it received from its inventory of municipal obligations in its gross income and deducted the interest expenses on the indebtedness that it incurred to carry the bonds from its gross income. The commissioner determined that the taxpayer had improperly deducted the interest expenses under Conn. Gen. Stat. 12-217(a)(A) and assessed an additional tax against the taxpayer. The commissioner subsequently denied the taxpayer's request for a correction and the taxpayer sought judicial review in the trial court. The trial court found that § 12-217(a)(A) violated the Equal Protection Clause. The commissioner claimed on appeal that § 12-217(a)(A) did not single out broker-dealers in municipal obligations from broker-dealers in corporate bonds as a particular class to whom differing treatment was afforded. The court agreed with the commissioner's claim. The court found that there were conceivable reasons for the different treatment of corporate and municipal bonds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that sustained the taxpayer's appeal on the ground that Con. Gen. Stat. § 12-217(a)(A) violated the Equal Protection Clause. The Connecticut legislature could conceivably have justified the disallowance of tax deductions for interest expenses incurred in connection with maintaining a municipal bonds when it allowed such deductions for expenses incurred in connection with maintaining corporate bonds.

State v. Hickam


(15256)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 614; 668 A.2d 1321; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 432


September 19, 1995, Argued  
December 26, 1995, decision released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 28, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 432.


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and failing to drive on the right, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number ten, where the court, McMahon, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of operating under the influence of intoxicating liquor and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review, with permission, of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number 10, which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of operating under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The appeal was transferred to the court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 4023 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: The State administratively suspended defendant's motor vehicle operator license pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b after she was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a). The trial court dismissed the criminal charges against defendant on double jeopardy grounds. The court held that: (1) the 90-day suspension period mandated by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b was not disproportionate to the public safety interest that was served by expeditious suspension of the operating privileges of an individual administratively found to have operated a motor vehicle with a specific blood alcohol content; (2) an administrative suspension of operating privileges pursuant to § 14-227b was rationally related to the legislature's assessment that public safety on highways was furthered by the prompt removal, even if temporarily, of those individuals who were arrested for operating under the influence; and (3) the administrative suspension of defendant's license had a legitimate remedial purpose and did not bar her criminal prosecution under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Covelli v. Commissioner of Revenue Servs.


(15198)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 539; 668 A.2d 699; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 423


September 19, 1995, Argued  
December 19, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the assessment of a marijuana and controlled substances tax against the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Tax Session at Hartford, where the court, Blue, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax commissioner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain, Tax Session at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted appellee taxpayer's motion for summary judgment on an appeal from the assessment of a marijuana and controlled substances tax against the taxpayer by the commissioner.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the commissioner, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-651(a) could collect a tax on illegal drugs assessed against the taxpayer after he had been arrested, prosecuted, convicted and sentenced for the possession of those same drugs with intent to sell. The trial court's held that the tax was violative of the Double Jeopardy Clause of the Fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The tax session of the Superior Court granted the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded holding that the tax did not rise to the level of punishment and did not require that the taxpayer be arrested or convicted in order to impose the tax. The court held further that the tax did not depend on the taxpayer's arrest, the destruction of the property, and did not discriminate against the casual user as it only required the possession of enough illegal substance that it could lead one to reasonably believe that they were involved in the manufacture or sale of the product.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court for the commissioner.

 

118 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. DeFrancesco


(14971)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


235 Conn. 426; 668 A.2d 348; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 393


September 20, 1995, Argued  
November 21, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of possession of a potentially dangerous animal, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the court, Gormley, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Heiman and Schaller, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment, and, on the granting of certification, the state appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed and defendant cross appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), reversing in part a trial court's judgment of conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26.40a for possessing potentially dangerous animals. The State's petition for review was to decide in part whether the appellate court had improperly determined that § 26.40a was unconstitutionally vague as to the jungle and Bengal cats that defendant possessed.


OVERVIEW: Also, the petition was to address whether the appellate court had improperly concluded that § 26.40a was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the hybrid bobcat. The state supreme court concluded that the list of felidae or cats prohibited by § 26.40a was not exclusive and that § 26.40a was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to all three cats. In order to decide whether § 26.40a was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case, the court was first required to consider whether the list of felidae in § 26.40 was exclusive. The court found that the legislature did not intend for the felidae listed in § 26.40a to be the sole felidae the possession of which was prohibited. The list was simply an example of the types of felidae prohibited. The State correctly argued that the term "including" was a term of expansion and that the list served as an example of felidae types. The conclusion was also supported by the doctrine of ejusdem generis and the legislative history of § 26.40a. The court also concluded that bobcats, Bengal cats, and jungle cats were all prohibited by § 26.40a. Possession of purebred and hybrid cats were prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment regarding the bobcat and reversed the judgment regarding the jungle and Bengal cats.

Affirmed by State v. Breton, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 244 (Conn., June 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of capital felony and two counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Heiman, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the notice of aggravating factor filed by the state and the state appealed to this court, which reversed the trial court's decision; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Heiman, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found an aggravating factor and no mitigating factor, and the court rendered judgment of guilty of capital felony and imposed the death penalty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Breton, 212 Conn. 258, 562 A.2d 1060, 1989 Conn. LEXIS 225 (1989)



DISPOSITION: Judgment imposing the death penalty reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of capital felony and sentenced to death by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), challenged both his conviction and his sentence on multiple grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital felony and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction but, owing to a penalty phase instructional error, ordered a new sentencing hearing. OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but his death sentence was reversed and his case remanded to the trial court for a new penalty hearing. Remand was required because defendant's jury was not instructed that mitigating factors were required to be unanimously rejected.

State v. Cobb


(14384)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 735; 663 A.2d 948; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 308


March 15, 1995, Argued  
August 8, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendant to expand the universe of cases to be considered by this court in its statutorily mandated proportionality review of the death sentence imposed by a three judge panel of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Kulawiz, Barnett and Langenbach, Js., on the defendant's conviction of, inter alia, two counts of the crime of felony murder.



DISPOSITION: Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury, Kulawiz, Barnett, and Langenback (Connecticut), which convicted him of, inter alia, two counts of felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an African-American male, was sentenced to death for the murder of a white female. He appealed his conviction and filed a motion to enlarge the class of similar cases to be used in determining whether his sentence was justified in light of the prohibition against disproportionality, provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46b(b)(3). Defendant contended that the expanded universe of cases would enable him to demonstrate that race had an impermissible effect on capital sentencing decisions in the state and rendered the imposition of the death penalty on him disproportionate. The court affirmed the sentence and denied defendant's motion, holding that proportionality review pursuant to § 53a-46b(b)(3) and legislative history did not contemplate the type of inquiry that would be necessitated by defendant's motion, which would necessarily be accompanied by detailed, complex fact-finding. Despite defendant's failure to raise the claim at trial and, therefore, to have created a proper trial record, he would be allowed to raise it by way of a petition for a writ of habeas corpus after appeal, if the ultimate disposition of his direct appeal rendered his claim still viable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and denied defendant's motion to enlarge the universe of cases used in determining whether his death sentence was justified or disproportionate. The court held that legislative history did not contemplate the complex fact-finding type of inquiry defendant advocated.

Donner v. Kearse


(15036)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 660; 662 A.2d 1269; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 278


March 22, 1995, Argued  
August 1, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a motor vehicle accident allegedly caused by the defendants' negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the action was withdrawn by the plaintiff Robert Donner as to all the defendants and where the named plaintiff withdrew her action as to the defendant Anna Riccio et al. and executed a release of liability; thereafter, the named defendant et al. filed a special defense regarding the executed release, which special defense was bifurcated from the issues of liability and damages for purposes of trial, and the matter was tried to the jury before M. Hennessey, J.; verdict for the named plaintiff against the named defendant et al.; subsequently, the jury found for the named plaintiff on the special defense and determined that the executed release did not apply to the named defendant et al., and the court denied the motion to set aside the verdict and for a new trial or remittitur filed by the named defendant et al. and rendered judgment for the named plaintiff in accordance with the verdict, and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger claimed that defendant police officer was negligent in operating his police cruiser so as to cause a collision with the vehicle driven by the passenger's husband. A judgment was rendered for the passenger and the police officer appealed to the appellate court (Connecticut). The case was transferred to the court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. 4023, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: The passenger, after settling with one defendant, amended her complaint to claim that the police officer was negligent in the operation of his police cruiser. The jury found that police officer was 100 percent at fault. The jury then found that the passenger did not intend to release the police officer from liability by signing a release with the other defendant. The court found that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 520572h(f), the passenger had initially defined the universe of negligent persons as the defendant and the released defendant. Because the passenger did not sign a release with her husband driver, or that he was no longer a party, the trial court did not commit error in striking the police officers special defense that the passenger's husband was at fault. The court noted that the police officer could have impleaded the passenger's husband as a third party defendant. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-216a did not erect a total bar that would have prevented a jury from ever considering the terms of a release agreement as evidence. It was not error to not let the jury know of the release while determining liability because it would have been prejudicial to the passenger.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Massameno v. Statewide Grievance Comm.


(14930), (14931)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 539; 663 A.2d 317; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 282


April 26, 1995, Argued  
August 1, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, the jurisdiction of the defendant to investigate and discipline the plaintiff as a result of certain grievances filed against him, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Schaller, J., granted the motion for joinder of interested party as plaintiff filed by the chief state's attorney, and where the intervening plaintiff filed a complaint seeking the same relief as the plaintiff; thereafter, on a stipulation of facts, the matter was tried to the court, Wagner, J., who rendered judgment for the defendant; subsequently, the court denied the joint motion by the plaintiff and the intervening plaintiff to open and reconsider, and the plaintiff and the intervening plaintiff filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prosecutor challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which held in favor of defendant grievance committee in prosecutor's action for a declaratory judgment to determine the grievance committee's jurisdiction to investigate and discipline him as a result of certain grievances filed against him.


OVERVIEW: Grievances were filed against a prosecutor that alleged violations of the rules of professional conduct. The grievance committee found merit to the allegations and was going to seek sanctions. The prosecutor sought declaratory relief regarding the grievance committee's jurisdiction. The court affirmed and held that the judicial branch, through the grievance committee, could regulate and sanction conduct by the prosecutor for the exercise of his official judgment without violating the separation of powers mandated by Conn. Const. art. II. The functions of a prosecutor were not purely those of an executive officer because a prosecutor maintained a position as an officer of the court. The authority underlying the prosecutor's powers merged with his obligations to the judicial process. The impeachment provisions of Conn. Const. art. IX, §§ 1, 3 did not bar other forms of discipline because the functions of the prosecutor were an integral part of the judicial process, and the judicial branch had an overlapping interest in the administration of justice. The judicial branch could exercise jurisdiction to supervise and discipline the prosecutor concurrently with the executive branch.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

124 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Benjamin v. Bailey


(14968)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 455; 662 A.2d 1226; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 263


April 26, 1995, Argued  
July 25, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of the state assault weapons law, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Dranginis, J.; judgment declaring the statutes to be constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendants cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals and an assault weapon manufacturer, brought an action against defendant state officials for declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of an assault weapons ban, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-202a through 53-202k. The Superior Court of the District of Litchfield (Connecticut) declared the ban to be constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part. Plaintiffs appealed and the state cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the ban was constitutional but narrowed the statutes by excising certain words from the enumeration of proscribed weapons in order to avoid an unconstitutional vagueness. The court ruled in favor of the state, agreeing that the ban was constitutional but disagreeing that any modification of the ban was necessary. A ban on assault weapons did not infringe on the right to bear arms guaranteed by Conn. Const. art. I, § 15 because the ban continued to permit access to a wide array of weapons. Equal protection rights applied only to persons, not weapons. Even if plaintiffs' claims were construed as disparate treatment claims, under the rational basis standard the ban was lawful. As to the weapons manufacturer whose product was specifically proscribed, the ban was not a bill of attainder because it did not inflict punishment without a trial and even if it were so construed, it did not apply only to named individuals or to easily ascertainable members of a group. It applied to all persons who sold that specific weapon. Finally, the ban was not subject to a vagueness challenge in a declaratory judgment setting because it was not vague in all its applications.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part, and the trial court was directed to enter judgment in favor of the state. The holding that the ban on assault weapons was constitutional was affirmed, but the finding that certain components of the legislation were unconstitutionally vague was reversed.

Bauer v. Waste Mgmt.


(14949), (14951)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 221; 662 A.2d 1179; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 208


March 17, 1995, Argued  
July 11, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in the first case, to enjoin the defendant from violating a certain zoning regulation that established the height limitation for landfills and to enjoin the defendant from expanding its nonconforming use and nonconforming structures on certain of its land, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where Loretta Brickley was substituted as party plaintiff; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Susco, J., which rendered judgment for the defendant, and the substitute plaintiff appealed.

Appeal, in the second case, from a decision by the defendant amending a certain local zoning regulation to limit to ninety feet the height of a landfill existing in an industrial zone as a nonconforming use, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the matter was tried to the court, Susco, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiff sustaining the appeal and remanding the matter to the defendant with direction to revoke the amendment, and the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed. Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases that involved the same property and regulation the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut) held that the regulation that limited the height of appellee landfill's property was unconstitutional and prohibited appellant enforcement officer's enforcement of the regulation. The trial court also held that state law did not preempt appellant city zoning commission's regulation. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the first action, the trial court concluded that the 90-foot height limitation imposed on the landfill by the city zoning commission (commission) constituted an unconstitutional taking of the landfill's property in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. The trial court also concluded that the commission had not waived its opportunity to seek height restrictions by its failure to appeal from the issuance of a permit by the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection (DEP), and the height regulation was not preempted by state law. In the second appeal, which was an enforcement action of the limitation, the trial court refused to grant the enforcement officer's request for injunction relief to cure the landfill's violation of the height limitation. On appeal, the court held that: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-208a(b) was not intended to preempt regulation by the local governing body; (2) the landfill did not prove a nonconforming use with respect to the height limitation; and (3) the limitation was a not an unconstitutional taking of the landfill's property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination that the height limitation imposed by the commission constituted an unconstitutional taking. The court remanded the enforcement action for consideration of the enforcement officer's claim for injunctive relief. The court remanded the administrative appeal with instructions to dismiss the landfill's appeal.

 

126 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


International Bhd. of Police Officers, Local 564 v. Borough of Jewett City


(15067), (15068)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 123; 661 A.2d 573; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 201; 150 L.R.R.M. 2805


May 31, 1995, Argued  
July 4, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application, in each case, to confirm an arbitral award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, O'Neill, J., granted the motion to intervene as party defendant in each case filed by C. Francis Driscoll, receiver for the borough of Jewett City; thereafter, the court, M. Hennessey, J., denied the intervening defendant's motions to dismiss the applications to confirm and the cases were tried to the court, O'Neill, J.; judgment in each case granting the plaintiff's application to confirm the award, from which the intervening defendant filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff unions filed applications against defendant borough, in two cases, to confirm an arbitral award. Party defendant, a receiver, was permitted to intervene. Under the Municipal Employees Relations Act (MERA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-467 et seq., the receiver challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) granting each union's application to confirm the award.


OVERVIEW: Having reached an impasse, binding arbitration was imposed on the unions and the borough, and an arbitration panel was appointed to hear the issues. Having reached complete agreement on the issues during the hearings before the panel, the unions and the borough agreed to waive the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-473(c) and stipulated to a collective bargaining agreement as the award of the panel of arbitrators. The trial court had denied the receiver's motions to dismiss the applications to confirm prior to the grant of the applications. The court reversed the judgment granting the applications. The court concluded that, when the parties expressly waived their rights under the compulsory arbitration statute, such stipulated awards were properly characterized as collective bargaining agreements, governed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-474, rather than arbitration decisions governed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-473c. The awards merely represented the parties' own agreements. Thus, in the absence of compliance with the statutory requirements for an arbitral award, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-417 to consider the applications for confirmation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and remanded the actions to the trial court with direction to render judgments dismissing the unions' applications.

Weidenbacher v. Duclos


(14942)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


234 Conn. 51; 661 A.2d 988; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 205


February 10, 1995, Argued  
July 4, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking custody of a minor child born to the respondent mother, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and referred to Hon. Daniel F. Spallone, who granted the respondents' motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Foti and Lavery, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father appealed the decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court that petitioner lacked standing to pursue his claim in which he sought custody of a minor child born to respondent mother.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner putative father alleged that he was the biological father of a minor child of respondent mother and sought custody. Petitioner appealed the appellate court's affirmation of the trial court's judgment that petitioner did not have standing to establish his paternity. The court reversed the appellate court's decision, concluding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172a did not foreclose the court's jurisdiction to determine whether a putative father was, in fact, the biological father of a child. The court held that the mere fact that a child was born while the mother was married was not a per se bar that prevented a man other than her husband from establishing standing to bring an action for a writ of habeas corpus for custody of or visitation with a minor child. The court determined that a putative father of such a child had to offer proof, at a preliminary evidentiary hearing devoted to standing, that he was entitled to set in motion the judicial machinery to determine whether he was the biological father of the child. The court remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with its opinion that petitioner established standing to pursue his habeas corpus action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. The court remanded the case to the trial court for proceedings consistent with its opinion that petitioner offered sufficient proof to establish that he had standing to pursue his habeas action.

State v. Day


(14418)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 813; 661 A.2d 539; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 191


February 6, 1995, Argued  
June 27, 1995, decision released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent civil proceeding at Day v. Milling, 2000 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15965 (D. Conn., Feb. 22, 2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Day v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 433 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony and assault in the third degree and with four counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with and convicted of murder. During the trial, defendant represented himself. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield convicted defendant and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly accepted his waiver of the right to counsel, granted his pro se motion for a speedy trial while he still was represented by counsel, and denied his request for a mistrial upon reappointment of counsel. Defendant also claimed the trial court improperly denied various motions during voir dire, granted a continuance only for two weeks rather than for the one month requested, and failed to instruct the jury on the "two witness" rule. This failure allegedly resulted in his conviction upon insufficient evidence. The court disagreed with all of defendant's claims and held that (1) the trial court properly accepted defendant's waiver of his right to counsel because defendant was competent, and the waiver was intelligently and knowingly made. (2) The motion for a speedy trial was properly granted because his subsequent waiver of counsel ratified the prior speedy trial motion. (3) The trial court was not required to grant the motion for a mistrial. And (4) there was no abuse of discretion by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hilton v. City of New Haven


(14925)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 701; 661 A.2d 973; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 174


June 9, 1994, September 20, 1994, Argued  
June 20, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from failing to provide emergency shelter to the plaintiff class of homeless individuals, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, DeMayo, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss the action and issued a memorandum of decision ordering the defendants to provide emergency shelter to the plaintiffs and to submit a plan outlining the implementation process of that order; thereafter, the court denied the defendants' motion to reconsider the decision and determined that certain statutory amendments did not invalidate the court's decision and that there was not a constitutional right to shelter, and ordered the defendants to submit a modified plan of compliance with the court's order; subsequently, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for an ex parte temporary injunction, granted, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, the motion by Georgianna Valtorta et al. to intervene as plaintiffs and, following the approval of the defendants' modified plan of compliance, rendered judgment for the plaintiffs in accordance with the memorandum of decision and the modified plan of compliance, and [***2] the defendants appealed and the plaintiffs cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the underlying action, plaintiff class of homeless individuals filed a complaint against defendant city to enjoin the city from failing to provide emergency shelter. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) ordered the city to provide emergency shelter and to submit a compliance plan. The matter came before the court on both parties' appeal from the trial court's approval of the city's compliance plan.


OVERVIEW: The homeless individuals argued that an affirmative governmental obligation to provide shelter to its citizens should be recognized under the Connecticut constitution either as a constitutionally incorporated right under Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 or as an unenumerated right. The city claimed that the trial court improperly failed to dismiss its previous order in light of amendments to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-273d (1993) and improperly required the city to submit a compliance plan and subjected it to continuing oversight. The court concluded that the homeless individuals' constitutional claim was controlled by its decision in a companion case which held that the state did not have a constitutional obligation to provide subsistence benefits, including shelter. It concluded that the trial court properly denied the city's request to dismiss its previous order because the 1993 amendments to § 17-273d did not alter the trial court's ability to grant relief for the city's failure to comply with the new statute's mandates. The court further concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ordering the city to file a compliance plan and subjecting it to continuing oversight.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which approved the city's compliance plan for providing shelter to homeless individuals.

Moore v. Ganim


(14923)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 557; 660 A.2d 742; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 175


June 9, 1994, Argued; September 20, 1994, Argued  
June 20, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from suspending the plaintiffs' general assistance benefits, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Vertefeuille, J., granted an ex parte temporary injunction allowing the continuance of such benefits to the plaintiffs until a hearing could be held and granted the motion of the state et al. to intervene as defendants; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiffs' request for temporary injunctive relief, and the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants sought declaratory and injunctive relief in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted a temporary restraining order pending a hearing and granted intervention to the State as a defendant. After a hearing, the trial court vacated the temporary restraining order and denied the claimants' request for a temporary injunction. The claimants, granted certification, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimants brought an action contesting the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-273b (1993), which limited the general assistance benefits employable persons could receive to no more than nine months in a 12-month period. The claimants argued that this durational limit abrogated the state's affirmative constitutional obligation to provide its indigent citizens with a minimal level of subsistence. The court concluded that the state constitution did not impose an affirmative duty on the state to provide the benefits sought by the claimants. Section 17-273b did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 because the claimants did not prove that an indigent person had a common law cause of action to compel the state, prior to the constitution's passage, to provide a level of minimal subsistence. The claimants also failed to prove that, in implementing Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-273b (1993), the state violated an unenumerated constitutional obligation. The precedents of the court, federal, and sister states did not support the claimants' assertion, nor did the state constitution's text; history; or contemporary economic, sociological, or public policy considerations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Connecticut Resources Recovery Auth. v. Commissioner of Envtl. Protection


(15013), (15014), (15015), (15016)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 486; 659 A.2d 714; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 165


April 19, 1995, Argued  
June 13, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in each case from a decision by the named defendant approving the applications for permits to construct a solid waste resources recovery facility filed by Riley Energy Systems of Lisbon Corporation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the cases were consolidated and where the court, Maloney, J., granted the motion filed by Riley Energy Systems of Lisbon Corporation to be made a party defendant in the first case; thereafter, the matter was referred to Hon. David M. Shea, state trial referee, who granted the motion of the town of Stonington to intervene in all four cases and issued a memorandum of decision sustaining the plaintiffs' appeals and remanding the cases to the named defendant for further proceedings; subsequently, the state trial referee denied the motion to open the judgment filed by Riley Energy Systems of Lisbon Corporation and the motions to open and reconsider filed by Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority and Southeastern Connecticut Regional Resources Recovery Authority and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment in each case in accordance with the memorandum of decision,  [***2] from which the town of Stonington appealed, Riley Energy Systems of Lisbon Corporation appealed and cross appealed, Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority appealed and cross appealed and Southeastern Connecticut Regional Resources Recovery Authority appealed and cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff's administrative appeals but ordered a remand for further administrative proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that the dispositive issue in the four administrative appeals was whether it had jurisdiction to review the judgments of a trial court that sustained plaintiffs' administrative appeals but ordered a remand for further administrative proceedings. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183 (j), which characterized any remand order in an administrative appeal as a final judgment, was not applicable because defendant's permit applications were made in 1988, prior to the July 1989 amendments. The court stated that in light of its conclusion that the administrative proceedings are not governed by the amended Uniform Administrative Procedure Act, whether the trial court rendered judgments that were immediately appealable depended upon whether its remand orders satisfied the generic test for a final judgment. The court stated that the remand orders were not ripe for final judicial adjudication because they sought amplification of a ruling that was incomplete. The court held that the appeals were not taken from final judgments and the cases were dismissed.


OUTCOME: The appeals were dismissed because they were not taken from final judgments.

Serrano v. Aetna Ins. Co.


(14944)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 437; 664 A.2d 279; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 168


December 8, 1994, Argued  
June 13, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover underinsured motorist benefits allegedly due the plaintiff pursuant to an automobile liability insurance policy issued by the defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, Parker, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to defendant insurer in her action to recover underinsured motorist benefits. Upon remand, the matter was transferred to the supreme court for a determination of whether the retroactive policy modifications mandated by 1993 Conn. Acts 93-77 comported with the United States and Connecticut constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Section 3 of 1993 Conn. Acts 93-77 prevented underinsured motorist benefit claims pending at the time of its enactment from being barred from policy limitations periods that were less than three years. The insured argued that her claim, which was brought after a two-year policy limitation period expired, was revived by § 3. The insurer argued that § 3 violated his constitutionally guaranteed contractual and due process rights. The court held that § 3 passed constitutional muster and that the grant of summary judgment to the insurer on grounds that the insured's action was time-barred under the two-year policy limitations period was therefore improper. Section 3 did not effect any extreme contract modification in view of the highly regulated nature of insurance. It was also an appropriate legislative response to mitigate the severe consequences of court holdings that were mandated by clear policy and statutory terms. The contractual interference was therefore justified as a reasonable exercise of the state's police powers. The statute did not contravene any other constitutional provisions because it served a legitimate public purpose and was neither arbitrary nor capricious.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment granted to the insurer on grounds that the insured's claim for underinsured motorist benefits was time-barred by the policy's two-year limitation period was reversed. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

DeMilo & Co. v. Commissioner of Motor Vehicles


(15135)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 281; 659 A.2d 162; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 132


February 8, 1995, Argued  
May 23, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an administrative decision by the defendant which determined that the plaintiff had violated numerous motor vehicle junkyard regulations, and ordered that the plaintiff pay a certain civil penalty and that its license to operate a junkyard be suspended for thirty days, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Susco, J.; judgment for the defendant dismissing the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff junkyard operator challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed its appeal of defendant commissioner of motor vehicles' determination that plaintiff had violated numerous motor vehicle junkyard regulations, and ordered that plaintiff pay civil penalty and that its license to operate a junkyard be suspended for 30 days. Plaintiff argued that it was not collaterally estopped from litigating.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff junkyard operator was found by defendant commissioner of motor vehicles to have violated numerous motor vehicle regulations. Plaintiff appealed, claiming that the decision was arbitrary, unreasonable and an abuse of discretion. Subsequently, an enforcement action was brought to enjoin plaintiff from operating or maintaining a motor vehicle junkyard in violation of motor vehicles regulations. Injunctive relief was ordered and plaintiff appealed but his appeal was dismissed as moot. After plaintiff's appeal from the earlier action had been dismissed, but before judgment had been rendered in the enforcement action, the trial court concluded that the earlier judgment had collateral estoppel effect on the issues raised in administrative appeal and dismissed the appeal. Plaintiff appealed, requesting a new hearing. The court held that the trial court improperly dismissed the appeal on collateral estoppel basis and instead the principles of res judicata were applicable. The court stated that plaintiff's failure to present relevant issues as special defenses in the enforcement action barred him from raising those same issues as affirmative claims in his subsequent appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal on alternative grounds. The court held that the trial court improperly dismissed plaintiff junkyard operator's appeal on basis of collateral estoppel. The court stated that the correct analysis was that the doctrine of res judicata applied on all of plaintiff's claims so that the earlier judgment was valid and enforceable by defendant commissioner of motor vehicles.

FDIC v. Hillcrest Assocs.


(15084)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


233 Conn. 153; 659 A.2d 138; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 131


March 14, 1995, Argued  
May 16, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions to foreclose a mortgage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation, as receiver of the original plaintiff, CityTrust, was substituted as plaintiff and where the case was removed to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut and referred to United States Magistrate Judge F. Owen Eagan; thereafter, the defendants were defaulted and with their consent, the court, Eagan, J., granted the substitute plaintiff's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure and issued an order and judgment thereon which was approved by the court, United States District Court Judge Ellen B. Burns; subsequently, the court, Burns, J., denied the substitute plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment and granted the defendants' motion to dismiss the motion for a deficiency judgment, and the substitute plaintiff appealed to the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit, Winter, McLaughlin and Jacobs, Js., which certified two questions of law to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two questions were certified to the court from the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit. One question asked whether the 30-day time limit for seeking a foreclosure deficiency judgment, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14, was jurisdictional in nature. The other asked when the 30 days began to run, i.e., whether from the last law day or from the day that title in the foreclosing party became absolute.


OVERVIEW: Debtors obtained a mortgage on a parcel of real estate but defaulted on the debt. The bank that was owed the debt went bankrupt and the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC) stepped into the bank's shoes and foreclosed on the real estate. The debtors did not attempt to redeem the real estate and consented to a 33-day extension of time following the last law day, after which title would vest in the FDIC. The parties agreed that after the vesting of title, the FDIC would have the 30 days allowed under § 49-14 to file for a deficiency judgment. When the FDIC did so, the debtors claimed that the filing was untimely. The court disagreed, finding that the parties could waive the time limit contained in § 49-14 because the legislature had not indicated that the time limit would deprive a court of subject matter jurisdiction. Instead, the court found that the time limit was mandatory and that compliance was necessary, absent waiver or consent.


OUTCOME: The court held that the 30-day time limit for seeking a deficiency judgment was not subject matter jurisdictional and could be waived. The court declined to answer the other certified question regarding when the 30 days began to run.

DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed a trial court's judgment convicting defendant of sexual assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and threatening. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the victim reported to the police that her assailant wiped his penis on her jacket after sodomizing her, the police seized the jacket as evidence. After repeated requests from the victim, however, the police later returned the jacket to her. Defendant was arrested after the jacket was returned. At trial, defendant moved to dismiss the charges against him because of the police's failure to preserve the victim's jacket as evidence. Defendant did not argue that the police had acted in bad faith, but argued that his ability to defend himself was irreparably harmed. The trial court denied the motion after applying a balancing test. At the lower appellate court level, defendant argued that the police's failure to preserve the jacket violated his right to due process of law under Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. The lower appellate court rejected the argument without reaching the merits because defendant failed to show bad faith on the part of the police. On review, the appellate court reversed and remanded, directing the lower appellate court to reconsider defendant's claim. despite the fact that he alleged no bad faith by the police.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's judgment and remanded with direction to reconsider defendant's claim regarding the state's loss of evidence.

Harkless v. Rowe


(15061)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


232 Conn. 599; 657 A.2d 562; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 100


January 10, 1995, Argued  
April 11, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from three decisions by the named defendant upholding the denials of extension of general assistance benefits subsequent to the suspension of those benefits, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgments sustaining the plaintiffs' appeals and remanding the matters to the named defendant for new hearings, from which the defendants filed three separate appeals to the Appellate Court, which were consolidated and transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the director of social services (director) and the commissioner of income maintenance (commissioner), sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which reversed the denial of an extension of the benefits to plaintiffs, general assistance recipients, and remanded the matter for new hearings.


OVERVIEW: The recipients failed to complete the workfare requirement resulting in a 90-day suspension of their benefits. The director denied the recipients' request for a three-month extension of benefits pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-118 and a hearing officer affirmed the denials. The recipients alleged that the regulations were inconsistent with § 17b-118 and deprived them of their property without due process of law. The trial court reversed the decision, holding that the hearing officer's refusal to consider the recipients evidence violated their due process rights. The court held that: (1) the regulations were consistent with § 17b-118; (2) the hearing officer was not required to consider evidence that was irrelevant to the substantive issue; (3) the department was authorized to deny the extensions of benefits based solely on the previous suspensions, unless, at the time of those suspensions, the recipients had been deprived of their property interests without due process of law; and (4) because the evidence was insufficient to determine whether the recipients were denied due process at the time of the suspensions, more facts were needed to resolve the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering a remand to the commissioner was affirmed, but the case was remanded with directions to amend the terms of the remand.

O & G Indus. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


(15063)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


232 Conn. 419; 655 A.2d 1121; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 80


November 29, 1994, Argued  
March 28, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine whether the plaintiff's use of certain of its real property for the processing of earth products was a pre-existing nonconforming use not prohibited by certain newly adopted town zoning regulations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Dranginis, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to enjoin the defendant temporarily from proceeding with hearings on the plaintiff's application for a special permit to operate its earth products processing plant; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Pickett, J.; judgment for the defendant dismissing the action and dissolving the temporary injunction, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction company's action against defendant zoning commission seeking a declaratory judgment to determine whether company's use of its real property for processing earth products was a preexisting nonconforming use not prohibited by Beacon Falls, Conn. Zoning Regs. § 64.10-11.


OVERVIEW: The company, which operated a gravel processing facility, sought a temporary injunction prohibiting the zoning commission from acting on its application to renew its existing special permit pursuant to Beacon Falls, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 64.11.2 and to register its land as a nonconforming use pursuant to Beacon Falls, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 10.6. On review, the court found that the company was required to exhaust its administrative remedies before seeking redress in court because it had an adequate remedy under the regulations. Although the company was not required to seek a special permit because it would not provide an adequate remedy, registering as a nonconforming use would afford the relief sought, namely, recognition of the nonconforming use and the right to continue to process gravel materials without regard to their origin. If the zoning commission denied the company's application to register its nonconforming use, the company could pursue a judicial appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 8-8(b), 8-9. The court found no merit to the company's contention that it should be excused from the exhaustion requirement because the commission was not an impartial forum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

State v. Linares


(14861)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


232 Conn. 345; 655 A.2d 737; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 76


November 2, 1994, Argued  
March 14, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of interfering with the General Assembly, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Clifford, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., and Heiman, J., with Schaller, J., concurring, which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to resentence the defendant accordingly, and, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed and the state cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part, judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court denied her motion to dismiss, the defendant pled no contest to intentional interference with the legislative process, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-1d. The defendant appealed. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed in part. Both parties sought certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The defendant displayed a large banner and chanted during a speech at the House of Representatives' Hall. The defendant challenged Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-1d as being unconstitutional on its face and as applied. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 2-1d(a)(2)(C),(E), which prohibited intentional interference with a legislative session by making unreasonable noise or by performing acts which disturbed, disrupted or interfered, were not unconstitutionally vague on their face because they required specific intent to disrupt and because it was not difficult to determine what behavior was unreasonable. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied because the defendant had adequate notice. The court held that the statute was not overbroad in violation of the First Amendment because it did not prohibit the content of speech, only its character as intentionally unreasonable and disruptive. The court held that the gallery of the Hall was a non-public forum which had traditionally allowed limited interaction between the spectators and the legislature. The court held that there was a legitimate interest in prohibiting disruption of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, reversed the appellate court in part, and remanded with directions to affirm the conviction.

Bridgeport Hosp. v. Commission on Human Rights & Opportunities


(15059), (15060)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


232 Conn. 91; 653 A.2d 782; 1995 Conn. LEXIS 15


December 1, 1994, Argued  
January 31, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant that the plaintiff had discriminated against the defendant Susan Frederick, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment sustaining, in part, the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff and the defendant filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with respect to the defendant's appeal; reversed with respect to the plaintiff's appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant filed a complaint with defendant commission alleging that plaintiff, her former employer, had unlawfully terminated her employment because of her mental condition in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60(a)(1). Plaintiff and defendant sought review of a decision from the trial court (Connecticut), contesting the validity of an emotional distress award and the determination on the issue of attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Complainant alleged that plaintiff, her former employer, had unlawfully terminated her employment because of her mental condition, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60(a)(1). Defendant commission made a finding of reasonable cause to believe that plaintiff had committed a discriminatory employment practice. A hearing officer awarded damages to complaint for emotional damages and made an award of attorney fees to complainant's private counsel. The trial court sustained plaintiff's appeal as to the award of attorney fees but dismissed the appeal as to the award for damages for emotional distress. On appeal by plaintiff and defendant, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-86 did not authorize the award of damages for emotional distress and attorney fees for a violation of § 46a-60(a)(1). The court stated that it was not plausible that the legislature intended the phrase "affirmative action" to include compensatory damages or attorney fees. Defendant had no authority to award compensatory damages under § 46a-86(a). Thus, the court held that the trial court's reliance on defendant's interpretation was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to plaintiff employer's appeal, and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal. On defendant commission's appeal, the judgment was affirmed.

Molinas v. Comm'r of Corr.


(14963)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


231 Conn. 514; 652 A.2d 481; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 446


November 2, 1994, Argued  
December 27, 1994, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Sferrazza. J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), which granted habeas relief to petitioner, a criminal defendant, ordered him released on parole, and remitted his criminal fine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner plead guilty to possession of narcotics with intent to distribute. He was sentenced to 12 years, with seven of those years suspended. In addition a $ 20,000 "committed" fine was imposed. He was later parole, but remained incarcerated only because he was financially unable to pay the fine. He filed a habeas petition. The petition was ultimately granted and the trial court ordered him released from custody and remitted his fine. On appeal, the state argued that petitioner's inability to pay was not ground to release him because he had waived any objection to the extended incarceration when he agreed to the committed fine. The court disagreed and held that petitioner was properly ordered released because the record was void of any indication that he was advised that there was a possibility that his incarceration would be extended in the event that he was unable to pay the fine. Accordingly, the court determined that petitioner could not have waived his objection and his continued incarceration merely because he was unable to pay the fine was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which granted the habeas corpus petition, ordered petitioner released on parole, and remitted his criminal fine, was affirmed.

State v. Wohler


(14798)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


231 Conn. 411; 650 A.2d 168; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 408


September 22, 1994, Argued  
December 6, 1994, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with six counts of the crime of larceny in the second degree, two counts of the crime of conspiracy and one count of the crime of larceny in the fifth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham at Putnam and tried to the court, Sferrazza, J.; after the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal was granted as to three counts of larceny in the second degree and one count of conspiracy, judgment of guilty of one count of larceny in the fifth degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti and Lavery, Js., with Landau, J., dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of acquittal, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Appellate Court of Connecticut, which reversed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of one count of larceny in the fifth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-125a(a) and 53a-119(7)(F) and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a water works employee, was convicted of larceny in the fifth degree resulting from his use of water department employees and equipment to assist a department customer to replace a water line running from the water department's connection at the curb into his residence. The appellate court reversed, finding that because the charged defendant in the conjunctive, alleging a benefit to himself and another, the State was required to prove that defendant had the intent to benefit and had benefited both himself and another person. The appellate court determined, however, that defendant derived no benefit or gain to himself as a result of his activities in assisting the customer. On further appeal the court reversed, holding that because the State properly charged defendant in the conjunctive with two ways of committing a single offense, it was entitled to a conviction if it proved beyond a reasonable doubt either alleged mode of committing that offense. The court held that where an information alleges that an offense has been committed in more than one way, a guilty finding could stand if the evidence supports a conviction based upon any of the statutory alternatives.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to the appellate court for disposition of the issues raised by defendant in his appeal.
