Civardi v. City of Norwich


14982


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


231 Conn. 287; 649 A.2d 523; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 376


September 22, 1994, Argued  
November 8, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the named defendant et al. from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the second district that dismissed the request to transfer liability for the plaintiff's health insurance premiums to the defendant Second Injury and Compensation Assurance Fund and determined that the named defendant had no standing to challenge the plaintiff's eligibility for continued permanent partial disability benefits, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's dismissal of the request to transfer liability but reversed the decision with respect to the named defendant's standing to challenge the continuation of benefits and remanded the matter to the commissioner for further proceedings, and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the City of Norwich, sought review of a judgment of the Compensation Review Board (Connecticut), which affirmed a decision of the Workers' Compensation Commissioner that dismissed the City's request to transfer liability for an injured worker's health insurance premiums to appellee, the Second Injury and Compensation Assurance Fund.


OVERVIEW: The court indicated that it disagreed with the City's contention that the transfer of a worker's case to the second injury fund pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349 created an obligation on the part of the fund to continue Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284b benefits as compensation. The court found that the absence of express statutory authority undermined the argument that the second injury fund was required to assume liability for the injured worker's insurance pursuant to § 31-284b as part of the transfer of liability for compensation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349. The court reasoned that the expanded definition of compensation proffered by the City exceeded the legislative intent and would produce an undesired, unanticipated burden on the fund, which was not supported by the legislative history relevant to the enactment of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284b. The court noted that the payment transfer provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284b(d) were drafted to encompass an employee that was totally incapacitated, in which instance the legislature expressly transferred liability for the worker's benefits to the fund, a provision that was not a substantive change from a prior enactment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the review board's judgment in favor of the second injury compensation fund.

 

147 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fleming v. Garnett


14700


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


231 Conn. 77; 646 A.2d 1308; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 290


March 24, 1994, Argued  
August 23, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the action was withdrawn as against the named defendant et al., and tried to the jury before Wagner, J., as against the remaining defendant, International Transport, Inc.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court, pursuant to the collateral source statute, reduced the jury's award and rendered judgment for the plaintiff against the defendant International Transport, Inc., from which that defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff executor's wrongful death action, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) entered judgment for the executor following a jury verdict in his favor. The verdict against defendant tortfeasor was reduced pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §52-225a of Tort Reform I, to reflect collateral source benefits received by the executor. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both parties challenged the trial court's application and interpretation of § 52-225a to calculate the tortfeasor's proportionate share of damages. The tortfeasor alleged that its share of the damages should have been reduced by the collateral sources after the damages attributable to the decedent's contributory negligence were reduced from the total damages. The court noted that § 52-225a provided that net collateral source reduction must be applied to the damages awarded to compensate the claimant. "Award" was defined in terms of the claimant's total loss, as opposed to the liability assessed against any particular defendant. The executor was not entitled to an offset of the collateral source reduction by the attorney's fees he expended in obtaining a settlement with the joint tortfeasors. Although § 52-225a provided for an offset for sums paid by a claimant to secure his right to a collateral source benefit, attorney's fees were not recoverable under common law absent a contractual or statutory exception. Because § 52-225a did not specifically refer to attorney's fees, the court held that such fees were not available as an offset.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court in favor of the executor was affirmed. The trial court's assessment of damages was also affirmed.

Schnabel v. Tyler


14853


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 735; 646 A.2d 152; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 257


March 30, 1994, Argued  
August 9, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for defamation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, and tried to the jury before J. Walsh, J.; verdicts for the defendant on the complaint and on the counterclaim; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion for a new trial, granted the defendant's motion for attorney's fees and rendered judgment in accordance with the jury's verdicts, from which the plaintiff filed separate appeals to the Appellate Court, Daly, Foti and Landau, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a defamation action brought by plaintiff police chief, police chief appealed a judgment of the Connecticut Appellate Court, which affirmed a trial court judgment awarding compensatory and punitive damages to defendant police officer on his counterclaims against police chief for false imprisonment, intentional infliction of emotional distress, abuse of process, and violation of police officer's civil rights pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Police officer publicly criticized police chief who subsequently retaliated against police officer by engaging in a series of actions which intimidated and harassed him as well negatively distorted his disciplinary record. The court held that police officer's speech related to a matter of public concern and that it was a substantial factor in causing police chief to take the employment action against him. Further, police officer established a prima facie case that his First Amendment rights were violated. Police chief failed to then establish that he would have taken the same personnel action against police officer in the absence of the protected conduct or that police officer's conduct interfered with the efficient fulfillment of his employer's responsibilities to the public. Therefore, police chief violated clearly established law in retaliating against police officer for his protected conduct. Because police chief could not reasonably believe that his acts were lawful in view of the firmly established law, he was not entitled to qualified immunity against police officer's First Amendment and equal protection claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

Orsi v. Senatore


14799


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 459; 645 A.2d 986; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 246


January 11, 1994, Argued  
August 2, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in three counts for, inter alia, a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of certain procedures used by the defendant in removing children from foster care for placement with family members, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Plainville, where the court, Brenneman, J., granted the defendant's motion to strike certain allegations of the complaint and rendered judgment for the defendant on count one of the complaint only, from which the named plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Lavery and Landau, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction that, inter alia, judgment be rendered declaring the defendant's procedures unconstitutional, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Department of Children and Youth Services challenged a judgment from an appellate court (Connecticut), which reversed a judgment that plaintiff foster parent had no standing as a foster child's next friend to challenge the Department's decision placing the child with his grandmother under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17-37-4 in the foster parent's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17-37-4 the Department placed a foster child with its grandmother and the foster parent filed suit, as next friend of the child, for declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court granted the Department's motion to strike the next friend allegations on the ground that the foster parent lacked standing to raise the claim on the child's behalf. Upon review the appellate court reversed, and upon further review, the court reversed the appellate court. The court held that the appellate court improperly determined that the foster parent had standing as a matter of law to serve as the child's next friend. The court held that the foster parent's status as a foster parent did not necessarily precluded her from serving as the child's next friend. The court held that the trial court failed to exercise its discretion to consider whether exceptional circumstances existed to warrant the commencement of the declaratory action on the child's behalf and, if so, whether the foster parent was a proper person to do so. The court remanded for such a determination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which had reversed a finding that the foster parent had no standing and the court remanded the case with direction to remand the case to the trial court to determine whether the foster parent had standing to bring the declaratory judgment action on the foster child's behalf.

State v. Metz


14909


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 400; 645 A.2d 965; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 253


May 11, 1994, Argued  
August 2, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. Metz, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 455 (Conn. App. Ct., Nov. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault of a victim sixty or older in the second degree and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Buzaid, J.; judgment of not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect committing the defendant to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board with placement at the Whiting Forensic Institute for a term not to exceed six years; thereafter, the court, Bingham, J., granted the state's motion to extend the defendant's commitment and denied the defendant's motions to dismiss, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) granted the state's motion to extend defendant's commitment to a psychiatric institution after he was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect in a murder case. Defendant appealed the recommitment order. The court transferred the appeal from the court of appeals.


OVERVIEW: After a trial on an information charging defendant with assault on a victim 60 or older in the second degree and interfering with an officer, he was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect. He was committed to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board with placement at the Whiting Forensic Institute for a term not to exceed six years. The state's motion to extend defendant's commitment was granted, and his motion to dismiss denied. On appeal, the principal issue was the proper allocation of the burden of proof to determine the continued commitment to a mental hospital of a person previously found not guilty of criminal charges by reason of mental disease or defect. The court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) impliedly imposed the same burden on the state at a hearing for the continued commitment of an acquittee beyond his current definite period of commitment as was imposed in a civil commitment hearing. That was to show by clear and convincing evidence that the acquittee was currently mentally ill and dangerous to himself or others or gravely disabled. Accordingly, the trial court's recommitment of defendant had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's recommitment of defendant to a psychiatric institution for an extended period. The court held that the state failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that defendant was currently mentally ill and dangerous to himself or others or gravely disabled.

State v. Ross


13224, 13225, 13226


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 183; 646 A.2d 1318; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 227


February 15, 1994, Argued  
July 26, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ross v. Connecticut, 513 U.S. 1165, 130 L. Ed. 2d 1095, 115 S. Ct. 1133, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 1265 (1995)
Motion denied by State v. Ross, 1995 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1639 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 1, 1995)
Later proceeding at State v. Ross, 237 Conn. 332, 677 A.2d 433, 1996 Conn. LEXIS 198 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations, in three cases, charging the defendant with eight counts of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the cases were consolidated and where the court, Hendel, J., granted, in part, the defendant's motion to dismiss and dismissed two of the four counts of capital felony in the second case; thereafter, the case was transferred to the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of capital felony in each case; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and the court, Ford, J., rendered judgment of guilty in each case in accordance with the verdicts and imposed the death penalty on each of the six counts, from which the defendant filed three separate appeals.
State v. Ross, 225 Conn. 559, 624 A.2d 886, 1993 Conn. LEXIS 133 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of guilt affirmed; judgments imposing the death penalty reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three cases, defendant was charged with eight counts of the crime of capital felony. The cases were then consolidated and the trial court dismissed two of the counts pursuant to defendant's motion. Thereafter, the case was transferred to another court and tried to the jury, which rendered a verdict of guilty of two counts of capital felony in each case. The trial court imposed a sentence of death in each case, from which defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Informations, in three cases, charged defendant with eight counts of the crime of capital felony. After trial, the trial court found that defendant kidnapped and killed four young girls, and sexually assaulted three of them, in a manner that was especially cruel, heinous or depraved. Subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found aggravating factors and no mitigating factor. As a result, the trial court rendered judgment of guilty in each case in accordance with the verdicts and imposed the death penalty on each of the six counts, from which defendant filed three separate appeals. The court affirmed defendant's convictions in their entirety. The court held that even a defendant who has offered no persuasive legal excuse for his felonious conduct was entitled to have a sentencing jury consider extenuating circumstances that may have explained his behavior and mitigated his moral culpability and may therefore have counseled against the ultimate sanction of death. Because evidentiary rulings by the trial court impaired defendant's ability to prove the existence of such mitigating factors, the court determined that a new sentencing hearing was to be held.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed with respect to his guilt of six counts of capital felony. The judgments were, however, set aside with respect to the imposition of the death penalty, and the cases were remanded to the trial court for an entirely new sentencing hearing.

Associated Inv. Co. Ltd. Partnership v. Williams Assocs. IV


14725


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 148; 645 A.2d 505; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 222


September 28, 1993, Argued  
July 19, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover moneys allegedly owed on a promissory note executed by the defendants, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the defendants filed a counterclaim, and where the court, Maiocco, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to strike the case from the jury docket; thereafter, the matter was referred to Hon. Philip E. Mancini, Jr., state trial referee, who denied the defendants' motion to restore the case to the jury docket and their motion for default for the plaintiff's failure to attend a deposition, and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the plaintiff on the complaint and on the counterclaim, and the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) that granted plaintiff's motion to strike the case from the jury docket in an action dealing with a violation of the Connecticut Uniform Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendants filed a counterclaim to an action to recover monies allegedly owed on a promissory note executed by them. Defendants contended that the trial court improperly determined that their counterclaim alleging a violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq., was not triable to a jury. Additionally ,defendants asserted that they were entitled to a jury trial on their counterclaim under Conn. Const. amend. I, § 19, which guaranteed the right to a jury trial in all cases for which such a right existed at the time of the adoption of the constitutional provision in 1818. The court determined that CUTPA did not bear a substantial similarity to a common law action triable to a jury prior to 1818. The court held that, in fact, CUTPA had its roots in the Federal Trade Commission Act § 5(a); 15 U.S.C.S. § 45(a)(1) and that, therefore, plaintiff's motion was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting plaintiff's motion to strike the case from the jury docket was affirmed because the court determined that the Connecticut Constitution did not guarantee a right to a jury trial for actions brought under the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act.

Ulichny v. City of Bridgeport


14910


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


230 Conn. 140; 644 A.2d 347; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 223


May 6, 1994, Argued  
July 19, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the named defendant's alleged temporary taking of certain of the plaintiff's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the plaintiff and the defendants filed motions for summary judgment, and submitted to the court, Spear, J., on the parties' stipulation of facts; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to defendants, a city and others, on the landowner's takings action under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 15-73 and 13(b)-43.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned real property near an airport. Initially, he built a restaurant on the land. At different times, the landowner also applied for permission from a zoning commission to construct a housing complex and a second floor on his restaurant. The city opposed the landowner's proposed development plans and challenged any zoning commission decisions in his favor. The landowner filed an action against the city, alleging that its opposition was a taking of property under §§ 15-73 and 13(b)-43. The lower court disagreed. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's grant of summary judgment to the city, concluding that the landowner did not prove that the city's acquired the functional equivalent of an interest in his property. On the contrary, the city's exercise of its legal rights to appeal zoning decisions did not qualify as takings under the harm tests, which recognized a taking on the grant of permanent injunctive relief to a municipality. Here, the city's appeals did not conclusively determine the rights of the parties as to the land. Thus, the landowner's claim failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which granted summary judgment to the city.

 

155 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Mulligan v. Rioux


14648


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 716; 643 A.2d 1226; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 184


February 17, 1994, Argued  
June 28, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, malicious prosecution, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before M. Hennessey, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court granted the defendants' motion to set aside the verdict and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public works director challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of the Hartford-New Britain District (Connecticut), which granted defendant detectives' motion to set aside a verdict, which had found in favor of plaintiff on common law malicious prosecution and federal civil rights claims pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court concluded that defendants were entitled to qualified immunity as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court incorrectly applied the federal objective reasonableness standard to plaintiff public works director's common law malicious prosecution claims. The trial court made no distinction between plaintiff's common law and civil rights claims and concluded that defendant detectives had qualified immunity as a matter of law without reference to any state cases. The court agreed that the exception to qualified immunity permitting a tort action against a municipal employee when the alleged acts involved malice, wantonness, or intent to injure applied. The court held that because the jury found in plaintiff's favor on malicious prosecution, it found that defendants acted with malice, which was sufficient to defeat a qualified immunity defense under common law. The court agreed that the trial court improperly substituted its judgment for the jury's on factual issues. Because the contract in question was not terminated and defendants knew of a prior investigation, the court concluded that defendants lacked probable cause for the arrests. The court rejected reliance on the state's attorney's advice as a defense. The judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which granted defendant detectives' motion to set aside the verdict of the jury, which found in favor of plaintiff public works director. The trial court improperly substituted its judgment for the jury's on factual issues. The court remanded the issue of whether the damages were excessive to the trial court for its consideration.

 

156 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Anziano v. Board of Police Comm'rs


14893


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 703; 643 A.2d 865; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 176


May 5, 1994, Argued  
June 21, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant dismissing the plaintiff from his position as chief of police of the town of Madison, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hadden, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police chief appealed from a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which affirmed a decision by defendants, a board of police commissioners (board) and individual board members, that dismissed the police chief from his position. The police chief contended that the board's proceedings violated his constitutional and statutory due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The board retained a private agency to investigate allegations of illegal activities by the police chief. On the basis of two reports, the board directed the preparation of formal charges. The police chief received copies of both reports and the charges. Twenty-two public hearings were held in which the police chief was represented by counsel and he had the opportunity to cross-examine all witnesses and to present evidence on his behalf. The board deliberated and voted to dismiss the police chief. On appeal, the court held that the police chief's dismissal comported with procedural due process because (1) the police chief was afforded significant rights to participate in quasi-judicial evidentiary hearings that led up to his dismissal, (2) the board's preadjudicative activity was authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-278, (3) the board did not shift the burden of proof to the police chief because each charge was proven by clear and convincing evidence, and (4) the board's failure to adopt regulations to govern the proceedings prior to the adjudicatory hearing was not prejudicial because the police chief was afford procedural safeguards by the high standard of proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the board did not violate the police chief's statutory and constitutional rights.

Barannikova v. Town of Greenwich


14857, 14858


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 664; 643 A.2d 251; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 170


March 24, 1994, Argued  
June 14, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant commissioner of income maintenance sustaining the named defendant's denial of general assistance benefits to the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Hickey, J., judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal and remanding her application to the named defendant for a determination of eligibility, from which the named defendant and the defendant commissioner of income maintenance filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of Income Maintenance, appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which set aside the commissioner's decision denying general assistance benefits to plaintiff immigrant, a single mother. The trial court found that denial of benefits violated the immigrant's right to equal protection as guaranteed by the U.S. Const. Amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a single mother and recent immigrant from the Soviet Union, applied for general assistance benefits for her and her two minor children after she was divorced from the children's father. The Connecticut state application for benefits required plaintiff to provide income information from her sponsor, her former husband's sister. The sponsor refused to provide the information, and subsequently the commissioner denied the application for benefits. The immigrant filed an action alleging that the commissioner's application of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17-273(d) and 17-3a-14(D)(8) violated her right to equal protection of the laws as guaranteed by the 14th Amendment of the U.S. constitution. The trial court agreed, and reversed the commissioner's decision. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision. The appellate court found that the two laws created a presumptively invidious state law classification based on alienage. The appellate court rejected the commissioner's contention that the laws should be evaluated under a rational basis review rather than under the strict scrutiny standard.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which reversed the commissioner's denial of general assistance benefits to an immigrant, a single mother of two.

Antinerella v. Rioux


14734


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 479; 642 A.2d 699; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 148


February 17, 1994, Argued  
May 31, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the allegedly wrongful termination of the named plaintiff's employment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant deputy sheriff challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which had been granted in favor of appellee sheriff, in his official and individual capacity, in an action brought to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged wrongful termination of the deputy sheriff's employment.


OVERVIEW: A deputy sheriff brought an action against the sheriff to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged wrongful termination of his employment. The lower court dismissed the suit on the grounds that the doctrine of sovereign immunity, and the immunity provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 4-165 shielded the sheriff from suit in his official and individual capacity, and the deputy sheriff appealed. On appeal, the court held that: 1) the sheriff could not claim protection of sovereign immunity when he exceeded his authority by engaging in illegal fee splitting arrangements with deputy sheriffs; and 2) the sheriff could not claim protection of personal immunity from a deputy sheriff's private cause of action where he wrongfully terminated the deputy sheriff for furthering illegal fee splitting arrangements with various appointed deputy sheriffs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's decision which dismissed the deputy sheriff's suit against the sheriff, in his official and individual capacity, in an action brought to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged wrongful termination of the deputy sheriff's employment.

Summerville v. Warden, State Prison


14649


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 397; 641 A.2d 1356; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 140


October 29, 1993, Argued  
May 24, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Scheinblum, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Foti and Freedman, Js., which reversed, in part, the judgment of the habeas court and remanded the case for further proceedings, and, on the granting of certification, the petitioner appealed and the respondent cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner and cross-appellant warden sought review of a judgment from the lower appellate court (Connecticut) reversing in part the decision of the trial court in a habeas proceeding and remanding the case for further proceedings. Petitioner was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner spent a night in a hotel with a woman, who was dead in the hotel the next morning. Based upon a theory that petitioner asphyxiated the woman, petitioner was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree. Petitioner contended that she died of cocaine intoxication. In a habeas proceeding, the trial court denied petitioner's application. On appeal, the lower appellate court remanded the case to the habeas court for a consideration of expert testimony not presented at petitioner's criminal trial; petitioner and cross-appellant warden sought review. On further appeal, the court reversed the decision of the lower appellate court. The court held that a claim of actual innocence of the crime of which the petitioner had been convicted was cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding. The court further held, however, that the evidence produced by the petitioner, that medical evidence was unreliable and that some medical evidence was not analyzed, was insufficient to establish a claim on habeas corpus and was, therefore, insufficient to justify any remand to the habeas court for evaluation of that evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court. Evidence demonstrating that medical proof was unreliable was insufficient to establish a claim of habeas corpus relief and was insufficient to justify remand for evaluation of the evidence.

 

160 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chapman


14604


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 529; 643 A.2d 1213; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 160


January 4, 1994, Argued  
May 18, 1994, * Released


* May 18, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before J. Walsh, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Norcott, Landau and Heiman, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which affirmed the judgment of the Appellate Court; subsequently, this court granted the state's motion for reconsideration and reargument en banc.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1). The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed the conviction. On further appeal, the court affirmed. Subsequently, the court granted the state's motion for reconsideration and reargument en banc. The state conceded that the trial court erred in instructing the jury but argued the appellate court failed to apply a harmless error analysis.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury that it could find defendant guilty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1) if it found defendant had compelled the victim to engage in sexual intercourse either by (1) use of force or (2) threat of use of force. The state conceded that the instruction was erroneous because there was no evidence of defendant's threat of use of force but argued that the error was harmless. On reconsideration, the court agreed, reasoning that the error was nonconstitutional in nature because defendant did not establish a violation of his constitutional right to be informed of the charges against him and the inclusion of a factually unsupported theory of liability did not violate defendant's federal due process rights. Defendant failed to demonstrate that the error more probably than not affected the outcome of his trial. There was no indication that defendant's defense of consensual sex would have been different if the reference to threat of use of force had not been included in the instructions. Further, the trial court specifically defined only the actual use of force and the jury could infer threat of force from evidence of defendant's actual use of force.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded the case to the appellate court with directions to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Kelley


14560


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 557; 643 A.2d 854; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 162


November 2, 1993, Argued  
May 18, 1994, * Released


* May 18, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected
Subsequent appeal at Kelley v. Comm'r of Corr., 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 312 (Conn. App. Ct., July 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree and sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(b)(3), defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which found him guilty of kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), first degree sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), and third degree sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the victim's uncle, forced the victim down to his basement, forced her onto a dirt and rock floor, and had intercourse with her. Defendant was tried and found guilty of one count of kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), one count of first degree sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), and one count of third degree sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2). Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate that his claim that the constancy of accusation doctrine was unconstitutional because the doctrine applied equally to male and female victims, was not gender biased and, therefore, did not violate defendant's rights under Conn. Const. art. I, § 20. The court held that the trial court's jury instructions on both forms of sexual compulsion, even where the State had presented insufficient evidence of one alternative, was not a constitutional violation, but constituted harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which found defendant guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, first degree sexual assault, and third degree sexual assault.

State v. Indrisano


14631


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


228 Conn. 795; 640 A.2d 986; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 86


April 28, 1993, Argued  
April 5, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., Daly and Norcott, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed affirmation by the Appellate Court (Connecticut) of his conviction by a trial court of the crime of disorderly conduct under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(1) and (2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of disorderly conduct in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(1) and (2). Defendant appealed, arguing his conviction was illegal because the statute was vague on its face and as applied. When that argument was rejected, he again appealed on the same grounds. The court found the mens rea portion of the statute was not unconstitutional because no one could inadvertently violate the statute - the person would have to intend to do the proscribed conduct. Moreover, the physical violence prohibition in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(1) could not be interpreted as unconstitutional. However, in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2), "annoying" and "offensive" conduct was prohibited. Such language was found to be unconstitutionally vague because it could encompass conduct protected by the Free Speech Amendment of the United States Constitution. While the court found the statute unconstitutional as applied to defendant, the court saved the statute by defining those terms. While defendant could not be retried under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2), he could be retried under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial under the constitutionally unvague portion of the disorderly conduct statute.

Francini v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


14685


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


228 Conn. 785; 639 A.2d 519; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 76


October 28, 1993, Argued  
March 29, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a zoning variance from a minimum lot area requirement for certain of his real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the court, Hurley, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which dismissed the landowner's appeal of defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Old Lyme's decision denying the landowner's application for a zoning variance.


OVERVIEW: The landowner applied to the board for a variance from the zoning regulations governing minimum lot area so that he could construct a year-round dwelling on his vacant lot. The board denied the application and the landowner appealed to the superior court, which upheld the board's decision. On further review, the court affirmed. Rejecting the landowner's claim that his plan constituted a nonconforming use for which a variance was not required, the court noted that a nonconforming use was merely an existing use the continuance of which was authorized by the zoning regulations and ruled that the landowner failed to establish a nonconforming use because the property had been maintained as a vacant lot, not as a year-round dwelling. The court further ruled that the record supported the board's determination that the landowner failed to demonstrate an unusual or unique hardship, and that the board's denial of the variance did not constitute a taking in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 11 because the denial did not rule out any reasonable use of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment dismissing the landowner's appeal.

Fair Cadillac-Oldsmobile Isuzu Partnership v. Bailey


14806


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 312; 640 A.2d 101; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 99


December 8, 1993, Argued  
March 24, 1994, * Released


* March 24, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of the statute prohibiting the operation of motor vehicle dealerships on Sundays and to enjoin the defendants from enforcing that statute, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the Connecticut Automotive Trades Association, Inc., et al. were joined as defendants and where Fair Chrysler-Plymouth Partnership was joined as a plaintiff; thereafter, the plaintiffs withdrew their claim for injunctive relief and withdrew the action as against the named defendant et al., and the court, Moraghan, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved the questions of law for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car dealerships reserved questions of law for the advice of the court in an action brought to the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a statute prohibiting the operation of motor vehicle dealerships on Sundays, to enjoin the defendant commissioner of motor vehicles from enforcing that statute, and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue in this case was whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-301, which prohibited a party engaged in the business of selling motor vehicles from selling them on Sunday, violated the state constitution. Because the court concluded that § 53-301 violated substantive due process under Conn. Const. art. I, § 8, the court did not reach the plaintiffs' other state constitutional claims. The court held that because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-301 merely regulated a commercial activity, the sale of motor vehicles on Sunday, it had to be reviewed in accordance with the rules that normally governed constitutional challenges of economic or social welfare legislation by ascertaining whether the legislature acted arbitrarily or irrationally. The court held that the purpose of these closing laws was to create a common day of rest. The court held that as a Sunday closing law, § 53-301 furthered an objective that was difficult to effectuate with clarity and precision. The court held that in view of the totality of circumstances, the plaintiffs had proven beyond a reasonable doubt that § 53-301 was arbitrary and therefore violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute prohibiting the operation of motor vehicle dealerships on Sundays was arbitrary and, therefore, violated the state constitution.

Blanchette v. Barrett


14745


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 256; 640 A.2d 74; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 102


January 5, 1994, Argued  
March 23, 1994, * Released


* March 23, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for medical malpractice, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Hurley, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient commenced a medical malpractice action against defendant doctor. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) entered a judgment in favor of the patient pursuant to a jury's verdict. The doctor appealed that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The patient obtained a mammogram at the doctor's request. She was informed by him that its results were negative. Over two years later she again sought a diagnosis, and at that time, it was determined that she had breast cancer. Nearly two years later, the patient commenced her malpractice action. Under the repose provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584, an action had to be brought within three years of the date of an act or omission. Pursuant to the continuous treatment doctrine, when the injurious consequences arose form a course of treatment, the limitations period did not commence until its termination. Similarly, the continuing course of conduct doctrine had been applied to toll the statute of limitations when there was an ongoing doctor-patient relationship. Given that the patient's expert testified that the doctor was obligated to pursue follow-up contacts and provide additional diagnostic procedures, those doctrines were applicable and tolled § 52-584. However, the court reversed because the jury instructions misstated the law with respect to the continuing course of conduct doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the patient in her medical malpractice action. The matter was remanded for a new trial.

Carpenter v. Meachum


14595


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 193; 640 A.2d 591; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 93


January 5, 1994, Argued  
March 18, 1994, * Released


* March 18, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Simms v. Warden, 229 Conn. 178, 640 A.2d 601, 1994 Conn. LEXIS 95 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from the decision of the Superior Court for the judicial district of Tolland, Scheinblum, J., brought subsequent to a denial of petition for certification to appeal, denying the plaintiff in error's appeal from the denial of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.
Carpenter v. Warden, State Prison, 1992 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2185 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 24, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus. The Superior Court for the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) denied the writ of habeas corpus. Without challenging the validity of this denial, petitioner filed a writ of error claiming that the judgment of the habeas court should be set aside.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that the judgment of the habeas court should be set aside because that court improperly excluded relevant evidence and improperly rejected his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. He also argued that any limitation on the court's authority to hear his writ of error was unconstitutional. Respondent State countered these contentions on their merits and also argued that, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-273, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the writ of error. The court agreed with the State's jurisdictional claim and dismissed the writ. The court found that § 52-273 provided that no writ of error could be brought for the correction of any error that might have been reviewed by process of appeal. The court held that the legislature could constitutionally limit recourse to a writ of error and that the court's jurisdiction was not impaired by such a limitation of the right to obtain appellate review. Thus, the court held that the § 52-273 exclusion of cases that might have been reviewed by process of appeal was constitutional and that dismissal of petitioner's writ was required.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the writ of error.

State v. Joyce


14708


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


229 Conn. 10; 639 A.2d 1007; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 85


October 25, 1993, Argued  
March 16, 1994, * Released


* March 16, 1994, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of arson in the first degree brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of arson in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Daly and O'Connell, Js., with Heiman, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a trial court judgment that defendant was guilty of arson in the first degree. At issue was whether Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7 required police who had defendant's clothing in their lawful custody to obtain a warrant before subjecting the clothing to chemical analysis.


OVERVIEW: After a house explosion, defendant was found in a nearby river, severely burned. His clothing was cut off and taken into police custody for safekeeping. When defendant became a suspect, a chemical analysis of the clothing was undertaken without a warrant and gasoline was identified.Defendant unsuccessfully sought to suppress the clothing as the product of an illegal search and seizure under both U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7. The court held that, although the police had lawful custody under their community care function, chemical analysis of the defendant's clothing constituted an illegal search under the state constitution. Under Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7, all warrantless searches, whether or not the police had probable cause to believe that a crime was committed, were per se unreasonable, unless they fell within one of a few specific exceptions to the warrant requirement.No exception applied. Contrary to the state's arguments, defendant's failure to retrieve the clothing within 24 hours, during which he was hospitalized, did not waive his reasonable expectation of privacy in the clothing. No evidence showed that defendant's clothing smelled of gasoline.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment affirming defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial on the first degree arson charge.

DeBeradinis v. Zoning Comm'n


14777


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


228 Conn. 187; 635 A.2d 1220; 1994 Conn. LEXIS 2


October 27, 1993, Argued  
January 4, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant conditionally granting the plaintiff's application for a coastal site plan permit for certain of his real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the commissioner of environmental protection was made a party defendant; thereafter, the court, Lewis J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, remanded the matter to the named defendant for submission of written findings underlying its decision; subsequently, the matter was tried to the court, Sylvester, J., which rendered judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal but voiding the entire permit, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipal zoning commission denied plaintiff landowner's request for approval of a coastal site plan but indicated that approval would be granted if certain conditions were met. The Superior Court (Connecticut) reversed the commission's decision because one of the conditions was statutorily invalid and denied plaintiff's application. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner appealed defendant municipal zoning commission's decision denying the landowner's application for a coastal site plan permit but indicating that the application would be granted if he created a public access easement along the waterfront. The trial court found that the easement was illegal and reversed the commission's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that there was substantial evidence that plaintiff's property had been identified for a water-dependent use in the city's plan of development and that the plan submitted by plaintiff had potential adverse impacts on future water-dependent development. The court held that the easement condition was imposed by defendant to mitigate the potential adverse impacts of the landowner's proposal by adding a water-dependent component to a proposed use that was not water-dependent. The court held that the easement was an essential part of the commission's decision, and that its illegality required reversal of the decision in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court and reversed the decision of defendant municipal zoning commission.

State v. Greenfield


14582


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


228 Conn. 62; 634 A.2d 879; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 406


September 23, 1993, Argued  
December 7, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder. Defendant argued that certain evidence should have been suppressed, there was no probable cause to prosecute him for murder, and that there was insufficient evidence to convict him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of murder. On appeal, defendant argued that certain evidence should have been suppressed, there was no probable cause to prosecute him for murder, and that there was insufficient evidence to convict him. The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. First, the court held that defendant was not unlawfully seized by the police and that evidence regarding his evasive statements and behavior during that time was properly admitted. The court held that there was no "seizure," because a reasonable person would not have believed that he was not free to leave. The court noted that defendant voluntarily went to the police station and once there, the police placed no limitations on defendant's freedom. Next, the court held that there was probable cause to prosecute defendant and there was sufficient evidence to subsequently convict him of murder. Defendant admitted he was present at the time of the assault, he had the victim's blood on his clothing and hands, his testimony contradicted other witness' testimony, and the multiple injuries to the victim showed defendant's intent to murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Statewide Grievance Comm. v. Whitney


14594


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 829; 633 A.2d 296; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 380


September 24, 1993, Argued  
November 16, 1993, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Presentment by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment suspending the defendant from the practice of law for one year, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which found the attorney guilty of professional misconduct and suspended the attorney from the practice of law for one year. Plaintiff statewide grievance committee had commenced disciplinary proceedings against the attorney after the attorney refused to attend a pretrial conference in a criminal matter.


OVERVIEW: The attorney claimed on appeal that the practice of scheduling mandatory pretrial conferences in criminal matters was unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions, that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-172 and 53a-173 were unconstitutional, and that mandatory criminal pretrial conferences were used to demoralize defendants and impair their constitutional rights. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment of the trial court suspending the attorney from the practice of law for one year. The court held that the trial court properly found the attorney's repeated refusals to obey trial court orders to appear for pretrial conferences had violated the rules of professional conduct and that the trial court reprimanded the attorney and ordered him to pay two $ 100 fines, which the attorney refused to do for quite some time. The court found that the attorney never claimed that the trial court abused its discretion in making its findings of misconduct and merely claimed affirmative defenses, i.e., that because criminal pretrial conferences were unconstitutional or unjust, his conduct should be excused. As a result, the court did not review the propriety of the trial court's findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court suspending the attorney from the practice of law for one year at the request of the statewide grievance committee's and upon its finding that the attorney engaged in professional misconduct for refusing to attend a pretrial conference in a criminal matter.

In re Zoarski


14589


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 784; 632 A.2d 1114; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 372


September 21, 1993, Argued  
November 2, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal to this court from a decision of the judicial review council suspending the respondent from exercising his duties as a judge of the Superior Court for fifteen days as a result of conduct prejudicial to the impartial and effective administration of justice.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent trial court judge was suspended by the judicial review council (Connecticut) for 14 days pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-51l for engaging in conduct prejudicial to the impartial and effective administration of justice. The judge appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge signed an arrest warrant and, sua sponte, added a bond of $ 1000. The warrant charged an individual with littering, which carried a maximum fine of $ 250. The individual was a member of a family who ran a poultry farm which had had a contentious history with a partnership that owned property abutting the farm. Before he ascended to the bench, the judge had been one of three partners in that partnership and had represented its legal interests in proceedings at which the accused litterer had been present. The court dismissed the judge's appeal from his suspension, determining that the action taken by the judicial review council had been proper. The court ruled that the judge's failure to disqualify himself from the matter constituted judicial misconduct that was prejudicial to the impartial and effective administration of justice. The court determined there was clear and convincing evidence to show that when the judge signed the warrant and set bail, he knew or should have known of the history of contentious relations and litigation with the poultry farm and that the littering suspect would have to spend time in jail while arranging bond.


OUTCOME: The judge's appeal from the order of suspension was dismissed.

State v. Chapman


14604


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 616; 632 A.2d 674; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 294


February 11, 1993, Argued  
September 7, 1993, Released *


* The state's motion for reconsideration or reargument en banc was granted October 5, 1993. This opinion has been superseded by State v. Chapman, 229 Conn. 529,     A.2d     (1994).


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 26, 1993. Second Amendment. Third Amendment.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before J. Walsh, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Norcott, Landau and Heiman, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court, which reversed defendant's conviction in the superior court for the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the trial court improperly instructed the jury that it could find defendant guilty of sexual assault in the first degree if it found that he had compelled sexual intercourse either by the use of force or by the threat of use of force. The State did not introduce evidence of a threat of use of force. The appellate court concluded that the jury was instructed on a statutory alternative for which there was no supporting evidence and ordered a new trial. The court affirmed that the instruction violated defendant's due process rights. A trial court should not submit an issue to the jury that was foreign to the facts in evidence. The text of the sexual assault statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), clearly separated "force" from "threat of use of force" by using the disjunctive "or." There were two methods of committing the same crime. The State argued that the use of force and the threat of force could not be statutory alternatives because they could occur together and because they caused an identical result, compelled sexual intercourse. The court affirmed that the error required automatic reversal, without engaging in a harmless error analysis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of defendant's conviction for the crime of sexual assault in the first degree.

State v. Sawyer


14650


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 566; 630 A.2d 1064; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 292


April 28, 1993, Argued  
August 31, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Byrne, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Daly, O'Connell, Norcott, Landau and Freedman, Js., with Foti and Cretella, Js., dissenting, which set aside the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder. Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of the lesser-included offense of manslaughter in the first degree. The Appellate Court (Connecticut), reversed the conviction and ordered a new trial on the ground that the trial court erred by instructing the jury that it was required to come to a unanimous verdict on the greater charge before considering any lesser-included offenses. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury that during the course of its deliberations it was required to unanimously agree to acquit of the greater offense of murder before it could go on to consider the lesser included offenses of manslaughter. The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. The appellate court suggested that the jury should have been instructed to use "reasonable efforts" before considering lesser-included offenses. The court held that the appellate court's instruction would have rendered unclear whether the jury's verdict of guilty of the lesser-included offense would have operated as an acquittal of the greater offense for the purposes of double jeopardy. Accordingly, the court held that, in order to ensure that the charged offense had been determined by unanimous agreement, the trial court was required to direct the jury to reach a unanimous decision on the issue of guilt or innocence of the charged offense before going on to consider the lesser included offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court for consideration of the defendant's remaining claim.

State v. Cooper


14223


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 417; 630 A.2d 1043; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 278


January 8, 1993, Argued  
August 24, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Mulcahy, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: Victim and defendant argued and fought about a drug deal. Defendant shot the victim and ran away. He was convicted of murder. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that evidence of defendant's marijuana possession two months prior to the homicide was properly entered. It corroborated other testimony regarding why defendant was in the neighborhood and what he was doing there. The trial court did not err when it permitted impeachment of defendant's girlfriend. The testimony about the witness' brother exposed her lack of credibility. It was within the trial court's discretion to allow the state to impeach a defense witness with a 1964 felony conviction, and in any case the verdict would not have been different had the jury believed his testimony. Defendant's due process and self-incrimination rights were not violated when the state commented in final argument about defendant's failure to make a written statement because the state's attorney withdrew his remarks. There was no error in instructing the jury concerning specific intent. It did not permit the jury to entertain a conclusive presumption concerning defendant's intent to kill from the consequences of his actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder conviction. The court held that evidence of defendant's drug possession two months before the murder was properly admitted, his girl friend's testimony was properly impeached, the prosecutor's statement in final argument about defendant's unwillingness to make a custodial statement was sufficiently cured, and the jury charge did not create a presumption of intent from defendant's actions.

State v. Hinton


14313


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 301; 630 A.2d 593; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 282


June 2, 1993, Argued  
August 24, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony, attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree and with three counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of murder, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, one count of capital felony, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b, one count of attempted murder, under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-54a, and one count of assault in the first degree, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59 by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut). Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant got into a scuffle with a group of individuals. Defendant later saw one of the individuals that was involved in the scuffle. Defendant took a sawed-off shotgun out of his coat and fired several shots at the group of people the individual was standing with. Three people were killed and another was injured. Defendant claimed at trial that he fired in self-defense. The jury rejected the claim and found defendant guilty on all counts. The court held (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a permitted the State to charge a defendant with separate counts of murder, on a theory of transferred intent, for every death resulting from the defendant's conduct where the defendant acted with the intent to kill a person other than the person or persons that were killed, (2) defendant's successful killing of his intended victim did not preclude the State from charging him for the murders of the other victims on a theory of transferred intent, (3) the jury's verdict on the attempted murder and assault in the first degree charges was legally inconsistent, and (4) defendant failed to show that the prosecutor's use of two peremptory challenges to remove African-American venirepersons was race-based.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, in part, reversed the judgment, in part, and remanded the matter to the trial court for a new trial on the attempted murder and assault in the first degree charges.

State v. Miller


14634


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 363; 630 A.2d 1315; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 286


June 2, 1993, Argued  
August 24, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict of not guilty; thereafter, the state filed a substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a weapon by a felon and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle; the state subsequently nolled the charge of possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, and the defendant was presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of possession of a weapon by a felon; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Lavery, Landau, Heiman and Freedman, Js., with Dupont, C. J., Daly, O'Connell and Norcott, Js., dissenting, in part, which remanded the matter for further proceedings, and, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed and the state cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest in the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) to possession of a weapon. Defendant sought review of the denial of his motion to suppress. The appellate court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. Defendant appealed and the prosecution cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's car was identified as being used by suspects fleeing a robbery. The police went to defendant's home in an adjoining city. When defendant arrived, he was arrested and his car was towed. A warrantless search of defendant's car was conducted at the police station, and a gun was found in the trunk. Defendant filed a motion to suppress based on the illegality of the stop and the warrantless search. The appellate court held that the stop was valid, but that the search was illegal. The court held that the home rule provisions of Conn. Const. art. X, § 1, did not apply to bar the police arrest in the adjoining city because the provisions applied only to legislative actions. The court held that Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 7, 9, which prohibited unreasonable searches and due process violations, did not cover territorial restrictions on police power. The court held that the state's preference for warrants was not overcome because there were no exigent circumstances and because there was ample time to obtain a warrant for the impounded car. The court affirmed the appellate court's remand for a determination if the gun would have been inevitably discovered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court, which had affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress based on the legality of the stop, but had reversed as to the legality of the search, and remanded for the trial court to determine if the gun would have been inevitably discovered.

New Eng. Sav. Bank v. Lopez


(14558)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 270; 630 A.2d 1010; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 281


January 13, 1993, Argued  
August 24, 1993, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property owned by the named defendant et al., and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich, where the court, Teller, J., granted the motion for judgment of foreclosure by sale made by the defendant Stephen B. Watrous Builder, Inc., et al., and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, a sale was held and the court Koletsky, J., denied the motion to set aside the sale and' the motion for judgment of strict foreclosure filed by the named defendant et al., and approved the sale; subsequently, the court, Koletsky, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment against the named defendant et al. and rendered judgment thereon, and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtors sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London at Norwich (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff creditor, and a finding of a deficiency and initiation of a foreclosure sale. The debtors also sought review of the superior court's order denying their motion to set aside the sale.


OVERVIEW: The debtors executed a mortgage to the creditor in order to secure a promissory note. When the debtors defaulted on the mortgage, the creditor sought and obtained a deficiency, and a foreclosure sale. On appeal, the debtors argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-29, providing for deficiencies, deprived them of procedural due process. Specifically, the debtors argued that they were entitled to a hearing on the fair market value of the property, rather than simply getting credit for the amount of the sale proceeds. The court ruled that the debtors were not entitled to a hearing. The debtors did not have a property interest in having the property's value measured at fair market value. Such a measurement was contrary to an auction sale because there was, by the very nature of the sale, no opportunity for negotiations in an open market. Moreover, the court found that the debtors did not have a right to a hearing on the property's value under Conn. Gen. § 49-14(a). Section 49-14(a) applied only to strict foreclosure proceedings, and not to proceedings for a judgment following a foreclosure by sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
