Gen. Stat. § 54-94a for, inter alia, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-196a, 53a-70, 53a-8, 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife had left at a store film for developing, which showed children in sexually explicit poses. The photographs from the film were turned over to police. A judge consulted by the officers provided them with, inter alia, a Federal Bureau of Investigation pamphlet. The police took the warrant application, and the photographs, to a second judge who concluded that the warrant application showed probable cause for a crime, and issued the search warrant. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly refused to allow him to call the first judge to testify at the suppression hearing. The court disagreed. There was no evidence that the two judges discussed the warrant affidavit with each other prior to its issuance. Thus there was no showing by defendant of any misconduct by the first judge. Defendant also sought to call the second judge to question her in connection with her viewing of the photographs. The court held the judge's viewing of the photographs was irrelevant to the propriety of the issuance of the warrant, because the information contained within the four corners of the supporting affidavit was sufficient to allow a finding of probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which affirmed the judgment of the habeas court; thereafter, this court denied the petitioner's motion for reargument but opened its judgment affirming the dismissal of the petition and remanded the case to the habeas court for further proceedings to determine whether good cause existed for the petitioner's failure to raise his jury array challenge before trial; on remand, the court, Axelrod, J., denied the parties' request for an evidentiary hearing and concluded that there existed no good cause for the petitioner's procedural default, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland, Connecticut, which denied his request for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Finding that petitioner did not show good cause for not pursuing his claim of unconstitutional jury composition at his trial, the superior court denied his request for habeas corpus relief. The court reversed that judgment and remanded the action for an evidentiary hearing, finding that the superior court erred by denying a request for an evidentiary hearing as to the claim of defendant's public defender that he was denied the funding that was needed to bring the jury array challenge during defendant's trial. The court reasoned that relying solely on the original habeas petition hearing's transcripts was unjustified because the evidence that was presented in the earlier hearing was not designed to address the issue of if cause existed for petitioner's default under the cause and prejudice standard because the state was using the deliberate bypass rule to determine the reviewability of habeas claims that were procedurally defaulted at trial at that time. The court also held that a showing that interference by the public defender's office that made compliance with a procedural rule impracticable would have constituted cause under the cause and prejudice standard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief and remanded the action.

Smith v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


14632, 14633


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


227 Conn. 71; 629 A.2d 1089; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 267


April 28, 1993, Argued  
August 10, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiffs' application to subdivide certain of their real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Cioffi, J., granted the motion to be made defendants filed by the Historical Society of the Town of Greenwich, Inc., et al.; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Ryan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Daly, Norcott and Lavery, Js., which set aside the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment sustaining the appeal and ordering the granting of the subdivision application, and the named defendant and the defendant Historical Society of the Town of Greenwich, Inc., et al., on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Greenwich (Board), the historical society, and a landowner, challenged the judgment of the appellate court (Connecticut), which concluded that the Board had not been authorized to consider historical factors in reviewing a subdivision application and reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The Board denied the subdivision applicants' appeal of the Zoning and Planning Commission's denial of their application to subdivide their lot. The subdivision plan conformed to applicable zoning regulations. However, the Board concluded that one of the proposed buildings would disrupt the sweeping front lawn and would not be consistent with the district's historic streetscape. The trial court affirmed. The appellate court, however, reversed, holding that the Board did not have the authority to consider historical factors in deciding whether to grant or deny a subdivision application. The court concluded that because the phrase public health and safety contained in section 101 of the Greenwich Charter included environmental factors, it included historical factors. The commission, therefore, had the authority to promulgate subdivision regulations that took into account historical factors. The court also concluded that § 6-266(a)(19)(h) of the Greenwich Land Use Regulations expressly permitted the commission to consider historical factors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded with direction for it to affirm the trial court's judgment dismissing the subdivision applicants' appeal.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which denied their application for an ex parte attachment of defendant real estate corporation's real and personal property in an action initiated by plaintiffs to recover damages for alleged misrepresentations by defendant in connection with the sale of realty.

The trial court denied plaintiffs' application for an ex parte attachment of defendant's real and personal property, and plaintiffs sought review. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-2781(a), an order denying a prejudgment remedy following a hearing under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278d was deemed a final judgment for the purposes of appeal. Further, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-2781(b), an appeal must have been filed within seven days of the rendering of the order from which the appeal was to be taken. The court held that the seven-day statutory period was subject matter jurisdictional and was not waivable by defendant. The court held that plaintiffs' right to a prejudgment remedy of attachment was purely statutory and that the appeal must have been taken within the time constraints of the statute. The court dismissed plaintiffs' appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff purchasers' appeal of an order of the trial court, which denied their application for an ex parte attachment of defendant real estate corporation's property in an action alleging misrepresentations by defendant. The court held that, pursuant to state statute, plaintiffs were required to take an appeal from the trial court's order within seven days of the rendering of the order.

Sassone v. Lepore


(14693)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 773; 629 A.2d 357; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 261


June 8, 1993, Argued  
August 3, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for injunctive relief and to recover damages for breach of a covenant not to compete, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford - Norwalk, where the court, Dean, J., denied the plaintiffs' application for a ex parte prejudgment attachment of certain of the defendants' real property, and the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff complainants appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norfolk (Connecticut) finding that they were prevented from seeking a prejudgment remedy against defendant corporation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-278c, 52-278d because those statutes were unconstitutional in that they permitted a prejudgment attachment without requiring an applicant to post a bond or other security.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff complainants asserted that defendants, a corporation and others, breached a covenant not to compete and brought an action against them. Plaintiffs subsequently sought a prejudgment remedy against defendants, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-278c, 52-278d. The court reversed the lower court's findings that those statutes were unconstitutional because they permitted a prejudgment attachment without requiring an applicant to post a bond or other security. The court noted that all statutes carried a presumption of constitutionality such that in the absence of weighty countervailing circumstances, it was improvident for it to invalidate a statute on its face. Instead, the court opted to find a constitutional construction of the disputed statutes, and so determined that in the absence of statutory limitations preventing it from modifying application for a prejudgment remedy, it was permitted to require whatever forms of security were constitutionally necessary. The court thus found that it could require an attaching party to post security against the risks of attachment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's decision, finding that in the absence of any statutory limitation preventing from modifying application for a prejudgment remedy, it was permitted to require whatever forms of security were constitutionally necessary. The court therefore determined that it could require an attaching party to post security against undue risks from an attachment subsequently found wrongful.

 

184 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tanzella


14627


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 601; 628 A.2d 973; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 223


March 26, 1993, Argued  
July 27, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of assault in the third degree, threatening and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Kline, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Daly and Freedman, Js., with Landau, J., dissenting in part, which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of assault in the third degree and threatening, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of sexual assault in the first degree, assault in the third degree, threatening, and unlawful restraint in the first degree. Upon defendant's appeal, the Appellate Court (Connecticut), reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of assault in the third degree and threatening. The State, on the granting of certification, appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the jury had been selected and sworn in defendant's trial, the trial court clerk read the information to the jury. The prosecutor noticed error in two counts of the information and moved to amend the information pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 624. The trial court granted the motion and offered defendant a continuance to remedy any possible surprise, which defendant declined. The Appellate Court reversed the judgment of conviction and ordered a judgment of acquittal because the trial court had improperly permitted the state to amend the information by alleging different or additional offenses in violation of § 624. The court held that the amended information did not charge the defendant with different or additional offenses that would violate his right to notice under § 624 because the subsections of the statutes in question did not constitute different crimes. The court held that the crimes charged were not different crimes but simply different means of committing the same crime. The court further held that defendant's substantive rights were not prejudiced because his defense did not change when the information was amended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the Appellate Court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

Genovese v. Gallo Wine Merchants, Inc.


14555

DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged the decision of the superior court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted defendant employer's motion for summary judgment in employee's lawsuit alleging wrongful discharge by retaliation.


OVERVIEW: The employee, after being unsuccessful in a related claim arbitrated under a collective bargaining agreement, filed a statutory cause of action for retaliatory discharge pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-290a. Based on collateral estoppel, the trial court granted the employer's motion for summary judgment. The employee appealed. The court concluded that the legislature intended that such an adverse determination should not have preclusive effect. The court recognized that the scope of the submission by the parties may have limited the arbitrator's ability to consider all of the relevant legal considerations. Preclusion was not warranted because § 31-290a was a remedial statute that was intended to guarantee the rights afforded to injured employees under the state's workers' compensation laws. Further, the court found standard rules of preclusion were not warranted because reliance on an employee's union to vindicate adequately the employee's statutory rights may not have been justified.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Diaz


14554


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 514; 628 A.2d 567; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 220


February 9, 1993, Argued  
July 20, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Hendel, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and rendered judgment dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Dupont, C. J., O'Connell and Norcott, Js., which reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to deny the motion to suppress and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state government sought reversal of the order of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which upheld a lower court's order granting appellee accused offender's suppression motion upon conducting a de novo review of a decision to issue a search-and-seizure warrant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee accused offender filed a motion to suppress drugs and drug trafficking evidence seized from his residence pursuant to a search-and-seizure warrant issued by a judicial officer. The trial judge granted the motion, finding that the affidavit of probable cause contained in the application for the warrant failed to list observations and information supporting the view that there was present probable cause to believe that drugs and drug trafficking evidence would be found inside appellee's residence. Appellant state government took an appeal. After an intermediate appellate panel upheld the trial judge's suppression order, appellant sought and was granted discretionary review. On such review, the court reversed the order and remanded the case for trial at which the evidence seized would be admissible. In so ruling, the court noted that de novo review of the issuing authority's warrant decision was precluded under U.S. Const. amend. IV. It then held, as a matter of first impression, that de novo review was also barred under Connecticut's state constitutional search warrant clause, Conn. Const. art. I § 7.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed, and the case remanded for trial at which the evidence seized would be admissible. De novo review of an authority's decision to issue a search warrant was improper under Conn. Const. art. I § 7, and it had already been held improper under U.S. Const. amend. IV.

State v. Ball


14646


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 265; 627 A.2d 892; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 208


April 1, 1993, Argued  
July 6, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Informations charging the defendants with the crime of obstructing or interfering with the lawful taking of wildlife, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, where the court, Dranginis, J., denied the defendants' motions to dismiss; thereafter, the cases were presented to the court on pleas of nolo contendere; the court, Gill, J., rendered judgments of guilty, from which the defendants filed a joint appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant protestors sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut), which denied their motion to dismiss and then rendered judgments of guilty based on pleas of nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: The protestors were arrested while they were interfering with hunting at a state forest and were charged with having violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183a. The protestors filed unsuccessfully a motion to dismiss, alleging that the statute was unconstitutional. The protestors entered conditional pleas of nolo contendere pursuant to § 54-94a and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 4003. They were then found guilty and fined a small amount. Upon review, the court reversed the denial of the motions to dismiss and remanded the case to the trial court four a further evidentiary hearing. The court found that the trial court correctly ruled that the harassment and interference with hunting proscribed by the statute encompassed communicative as well as noncommunicative conduct. Stating that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183a implicated the First Amendment, the court found that the statute did not, on its face, single out a particular point of view for discriminatory treatment. The court stated that the protestors' motion in limine should have been denied because it precluded the state from introducing evidence concerning the public interest in the protection of hunters from intentional harassment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing to determine the nature and the extent of the public interest served by the relevant statute.

 

188 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lynn v. Haybuster Mfg., Inc.


14665


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 282; 627 A.2d 1288; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 209


April 27, 1993, Argued  
July 6, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Action, in two counts, to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of, inter alia, the defendant's alleged product design negligence, and for other relief, brought to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut, where the defendant filed a motion to dismiss, inter alia, the second count claiming loss of consortium by the plaintiff Theresa Lynn; the matter was referred to Hon. Thomas P. Smith, United States Magistrate, who recommended that the question whether a loss of consortium claim by an injured person's spouse is barred in an action brought pursuant to the Connecticut Product Liability Act be certified to this court; thereafter, the District Court, Covello, J., certified to this court that question of law.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, filed an action against defendant manufacturer pursuant to the Connecticut Product Liability Act (Act), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-572m et seq. The case was removed to federal court, and the manufacturer moved to dismiss the wife's claim for loss of consortium. The United States District Court for the District of Connecticut certified to the court the question whether the loss of consortium claim was barred by the Act.


OVERVIEW: The question certified was whether a loss of consortium claim by an injured person's spouse was barred in an action brought pursuant to the Connecticut Product Liability Act (Act), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-572m et seq. The manufacturer argued that the exclusivity of the Act abolished the common law claim of loss of consortium. The court disagreed and found that the claim was not barred. The court found that a spouse's claim for loss of consortium was firmly rooted in the common law and that to the extent that the Act abrogated the common law it was to be strictly construed. The court noted that the Act made no explicit mention of whether a loss of consortium claim was barred. Furthermore, the broad definition given to the term claimant as used in the Act could include a spouse asserting a derivative claim of loss of consortium. Finally there was no indication from the legislative history that the Act was intended to apply to a spouse's loss of consortium claim.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative and determined that the wife was not barred from bringing a claim for loss of consortium in an action pursuant to the Connecticut Product Liability Act for injuries suffered by her husband.

Kelley Property Dev., Inc. v. Lebanon


14640


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 314; 627 A.2d 909; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 211


February 10, 1993, Argued  
July 6, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged wrongful denial of the named plaintiff's application for subdivision approval of certain of its real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Austin, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate developer appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which granted the defendant, a town, the planning and zoning commission, and individual members of the planning and zoning commission's, motion for summary judgment in an action to recover damages for the alleged wrongful denial of the developer's application for subdivision approval of certain of its real property.


OVERVIEW: The developer's application for subdivision approval was denied. The developer filed a civil rights action against the town, its zoning commission, and its members. The trial court rendered summary judgment for the defendants, and the developer appealed. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly held that the developer's subdivision application was subject to the commission's discretion and that the town's land use regulations, therefore, did not clearly entitle the developer to approval. The court disagreed with the developer's contention that he met the "clear entitlement" test. The court concluded that the developer failed to establish a protected property interest in subdivision approval, therefore, the developer had not satisfied the threshold requirement of a federal due process claim. The court rejected the developer's two alternative arguments that the Connecticut Constitution ensured such recovery, and that the reasoning of Bivens applied in the state constitutional context. The court found that existing statutory remedies provided sufficient avenues of relief.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for the town and the zoning commission and its members was affirmed.

Starr v. Commissioner of Envtl. Protection


14529


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


226 Conn. 358; 627 A.2d 1296; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 212


December 10, 1992, Argued  
July 6, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant ordering the plaintiff to eliminate soil, surface and groundwater pollution in and on certain of her real property located in the town of Enfield and to take certain other remedial measures, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal, from which the named defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed an order of defendant Commissioner of Environmental Protection (commissioner), which ordered her to eliminate pollution on her property. The Connecticut Superior Court rule in favor of the landowner, finding the commissioner had been incorrect in determining that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-432 and 22a-433 imposed liability on the landowner regardless of her innocence in causing the pollution. The commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The main issue on appeal was whether the landowner could be held liable pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-432 to correct a condition on her land that could reasonably be expected to create a source of pollution to the waters of the state, even though she did not create the condition, acquiesce in its creation, or even own the property when the condition was created. The commissioner had decided that the "mere passive ownership" of contaminated real property constituted maintaining a facility or condition which reasonably could be expected to create a source of pollution under § 22a-432. The court held that the legislature intended that the word "maintaining" in § 22a-432, be interpreted liberally to include within its purview a landowner who had failed to abate pollution existing on his or her land that reasonably could be expected to create a source of pollution to the state's waters regardless of blame for the creation of the condition. The court held, therefore, that, pursuant to § 22a-432, the commissioner was empowered to order a cleanup of polluted land without regard to fault or economic hardship.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed it to dismiss the landowner's appeal from the commissioner's final decision.

Wnuk v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


14482, 14484


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 691; 626 A.2d 698; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 166


December 4, 1992, Argued  
June 8, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, from a decision by the named defendant granting an application for a variance filed by the defendant West Main Street Associates, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the cases were consolidated and where the defendant West Main Street Associates filed a counterclaim, and tried to the court, Goldberg, J.; judgments dismissing the appeals, from which the plaintiffs in each case filed separate appeals; thereafter, the appeals were consolidated and transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiffs, a zoning enforcement officer and abutting landowners, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), which upheld defendant zoning board's decision to grant defendant business a variance.


OVERVIEW: The business applied for a permit to establish a parlor. The zoning officer refused to grant the permit because street parking was insufficient. The business submitted an application to the zoning board seeking a variance and appealing the zoning officer's decision not to issue the building permit. The zoning board granted the business a variance. The court held that the zoning board was required to decide the business's appeal from the decision of the zoning enforcement officer's denial of their building permit before it could act on the business's request for a variance. The zoning board's failure to decide the business's appeal before granting the variance violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6a. The court also held that neither the alleged arbitrariness of the zoning officer's decision, nor the purported uncertainty of the ordinances, constituted the undue hardship necessary to support a variance. Accordingly, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded to the zoning board for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment that affirmed the zoning board's grant of a variance to the business was reversed, and the case was remanded to the zoning board for a new hearing.

J., Daly and Norcott, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the appellate court (Connecticut), which affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for attempted murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a)(2), 53a-54a, assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for attempted murder, assault in the first degree, and burglary in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a)(2), 53a-59(a)(1), 53a-101(a)(2), which the appellate court affirmed. The trial court dismissed defendant's appeal because certification was improvidently granted. Gen. Stat. § 54-56d in the trial court. Because the application of § 54-56d to defendant was a prerequisite to his due process challenge to the constitutionality of the statute and because that issue was fully explored in the appellate court, the court dismissed defendant's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of his convictions for attempted murder, assault in the first degree, and burglary in the first degree.

State v. Robinson


14466


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 519; 624 A.2d 889; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 131


February 11, 1993, Argued  
May 11, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, larceny in the second degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of three counts of sexual assault in the first degree, one count of the lesser included offense of sexual assault in the third degree and one count each of kidnapping in the first degree and assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which upheld a jury verdict that found the defendant guilty of first degree kidnapping, first degree sexual assault, third degree sexual assault, and third degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stopped his car and asked victim for directions. When the defendant made rude comments to the victim, she became offended and swore at the defendant. The defendant then proceeded to grab the victim by the hair and take her to a heavily wooded area. The defendant physically and sexually assaulted the victim. The defendant was charged with first degree kidnapping, first degree sexual assault, third degree sexual assault, and third degree assault. At trial, the trial judge instructed the jury that it was authorized to infer intent by a person's actions or statement and used the visual example of pouring water into a glass, which indicated an intent to fill the glass. The defendant was convicted as charged by the jury. The defendant sought review challenging the jury instructions. The court affirmed the conviction holding that a jury instruction was only unconstitutional if contained a mandatory or conclusive presumption of a person's intent. In this case the jury was simply instructed that they were able to infer intent, thus the instruction was not unconstitutional. The illustration used by the court was clear and did not mislead the jury..


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction of first degree kidnapping, first degree sexual assault, third degree sexual assault, and third degree assault.

Johnson v. Meehan


14556


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 528; 626 A.2d 244; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 132


October 27, 1992, Argued  
May 11, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a certain public act that eliminated the excise tax exemption for cigarettes purchased by inmates housed in state correctional institutions, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Walsh, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate brought an action for declaratory judgment against defendants, revenue commissioner and corrections commissioner, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-1 and 52-29, challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-297. The Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) granted the revenue commissioner's and corrections commissioner's motion for summary judgment. The inmate brought an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that the statute which eliminated the excise tax exemption for cigarettes purchased by inmates housed in state correctional facilities was unconstitutional. The court held that in the context of an equal protection challenge to social and economic legislation that did not infringe upon a fundamental right or affect a suspect group, the classification drawn by the statute would not violate the equal protection clause if it was rationally related to a legitimate public interest. The court held that although the inmate had a right to equal protection of the law that survived imprisonment, the trial court could reasonably have found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-297 did not violate the inmate's rights to equal protection because the legislature had a rational basis to justify differential treatment of inmates of state correctional institutions, and inmates and patients residing in other state institutions. The court held that the rational basis justifying the statute lied in the distinction that inmates housed in state correctional institutions were more able to pay the cigarette tax than those who were housed in the state's other institutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Joyner


14349


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 450; 625 A.2d 791; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 129


December 2, 1992, Argued  
May 4, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, one count of the crime of assault in the first degree, and three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the first degree, and sexual assault in the first degree, and was tried in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut). The trial court entered judgment on a jury verdict of guilty. Defendant appealed, claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-13(a), which allocated to the defense the burden of proof on a plea of insanity, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of insanity on various charges but a jury found him guilty. He appealed and the court affirmed. After rejecting challenges to evidentiary sufficiency, the court found no merit to claims that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-13(a), which required defendant to prove mental disease or defect, violated state constitutional guarantees. It held that proof of sanity was an independent fact, not an element of the State's case; that the legislature was free to allocate the burden of proof to defendant; that § 53a-13(a) was not unconstitutional for having done so; and that regardless of the statute, common law principles did not require the State to assume that burden of proof. The court also upheld rulings denying a new trial due to an improper comment by the prosecutor; allowing the State to introduce evidence of prior misconduct through cross-examination of a defense psychiatrist; and refusing an in camera inspection of the victim's health records. The court also held that psychiatric testimony relating to defendant's capacity to conform his conduct to legal requirements was properly handled, as was defense counsel's statement that defendant did not wish to testify.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment of guilty entered on a jury verdict and rejected various defense claims of error, including a claim that a statute that allocated to defendant the burden of proof on his plea of insanity was not unconstitutional under the state constitution's due process clause.

Serrani v. Board of Ethics


14570


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 305; 622 A.2d 1009; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 96


January 5, 1993, Argued  
April 6, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, whether the defendant had jurisdiction to investigate alleged ethical violations by the plaintiff as a former public employee, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Nigro, J., denied the plaintiff's application to enjoin the defendant from continuing its investigation; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment and rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former mayor, sought review of the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which denied the mayor's request for declaratory and injunctive relief to prevent defendant, a city board of ethics, from continuing to investigate the mayor's conduct during his expired term of office.


OVERVIEW: The mayor argued that a municipal ordinance, which permitted the board to continue an investigation into his alleged official misconduct after his term expired, was invalid. The court concluded that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to render a judgment, therefore it reversed and remanded the case for further proceedings. In order to bring an action for declaratory relief, the mayor first had to satisfy the provisions of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book R. App. P § 390(d), which provided that a trial court could not render declaratory judgments upon the complaint of any person unless all persons with an interest in the subject matter of the complaint had reasonable notice thereof. The record did not disclose that the required notice had been given. The court rejected the mayor's offer to withdraw his request for declaratory relief regarding the general validity of the ordinance in question as a means to cure the jurisdictional defect, holding that the lack of subject matter jurisdiction could not be cured retrospectively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with its opinion that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction, on the record as it stood, to render a declaratory judgment.

Robbins v. Van Gilder


14453, 14454, 14455


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 238; 622 A.2d 555; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 92


December 10, 1992, Argued  
March 30, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in three counts to recover damages for medical malpractice, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the action was withdrawn as to the defendant Joan L. Venes et al., and tried to the jury before D. Dorsey, J.; directed verdicts for the defendants on counts two and three and verdict for the plaintiff on count one against the named defendant et al., which the court refused to accept; thereafter, the court declared a mistrial on count one and ordered a new trial, and the named defendant et al. (Docket No. 14453), the plaintiff (Docket No. 14454), and the defendant Yale-New Haven Hospital (Docket No. 14455) filed separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient and defendants, a neurosurgeon, a hospital, and a medical school, both sought review of an order by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which declared a mistrial on plaintiff's allegation that the neurosurgeon had been negligent in the operation he performed on plaintiff and that the neurosurgeon caused plaintiff serious and permanent injury. The trial court ordered a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The patient contended that the trial court should have granted his motion to accept the jury's verdict and that the trial court should not have ordered a mistrial. The court concluded that there was not any basis for an appeal because the trial court's declaration of a mistrial would have led to a second trial. Thus, there was no final judgment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-263 because no rights of the parties had been yet determined. The court stated that the parties offered no specific statutory basis, other than the final judgment rule embodied in § 52-263, for an appeal. The court also stated that the trial court's denial of defendants' motions for a directed verdict and for judgment notwithstanding the failure of the jury to reach a verdict did not provide the basis for an appeal. The court determined that the trial court proceedings produced no more of a final judgment for purposes of an appeal than would have an order, opening a judgment previously rendered, entered upon a motion for a new trial. Given the circumstances of the trial court proceedings, the court held that there was not a final judgment and, accordingly, dismissed both the appeals.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals filed by both the patient and defendants.

State v. Adams


14445


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 270; 623 A.2d 42; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 94


December 2, 1992, Argued  
March 30, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree, robbery in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of felony murder, robbery in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as error the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which after a jury trial, convicted him of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, first degree robbery in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2), and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35.


OVERVIEW: Defendant provided the murder weapon used to kill a taxi driver in a robbery. The state alleged he also was present and assisted in moving the body. The jury convicted him of felony murder, first degree robbery, and carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. There was sufficient evidence to establish defendant's guilt to a reasonable jury. The fact that the evidence had not disproved defendant's story was unpersuasive because the jury plainly concluded that the evidence supported the State's theory of the case. Defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on the defense of renunciation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-10 because he failed to raise sufficient evidence of reasonable doubt concerning the existence of the defense. Defendant's alleged walking away was insufficient grounds for renunciation. Renunciation required termination of the effectiveness of any aid provided. Defendant's acts had not ended his accomplice liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-8. Defendant's other attacks on the jury instructions were not addressed because on appeal he changed his grounds for objection. The jury instructions taken as a whole were appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court which convicted defendant.

State v. Rasmussen


14227


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


225 Conn. 55; 621 A.2d 728; 1993 Conn. LEXIS 54


September 29, 1992, Argued  
March 16, 1993, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Walsh, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for, inter alia, acquittal and for a mistrial and rendered judgment of guilty, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which denied defendant's motions for acquittal and for a mistrial, and which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, and at the end of the trial, defendant sought acquittal and a mistrial. The trial court denied the motions, and defendant was convicted. He sought review. The court affirmed. The court found that the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's request to instruct the jury on lesser-included offenses because he failed to show some evidence that justified instructions on manslaughter. The trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal. Defendant's motions to suppress were denied because defendant had the burden to show that police questioning constituted a custodial interrogation and because the resulting search warrant was supported by probable cause. The trial court's findings were proper when it refused to excuse a juror and denied defendant's related motion for a mistrial. It was not improper when the trial court refused to instruct the jury on defendant's theory of defense. The court concluded that there was no error when the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss and motion for a mistrial for failure of the state to disclose material exculpatory evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and found that the trial court did not make errors in its evidentiary rulings, when it denied defendant's motion to dismiss, and when it denied defendant's motion for a mistrial.
